Conditions for the Shahada Utterance
The author enumerates the conditions for the wording of the two testimonies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the specific conditions that must be fulfilled when uttering the two testimonies to enter Islam, including the requirement of the word 'ashhadu' and its repetition, order, continuity, and universality of the Prophet's message.

Core Idea
The shahada has a specific divinely prescribed wording; synonyms or omissions are not sufficient.

This lesson examines the precise requirements for the testimony of faith. The author lists several conditions that go beyond simply stating 'La ilaha illa Allah'. Understanding these conditions helps us appreciate the care taken in the foundational act of embracing Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the conditions
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice how each condition is introduced with 'ولا بدَّ من'.
2
Note the requirement of 'ashhadu' and its repetition
The author emphasizes that the word 'ashhadu' must be used and repeated for each testimony. He also notes that synonyms are not acceptable due to the devotional meaning.
3
Understand the importance of order and continuity
The two testimonies must be said in the correct order (tawheed before risalah) and without interruption.
4
See the universality of the message and need to renounce false beliefs
One must acknowledge that the Prophet was sent to all people, and if one held false beliefs like the pre-eternity of the world, they must renounce them.
5
Learn that non-Arabic utterance is valid
The author states that saying the testimonies in a non-Arabic language is valid even if the person knows Arabic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا بدَّ من لفظ (أشهد ) وتكريره، ولا يشترط أن يأتي بحرف العطف على ما قاله الزيادي، ورجع إليه الرملي آخراً، فلا يكفي إبدال لفظ (أشهد) بغيره وإن كان مرادفاً؛ لما فيه من معنى التعبد، ولا بدَّ من ترتيب الشهادتين وموالاتهما، ولا بدَّ من الاعتراف برسالته صلى الله عليه وسلم إلى غير العرب أيضاً إذا كان يعتقدُ اختصاص رسالته بالعرب كالعيسوية، وإذا كان كافراً باعتقاد قدم العالم مثلاً فلا بدَّ من رجوعِهِ عنه. ولو أتى بالشهادتين بالعجمية صح إسلامه وإن أحسنَ العربية. وما تقدَّمَ من الشروط مبني على المعتمد في مذهبنا معاشر الشافعية، وبه قال ابنُ عرفة من المالكية؛ حيث قال لا بدَّ أن يقول : أشهد أن لا إلهَ إلا الله وأشهد أن محمداً رسول الله، وخالف الأبي شيخه ابن عرفة؛ فقال : لا يتعيَّن ذلك، بل يكفي كلُّ ما يدلُّ على الإيمان، فلو قال : الله واحدٌ ومحمد رسول، كفى، ونحو ما قاله الأبي لبعض الشافعية، وهو العلامة ابن حجر، وللنووي ما يوافقه أيضاً، فيكون في المسألة قولان لأهل كل من المذهبين. قال المصنف في شرحه: (وأولهما أولى بالتعويل عليه انتهى .
And there must be the wording 'ashhadu' (I bear witness) and its repetition, and it is not required that he bring the conjunction according to what al-Ziyadi said, and al-Ramli returned to it later, so it is not sufficient to substitute the word 'ashhadu' with another even if it is synonymous, because of the meaning of worship therein. And there must be order of the two testimonies and their continuity, and there must be acknowledgement of his message (peace be upon him) to non-Arabs as well if he believes his message is exclusive to Arabs like the 'Isa (Jesus) sect. And if he is an unbeliever due to believing in the pre-eternity of the world, for example, then he must renounce it. And if he utters the two testimonies in a non-Arabic language, his Islam is valid even if he knows Arabic well. And all that preceded of conditions is based on the relied-upon view in our school, the Shafi'is, and Ibn 'Arafa from the Malikis also said it; he said there must be saying 'ashhadu...'. But al-Abi disagreed with his shaykh Ibn 'Arafa and said that is not specific, rather any wording that indicates faith suffices, so if he says 'Allah is one and Muhammad is a messenger', it suffices. And similar was said by al-Abi from some Shafi'is, namely Ibn Hajar, and al-Nawawi also agreed with it. So there are two views among the followers of each of the two schools. The author said in his commentary: 'And the first of them is more deserving of reliance.'
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage enumerates conditions for properly uttering the two testimonies when entering Islam. Conditions: (1) must use the word 'ashhadu' and repeat it for both testimonies, (2) cannot substitute with synonyms, (3) must order the two testimonies (tawheed first then risalah), (4) must be continuous, (5) must acknowledge the universality of the Prophet's message, (6) must renounce previous false beliefs (like pre-eternity of the world). Non-Arabic utterance is valid. The Shafi'i relied-upon view requires 'ashhadu', supported by Maliki Ibn 'Arafa, but his student al-Abi and some Shafi'is (Ibn Hajar, al-Nawawi) hold any indicative wording suffices. The author prefers the stricter view.

Key Terms
أشهد
الشهادتين
الترتيب
الموالاة
العجمية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That saying 'La ilaha illa Allah' alone is sufficient to enter Islam without mentioning the Prophethood.
Correction: The text requires both testimonies, including 'Muhammadur Rasulullah', in a specific order.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for the utterance of the two testimonies?
A) Using the word 'ashhadu'
B) Repeating it for each testimony
C) Saying it in Arabic only
D) Ordering the two testimonies

Key Takeaway
The testimony of faith has precise conditions that must be fulfilled for it to be valid according to the Shafi'i school.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you recite the shahada in your prayers, are you consciously affirming each condition mentioned in this passage—the exact wording, the order, the continuity—or do you rush through it? How can you bring more awareness to your utterance?
?
This lesson shows that even a synonym for 'ashhadu' is not acceptable. Are there areas of your faith where you substitute what is prescribed with something more convenient? What would it cost you to be precise in your worship?
?
Do you truly believe that the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) was sent to all people, including those you dislike or consider 'other'? How does this belief manifest in your interactions with non-Muslims, or does it remain a theoretical statement?

The Scholarly Dispute Over the Shahada's Required Wording
The author presents a disagreement between scholars on the minimal wording of the testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between the relied-upon Shafi'i view requiring 'ashhadu' and the alternative view allowing any wording indicating faith, and the author's preference.

Core Idea
There is a valid scholarly disagreement on whether the shahada requires a specific wording or merely indicates faith.

Having learned the conditions, we now turn to a debate within the Shafi'i and Maliki schools. While the relied-upon view insists on the word 'ashhadu', some scholars like Ibn Hajar and al-Nawawi argue that any phrase indicating tawheed and risalah is sufficient. The author weighs in on this dispute.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contrasting views
Read the passage and clearly separate the first view (requiring 'ashhadu') from the second view (any wording indicating faith).
2
Note the proponents of each view
The first view is held by the relied-upon Shafi'i stance and Malik Ibn 'Arafa. The second view is held by al-Abi, Ibn Hajar, and al-Nawawi.
3
Understand the author's preference
The author states that the first view is more deserving of reliance.
4
Reflect on the implications for practice
Consider how this difference might affect someone accepting Islam. Does it change the essential meaning?

Are Works a Condition or a Part of Faith?
The verse asks the central question and gives two answers.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two main opinions in the classical kalam debate about the relationship between faith and works: that works are either a condition (shart) for faith or an integral part (shathr) of it.

Core Idea
Faith and works: condition or part? A defining debate in Islamic theology.

This short passage from the commentary on Jawharat al-Tawhid introduces a critical question: Is faith merely an inner conviction that requires outward works as a condition, or are works themselves part of the reality of faith? The dispute has implications for understanding salvation, the definition of belief, and the role of actions in Islam.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Begin by reading the Arabic passage and its literal English translation. Notice how the verse poses the question directly.
The passage is incomplete due to page break but captures the essence.
2
Identify the two opinions
The passage mentions two views: 'so it is said: a condition' and 'it is said: rather a part'. Find these in the text.
3
Consider the significance
Reflect on why this distinction matters. If works are a condition, faith can exist without them temporarily; if a part, then incomplete works mean incomplete faith.
This connects to broader discussions about sin and faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
هل العمل شرطُ الإيمانِ أم شطرٌ مِنْه؟ ۱۹ - فَقِيلَ : شَرْطٌ كَالعَمَلُ، وَقِيلَ : بَلْ شَطْرُ وَالاسْلَامَ اشرَحَنَّ بِالعَمَلْ قوله: (فَقِيلَ ... إلخ)؛ أي: إذا أردت تفصيل هذا الخلافِ فقيل ... إلى
Is action a condition of faith or a part of it? 19 - So it is said: a condition like action, and it is said: rather a part, and Islam clarify by action. His saying: 'So it is said ... etc.' i.e., if you want the detail of this dispute, then it is said ... to.
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage introduces the well-known kalam dispute: is 'amal (action/works) a condition (shart) for faith, or a part (shathr) of it? The verse from the poem states two opinions: some say it is a condition (like the Mu'tazila? actually it's a general statement), others say it is a part. The commentator explains that the line 'فقيل...' introduces the detail of the dispute, which follows in the text. This sets up the discussion of the relationship between faith and works.

Key Terms
العمل
الشرط
الشطر
الإيمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith is purely internal and has no connection to works.
Correction: The dispute shows that works are either a condition or a part of faith, meaning they are intrinsically connected.

Checkpoint

A) Works are obligatory but not related to faith

C) Works are a condition only, not a part
D) Works are a part only, not a condition

Key Takeaway
The relationship between works and faith is a debated topic in kalam, with positions ranging from works being a condition to being an actual part of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you were to truly believe that actions are a part of faith, how would your daily struggle with sins change? Name one sin you tolerate that you would have to reconsider.

Essential Conditions for the Shahada
Sanusi enumerates the necessary conditions for the shahada and addresses language flexibility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the necessary conditions for uttering the shahada, including order, consecutiveness, renunciation of prior disbelief, and the validity of saying it in a non-Arabic language.

Core Idea
The shahada is valid even in another language, but must be recited in order and after renouncing false beliefs.

This passage from Tuhfat al-Murid lays out the practical requirements for the Islamic testimony of faith. It explains that the two testimonies must be sequenced without interruption, and a person must abandon any previous disbelief. Interestingly, it also clarifies that uttering the shahada in a non-Arabic language is accepted even if one knows Arabic, showing Islam's practical flexibility.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Carefully read the original Arabic text concerning the conditions, then its English translation. Note the specific conditions listed.
The text uses concise legal phrasing.
2
Identify the conditions
List the conditions: order, consecutiveness, acknowledgment of the Prophet's mission to all, renunciation of beliefs like pre-eternity of the world, and language flexibility.
3
Reflect on the flexibility of language
Ponder why the shahada is accepted in non-Arabic even when one knows Arabic. This underscores the focus on sincere belief over linguistic form.
This condition differentiates Islam from some other religious traditions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الإلهيات ۱۳۱ مرادفاً ؛ لما فيه من معنى التعبد (۱) ، ولا بدَّ من ترتيب الشهادتين وموالاتهما، ولا بدَّ من الاعتراف برسالته إلا الله إلى غير العرب أيضاً إذا كان يعتقدُ اختصاص رسالته بالعرب كالعيسوية، وإذا كان كافراً باعتقاد قدم العالم مثلاً فلا بدَّ من رجوعِهِ عنه ولو أتى بالشهادتين بالعجمية صح إسلامه وإن أحسنَ العربية .
عنه (۲) 
وما تقدَّمَ من الشروط مبني على المعتمد في مذهبنا معاشر الشافعية، وبه قال ابنُ عرفة من المالكية؛ حيث قال لا بدَّ أن يقول : أشهد أن لا إلهَ إلا الله وأشهد أن محمداً رسول الله ، وخالف الأبي شيخه ابن عرفة؛ فقال : لا يتعيَّن ذلك، بل يكفي كلُّ ما يدلُّ على الإيمان، فلو قال : الله واحدٌ ومحمد رسول، كفى، ونحو ما قاله الأب لبعض الشافعية، وهو العلامة ابن حجر، وللنووي ما يوافقه أيضاً، فيكون في المسألة قولان لأهل كل من المذهبين. قال المصنف في شرحه): (وأولهما أولى بالتعويل عليه انتهى
(۱) في (ب) (التصديق) بدل (التعبد)، وفي (ج) : (القصد) وعلى هامش النسخة (التعبد) بدون حذف كلمة (القصد)، وكلمة القصد في آخر السطر وبجانبها كلمة القصد على الهامش.
(۲) والمسألة اجتهادية في اشتراط كل هذا، ولا سيما أن الآبي مؤمن على القول الأظهر عند الإمام الغزالي كما سيأتي تعليقاً .
(۳) قال العلامة الأمير في حاشيته على عبد السلام (ص) (٥٧) وسمعنا من المشايخ كثيراً أن المدار عند المالكية على أي لفظ يُفيد الوحدانية والرسالة، ونقله المصنف في شرحه عن الأُبي مخالفاً لشيخه ابن عرفة المشترط اللفظ المخصوص . . . ) ، وانظر هداية المريده (۲۷۲/۱).
The Divine Things 131: synonymous; because of the meaning of worship (1) in it. It is necessary to order the two testimonies and to be consecutive. It is necessary to acknowledge his message except to non-Arabs as well if he believes in the specificity of his mission to the Arabs, like the 'Isawiyya. And if he is a disbeliever due to believing in the pre-eternity of the world, for example, he must renounce it. And if he utters the two testimonies in non-Arabic, his Islam is valid even if he is proficient in Arabic. From him (2). And what was mentioned of conditions is based on the relied-upon in our school, the community of Shafi'is, and Ibn 'Arafa of the Malikis said it; he said: it is necessary that he say: I bear witness that there is no god but Allah and I bear witness that Muhammad is the Messenger of Allah. But al-Abi disagreed with his shaykh Ibn 'Arafa; he said: that is not specific, rather anything that indicates faith suffices. So if he says: Allah is one and Muhammad is a messenger, it suffices. And similar to what al-Abi said, some Shafi'is, namely al-Allama Ibn Hajar, held it, and al-Nawawi also agreed with it. So there are two sayings for the people of each of the two schools. The author said in his commentary: "And the first of the two is more worthy of reliance." (1) In (b): (al-tasdiq) instead of (al-ta'abbud), and in (j): (al-qasd), and on the margin of the copy (al-ta'abbud) without deleting the word (al-qasd), and the word (al-qasd) at the end of the line and next to it the word (al-qasd) in the margin. (2) The matter is ijtihadī in stipulating all of this, especially since al-Abi is a believer according to the most apparent opinion of Imam al-Ghazali, as will come in commentary. (3) Al-Allama al-Amir said in his gloss on 'Abd al-Salam (p. 57): "We heard from the shaykhs often that the criterion among the Malikis is any wording that conveys tawhid and the message, and the author transmitted it in his commentary from al-Abi disagreeing with his shaykh Ibn 'Arafa who stipulated the specific wording..." See Hidayat al-Murid (1/272).
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage discusses the necessary conditions for the Islamic testimony of faith (shahada) and the scholarly disagreement regarding its formulation. It first states that the two testimonies must be uttered in order and consecutively, and that one must also acknowledge the Prophet's mission to non-Arabs if one previously believed it was only for Arabs, like the 'Isawiyya sect. If someone believes in the pre-eternity of the world, they must renounce that belief. Uttering the shahada in a non-Arabic language is valid even if one knows Arabic. The author then explains that these conditions are based on the relied-upon view of the Shafi'i school, and also held by the Maliki scholar Ibn 'Arafa, who insisted on the specific Arabic formula. However, Ibn 'Arafa's student al-Abi disagreed, saying any wording that indicates faith suffices, and this view is also supported by some Shafi'is like Ibn Hajar and al-Nawawi. The author notes that his preferred view is the first (Ibn 'Arafa's). Footnotes provide textual variants and additional context: one footnote mentions a variant reading of 'al-ta'abbud' (worship) being replaced by 'al-tasdiq' (belief) or 'al-qasd' (intent); another states that the issue is ijtihadī and that al-Abi is still considered a believer according to al-Ghazali; a third cites al-Amir's gloss that among Malikis the criterion is any wording conveying tawhid and the message.

Key Terms
الشهادتين
العجمية
شروط

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The shahada must always be recited in Arabic exactly as 'Ashhadu an la ilaha illa Allah...' to be valid.
Correction: While the specific Arabic phrase is recommended, the passage states that uttering the shahada in non-Arabic is valid even if one knows Arabic, showing that the essential condition is sincere belief, not linguistic precision.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, is the shahada valid if recited in a non-Arabic language?
A) No, it must be in Arabic even if one does not understand it.
B) Yes, but only if the person does not know Arabic.
C) Yes, even if the person knows Arabic.
D) No, the shahada is only valid in Arabic.

Key Takeaway
The shahada is valid even in another language, but must be recited in proper order, without interruption, and after renouncing any contrary beliefs.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever recited the shahada without consciously renouncing a false belief you held deep inside? What was that belief, and when will you actively renounce it?
?
If you were to help someone convert today, are you certain you would instruct them to acknowledge that the Prophet was sent to all people, including non-Arabs? Would you dare to omit any condition?
?
The passage requires the shahada to be said in order and without interruption. When you recite it daily, do you take it as seriously as a life-or-death condition? How would your recitation change if you saw it as the moment your faith is either accepted or rejected?

Scholarly Disagreement on the Shahada's Wording
Sanusi presents the scholarly disagreement on the shahada's wording and gives his preference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the disagreement between Maliki scholars Ibn 'Arafa and al-Abi on whether the shahada requires a specific Arabic formula or any wording indicating faith suffices, and how the author of our text resolves it.

Core Idea
Scholars differ: some require exact Arabic phrase; others accept any wording showing faith.

This passage presents a notable intra-school debate among Malikis (and echoed among Shafi'is) regarding the precise formulation of the shahada. Ibn 'Arafa insisted on the exact Arabic formula, while his student al-Abi held that any wording indicating faith is sufficient. The author of Tuhfat al-Murid favors the stricter view, but acknowledges the issue is a matter of ijtihad.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage on the two positions
Read the Arabic text and translation carefully, focusing on the two opposing views and the scholars who supported each.
Note the names: Ibn 'Arafa, al-Abi, Ibn Hajar, and al-Nawawi.
2
Compare the two views
List the differences: Ibn 'Arafa requires the exact Arabic phrase; al-Abi accepts any wording that indicates faith, like 'Allah is one and Muhammad is a messenger.'
3
Understand the author's preference
The author states that the first view (Ibn 'Arafa's) is more worthy of reliance. Reflect on why the author might prefer this stricter view.
The issue is ijtihadī, so both positions are valid scholarly opinions.

Is Action a Condition or Part of Faith? The Two Views
Presents two opinions on action's relation to faith and defines 'condition'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two views on whether action is a condition or a part of faith, and what the term 'condition' means in this context.

Core Idea
Action is not part of faith's essence but a condition for its worldly recognition.

This lesson introduces a foundational debate in Islamic theology: Is action (including uttering the shahada) an integral part of faith (shatr) or merely a condition (shart) for its application? The commentator clarifies that the majority of Ash'ari and Maturidi scholars consider it a condition, meaning it is external to the essence of faith. Understanding this distinction is crucial for grasping how faith relates to outward practice.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening line and commentary
Read the poem line and the commentator's explanation. Note that the poet presents two views.
2
Identify the definition of 'shart'
The commentator defines 'shart' as something outside the essence (kharij 'an mahiyya). Understand that this means action does not constitute the reality of faith.
This is key to the Ash'ari position.
3
Note the proponents of this view
This view (condition) is held by the verifying scholars of the Ash'aris and Maturidis and others.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask yourself why such a distinction matters. It affects how we judge a person's faith in this world and the next.
Connects to the next lesson on practical implications.

هل العمل شرطُ الإيمانِ أم شطرٌ مِنْه؟
۱۹ - فَقِيلَ : شَرْطٌ كَالعَمَلُ، وَقِيلَ : بَلْ شَطْرُ وَالاسْلَامَ اشْرَحَنَّ بِالعَمَلْ
قوله: (فَقِيلَ ... إلخ)؛ أي: إذا أردت تفصيل هذا الخلافِ فقيل ... إلى آخره، فالفاء فاء الفصيحة. ويحتمل أن تكون لمجرَّدِ العطف، فيكون معطوفاً على الجملة الاسمية وهي قوله والنطق (...) إلى آخره من عطف المفصل على المجمل .
وقوله : (شَرْطُ ... إلخ)؛ أي: خارج عن ماهِيَّتِهِ ، وهذا القولُ لمحققي الأشاعرة والماتريدية ولغيرهم .
وقد فهم الجمهورُ أن مرادهم أنه شرط لإجراء أحكام المؤمنين عليه؛ من التوارث، والتناكح ، والصلاة خلفَهُ، وعليه، والدفن في مقابر المسلمين، ومطالبته بالصلوات والزكوات وغير ذلك؛ لأن التصديق القلبي وإن كان إيماناً إلَّا أنه باطن خفي، فلا بد له من علامة ظاهرة تدلُّ عليه ؛ لتناط - أي : تعلّق ـ به به تلك الأحكام، فمَنْ صدق بقلبه ولم يقر بلسانه لا لعذر منعه ولا لإباء، بل اتفق له ذلك، فهو مؤمن عند الله غير مؤمن في الأحكام الدنيوية.
أما المعذور إذا قامت قرينة على إسلامه بغير النطق ؛ كالإشارة، فهو مؤمن فيهما . وأما الآبي ؛ بأن طلب منه النطق بالشهادتين فأبى، فهو كافر فيهما (١)، ولو أذعن
(۱) والذي استظهره إمامنا الغزالي أن الآبي مؤمن والمسألة فقهية وعبارته في إحيائه» (۱۱۸/۱): (الدرجة الخامسة : أن يصدق بالقلب ويساعده من العمر مهلة النطق بكلمتي الشهادة، وعلم وجوبها، ولكنه لم ينطق بها، فيحتمل أن يجعل امتناعه عن النطق كامتناعه عن الصلاة، ونقول : هو مؤمن غير مخلَّدٍ في النار، والإيمان هو التصديق المحض، واللسان ترجمان الإيمان، فلا بدَّ أن يكون الإيمان موجوداً بتمامه قبل اللسان حتى يترجمه اللسان، وهذا هو الأظهر؛ إذ لا مستند إلا اتباع موجبِ الألفاظ، ووضع اللسان أن الإيمان هو عبارة عن التصديق بالقلب، وقد قال : يخرج من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من الإيمان ، ولا ينعدم الإيمان من القلب بالسكوت عن النطق الواجب، كما لا ينعدم بالسكوت عن الفعل الواجب. وقال قائلون: القول ركن ؛ إذ ليس كلمتا الشهادة إخباراً عن القلب، بل هو إنشاء عقد آخر، وابتداء شهادة والتزام والأول أظهر، وقد غلا في هذا طائفة المرجئة فقالوا: هذا لا يدخل النار أصلاً وقالوا إن المؤمن وإن عصى فلا يدخل النار، وسنبطل ذلك عليهم). : وعلى هذا القول لا داعي أصلاً للشروط المذكورة في لفظ الشهادة كما لا يخفى، ولكن يبقى أن يقال من آمن بقلبه وأبى النطق بما يدل على إيمانه، فهو مؤمن عنده، ومن قال يقوله ولكن عند الله ، لا في الدنيا، أما إن اقترن بدليل دال على الإيمان؛ كأن قال: آمنت بما آمن به -
Is action a condition of faith or a part of it? 19 - So it was said: a condition like action, and it was said: rather a part, and Islam is explained by action. His saying: (so it was said ... etc.), i.e., if you want the detail of this disagreement, so it was said ... to the end. So the 'fa' is the fa of explanation. It is also possible that it is for mere conjunction, so it is conjoined to the nominal sentence which is his saying 'and speech ( ... )' to the end, as conjoining the detailed to the summary. And his saying: (a condition ... etc.), i.e., outside its essence, and this is the saying of the verifying scholars of the Ash'aris and Maturidis and others. And the majority understood that they mean it is a condition for applying the rulings of believers upon him: such as inheritance, marriage, praying behind him, and upon him, burial in Muslim cemeteries, and requiring him to pray, give zakat, and other things; because heart belief, even if it is faith, is hidden and concealed, so it must have an apparent sign indicating it, so that those rulings may be attached—i.e., connected—to it. So whoever believes in his heart but does not confess with his tongue, without an excuse preventing him nor obstinacy, but it so happens to him, he is a believer before Allah but not a believer in worldly rulings. As for the excused person, if there is evidence of his Islam other than speech, like a gesture, then he is a believer in both realms. As for the obstinate one: if he is asked to utter the two testimonies and he refuses, then he is a disbeliever in both realms (1), even if he acquiesces. (1) And what our Imam al-Ghazali considered most likely is that the obstinate one is a believer, and the matter is jurisprudential. His expression in his Ihya (1/118): (The fifth degree: that he believes in his heart and his lifespan allows him time to utter the two words of testimony, and he knows their obligation, but he does not utter them. Then it is possible to consider his abstention from utterance like his abstention from prayer, and we say: he is a believer not eternally in the Fire, and faith is pure belief, and the tongue is the interpreter of faith, so faith must exist in its entirety before the tongue so that the tongue may interpret it. And this is the most apparent; because there is no basis except following the implication of words, and the linguistic convention is that faith is expression of belief in the heart, and he [the Prophet] said: 'He will be brought out who has in his heart a grain's weight of faith.' And faith does not cease from the heart by silence about the obligatory utterance, just as it does not cease by silence about the obligatory action. And some said: utterance is a pillar, for the two words of testimony are not a report from the heart, but rather an initiation of another contract, and a beginning of testimony and commitment. And the first is more apparent, and a group of the Murji'a exaggerated in this and said that this person will not enter the Fire at all, and they said that the believer, even if he disobeys, will not enter the Fire, and we will refute that against them.) And according to this saying, there is no need at all for the conditions mentioned regarding the wording of the shahada, as is obvious. But it remains to be said: whoever believes in his heart and refuses to utter what indicates his faith, then he is a believer according to him [al-Ghazali], but it is said concerning his judgment: but before Allah, not in the world. If there is evidence indicating his faith, like saying: I believe in what so-and-so believed in -
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage addresses the debated question: Is action (such as uttering the shahada) a condition (shart) for faith, or a part (shatr) of faith? The poem states that one view says it is a condition, like action, and another says it is a part. The commentator explains that the word 'fa' in 'fa-qila' is either for elaboration (fa al-fasiha) or simply for conjunction, connecting this detail to an earlier summary. He then clarifies that 'shart' means something outside the essence of faith. This view is held by the verifying scholars of the Ash'aris and Maturidis and others. The majority understood that this condition applies to worldly rulings (ahkam dunyawiyya) such as inheritance, marriage, prayer behind him, burial in Muslim cemeteries, and requiring him to perform religious duties. The reason is that inner belief (tasdiq qalbi) is hidden, so an outward sign is needed to attach these rulings. Therefore, if a person believes sincerely in his heart but does not utter the shahada without any excuse or obstinacy—just by happenstance—he is a believer before Allah but not considered a believer in worldly rulings. The excused person (e.g., one who cannot speak) is a believer in both realms if there is evidence like a gesture. The obstinate person (al-abi)—who is asked to utter the shahada and refuses—is a disbeliever in both realms. A lengthy footnote from al-Ghazali argues that the obstinate person is a believer before Allah, based on the definition of faith as pure belief and the hadith about a grain's weight of faith. Al-Ghazali compares abstention from utterance to abstention from prayer, saying it does not negate faith. He refutes the Murji'a who claim such a person will never enter the Fire. The footnote concludes that if one follows al-Ghazali's view, the detailed conditions for the shahada become unnecessary, but the person is still judged as a believer before Allah, not in worldly affairs.

شرط
شطر
إيمان
عمل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if action is a condition, it must be part of the essence.
Correction: The commentator explicitly says 'shart' means outside the essence; it is a prerequisite for worldly rulings, not intrinsic to faith.

Checkpoint
What does the term 'shart' mean in the context of this passage?
A) A part of the essence
B) Something outside the essence
C) A pillar of faith
D) A recommended act

Key Takeaway
The Ash'ari and Maturidi mainstream view is that action is a condition for applying worldly rulings, not an essential part of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If action is only a condition for worldly rulings and not for the reality of your faith, then why do you sometimes judge others' faith by their actions? What would it take for you to separate your evaluation of someone's actions from your judgment of their iman?
?
Does the fact that your deeds do not constitute your faith's essence make you more or less motivated to obey Allah? Examine your heart: is your obedience driven by a fear of losing faith itself, or by love and gratitude?
?
If your faith's reality is solely your internal conviction, then what does your struggle to act on that conviction reveal about the condition of your heart? What would it mean to treat action as a condition that protects and manifests faith, rather than as its foundation?

Practical Implications: Action as Condition for Worldly Rulings
Details the practical function of action as a condition and describes three categories of people.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the practical implications of the condition view, including the categories of believers based on their action.

Core Idea
Outer actions are necessary signs for implementing worldly rulings of faith.

After establishing that action is a condition external to faith's essence, this lesson dives into its practical application. The commentator explains why an outward sign is needed for worldly rulings like inheritance and prayer. He then distinguishes three categories: the silent believer, the excused, and the obstinate. This lesson also includes al-Ghazali's nuanced view on the obstinate person.

Guided Path
1
Read the rationale for the condition
The commentator explains that inner belief is hidden, so an outward sign is needed for worldly rulings.
2
Identify the three categories
Find the descriptions of the ordinary silent believer, the excused, and the obstinate person.
Note the different judgments in each case.
3
Understand the dual judgment
Some people are believers before Allah but not in worldly rulings; others are believers in both or disbelievers in both.
4
Examine al-Ghazali's view
Read the footnote from al-Ghazali, who argues that the obstinate person is still a believer before Allah.
Compare with the majority view.

۱۹ - فَقِيلَ : شَرْطٌ كَالعَمَلُ، وَقِيلَ : بَلْ شَطْرُ وَالاسْلَامَ اشْرَحَنَّ بِالعَمَلْ
قوله: (فَقِيلَ ... إلخ)؛ أي: إذا أردت تفصيل هذا الخلافِ فقيل ... إلى آخره، فالفاء فاء الفصيحة. ويحتمل أن تكون لمجرَّدِ العطف، فيكون معطوفاً على الجملة الاسمية وهي قوله والنطق (...) إلى آخره من عطف المفصل على المجمل .
وقوله : (شَرْطُ ... إلخ)؛ أي: خارج عن ماهِيَّتِهِ ، وهذا القولُ لمحققي الأشاعرة والماتريدية ولغيرهم .
وقد فهم الجمهورُ أن مرادهم أنه شرط لإجراء أحكام المؤمنين عليه؛ من التوارث، والتناكح ، والصلاة خلفَهُ، وعليه، والدفن في مقابر المسلمين، ومطالبته بالصلوات والزكوات وغير ذلك؛ لأن التصديق القلبي وإن كان إيماناً إلَّا أنه باطن خفي، فلا بد له من علامة ظاهرة تدلُّ عليه ؛ لتناط - أي : تعلّق ـ به به تلك الأحكام، فمَنْ صدق بقلبه ولم يقر بلسانه لا لعذر منعه ولا لإباء، بل اتفق له ذلك، فهو مؤمن عند الله غير مؤمن في الأحكام الدنيوية.
أما المعذور إذا قامت قرينة على إسلامه بغير النطق ؛ كالإشارة، فهو مؤمن فيهما . وأما الآبي ؛ بأن طلب منه النطق بالشهادتين فأبى، فهو كافر فيهما (١)، ولو أذعن
(۱) والذي استظهره إمامنا الغزالي أن الآبي مؤمن والمسألة فقهية وعبارته في إحيائه» (۱۱۸/۱): (الدرجة الخامسة : أن يصدق بالقلب ويساعده من العمر مهلة النطق بكلمتي الشهادة، وعلم وجوبها، ولكنه لم ينطق بها، فيحتمل أن يجعل امتناعه عن النطق كامتناعه عن الصلاة، ونقول : هو مؤمن غير مخلَّدٍ في النار، والإيمان هو التصديق المحض، واللسان ترجمان الإيمان، فلا بدَّ أن يكون الإيمان موجوداً بتمامه قبل اللسان حتى يترجمه اللسان، وهذا هو الأظهر؛ إذ لا مستند إلا اتباع موجبِ الألفاظ، ووضع اللسان أن الإيمان هو عبارة عن التصديق بالقلب، وقد قال : يخرج من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من الإيمان ، ولا ينعدم الإيمان من القلب بالسكوت عن النطق الواجب، كما لا ينعدم بالسكوت عن الفعل الواجب. وقال قائلون: القول ركن ؛ إذ ليس كلمتا الشهادة إخباراً عن القلب، بل هو إنشاء عقد آخر، وابتداء شهادة والتزام والأول أظهر، وقد غلا في هذا طائفة المرجئة فقالوا: هذا لا يدخل النار أصلاً وقالوا إن المؤمن وإن عصى فلا يدخل النار، وسنبطل ذلك عليهم). : وعلى هذا القول لا داعي أصلاً للشروط المذكورة في لفظ الشهادة كما لا يخفى، ولكن يبقى أن يقال من آمن بقلبه وأبى النطق بما يدل على إيمانه، فهو مؤمن عنده، ومن قال يقوله ولكن عند الله ، لا في الدنيا، أما إن اقترن بدليل دال على الإيمان؛ كأن قال: آمنت بما آمن به -
Is action a condition of faith or a part of it? 19 - So it was said: a condition like action, and it was said: rather a part, and Islam is explained by action. His saying: (so it was said ... etc.), i.e., if you want the detail of this disagreement, so it was said ... to the end. So the 'fa' is the fa of explanation. It is also possible that it is for mere conjunction, so it is conjoined to the nominal sentence which is his saying 'and speech ( ... )' to the end, as conjoining the detailed to the summary. And his saying: (a condition ... etc.), i.e., outside its essence, and this is the saying of the verifying scholars of the Ash'aris and Maturidis and others. And the majority understood that they mean it is a condition for applying the rulings of believers upon him: such as inheritance, marriage, praying behind him, and upon him, burial in Muslim cemeteries, and requiring him to pray, give zakat, and other things; because heart belief, even if it is faith, is hidden and concealed, so it must have an apparent sign indicating it, so that those rulings may be attached—i.e., connected—to it. So whoever believes in his heart but does not confess with his tongue, without an excuse preventing him nor obstinacy, but it so happens to him, he is a believer before Allah but not a believer in worldly rulings. As for the excused person, if there is evidence of his Islam other than speech, like a gesture, then he is a believer in both realms. As for the obstinate one: if he is asked to utter the two testimonies and he refuses, then he is a disbeliever in both realms (1), even if he acquiesces. (1) And what our Imam al-Ghazali considered most likely is that the obstinate one is a believer, and the matter is jurisprudential. His expression in his Ihya (1/118): (The fifth degree: that he believes in his heart and his lifespan allows him time to utter the two words of testimony, and he knows their obligation, but he does not utter them. Then it is possible to consider his abstention from utterance like his abstention from prayer, and we say: he is a believer not eternally in the Fire, and faith is pure belief, and the tongue is the interpreter of faith, so faith must exist in its entirety before the tongue so that the tongue may interpret it. And this is the most apparent; because there is no basis except following the implication of words, and the linguistic convention is that faith is expression of belief in the heart, and he [the Prophet] said: 'He will be brought out who has in his heart a grain's weight of faith.' And faith does not cease from the heart by silence about the obligatory utterance, just as it does not cease by silence about the obligatory action. And some said: utterance is a pillar, for the two words of testimony are not a report from the heart, but rather an initiation of another contract, and a beginning of testimony and commitment. And the first is more apparent, and a group of the Murji'a exaggerated in this and said that this person will not enter the Fire at all, and they said that the believer, even if he disobeys, will not enter the Fire, and we will refute that against them.) And according to this saying, there is no need at all for the conditions mentioned regarding the wording of the shahada, as is obvious. But it remains to be said: whoever believes in his heart and refuses to utter what indicates his faith, then he is a believer according to him [al-Ghazali], but it is said concerning his judgment: but before Allah, not in the world. If there is evidence indicating his faith, like saying: I believe in what so-and-so believed in -
Source pages p. 126

Commentary
This passage addresses the debated question: Is action (such as uttering the shahada) a condition (shart) for faith, or a part (shatr) of faith? The poem states that one view says it is a condition, like action, and another says it is a part. The commentator explains that the word 'fa' in 'fa-qila' is either for elaboration (fa al-fasiha) or simply for conjunction, connecting this detail to an earlier summary. He then clarifies that 'shart' means something outside the essence of faith. This view is held by the verifying scholars of the Ash'aris and Maturidis and others. The majority understood that this condition applies to worldly rulings (ahkam dunyawiyya) such as inheritance, marriage, prayer behind him, burial in Muslim cemeteries, and requiring him to perform religious duties. The reason is that inner belief (tasdiq qalbi) is hidden, so an outward sign is needed to attach these rulings. Therefore, if a person believes sincerely in his heart but does not utter the shahada without any excuse or obstinacy—just by happenstance—he is a believer before Allah but not considered a believer in worldly rulings. The excused person (e.g., one who cannot speak) is a believer in both realms if there is evidence like a gesture. The obstinate person (al-abi)—who is asked to utter the shahada and refuses—is a disbeliever in both realms. A lengthy footnote from al-Ghazali argues that the obstinate person is a believer before Allah, based on the definition of faith as pure belief and the hadith about a grain's weight of faith. Al-Ghazali compares abstention from utterance to abstention from prayer, saying it does not negate faith. He refutes the Murji'a who claim such a person will never enter the Fire. The footnote concludes that if one follows al-Ghazali's view, the detailed conditions for the shahada become unnecessary, but the person is still judged as a believer before Allah, not in worldly affairs.

تصديق قلبي
آبي
معذور

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if a person does not perform outward actions, they are not a believer at all.
Correction: The passage teaches that one can be a true believer before Allah even without outward action, unless obstinate refusal occurs.

Checkpoint
According to the majority, what is the status of a person who believes in their heart but does not utter the shahada due to obstinacy?
A) Believer before Allah and in worldly rulings
B) Believer before Allah but not in worldly rulings
C) Disbeliever in both realms
D) Disbeliever only in worldly rulings

Key Takeaway
The condition of action affects only worldly rulings; inner faith can be present without external display, except in cases of obstinate refusal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever judged someone's faith solely based on their outward actions, forgetting that inner belief is hidden? How can you balance the need for visible signs with humility about what only Allah knows?

If you were faced with a situation where uttering the shahada could cost you your life, would your heart's belief be enough to sustain you? Reflect on whether your faith is deep enough to survive without external expression.
?
The lesson distinguishes between worldly rulings and ultimate salvation. Do you live as if your outward compliance is enough for Allah, or do you actively nurture your inner conviction? What one change can you make today to strengthen your heart's belief over mere rituals?

Verbal Confession: Condition, Not Essence
Defines verbal confession as a condition and explains three cases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that verbal confession is a condition for worldly rulings, not part of the essence of iman, and how the rulings apply to different cases.

Core Idea
Verbal confession is a condition, not the essence of faith.

This passage from the Tuhfat al-Mureed clarifies a key distinction in Islamic theology: verbal confession (iqrar) is a requirement for applying worldly rulings, but it is not part of the inner reality of faith. The author explains the consensus of Ash'ari and Maturidi scholars and then details three scenarios to illustrate how this principle is applied.

Guided Path
1
Understand the condition-essence distinction
The passage begins by stating that verbal confession is a condition outside the essence of faith. This is a technical point that sets the framework for the rest of the discussion.
The condition is for practical purposes, not for salvation.
2
Identify the purpose of the condition
The majority understood that the condition is to enable the application of worldly rulings. Inward faith is hidden, so an outward sign is needed for legal transactions.
3
Examine the three cases
The passage outlines three scenarios: silent believer, excused, and refuser. Note how the ruling differs in each case.
The excused person is considered a believer in both worlds if there is evidence, while the refuser is a disbeliever.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (شَرْطُ ... إلخ)؛ أي: خارج عن ماهِيَّتِهِ ، وهذا القولُ لمحققي الأشاعرة والماتريدية ولغيرهم . وقد فهم الجمهورُ أن مرادهم أنه شرط لإجراء أحكام المؤمنين عليه؛ من التوارث، والتناكح ، والصلاة خلفَهُ، وعليه، والدفن في مقابر المسلمين، ومطالبته بالصلوات والزكوات وغير ذلك؛ لأن التصديق القلبي وإن كان إيماناً إلَّا أنه باطن خفي، فلا بد له من علامة ظاهرة تدلُّ عليه ؛ لتناط - أي : تعلّق ـ به به تلك الأحكام، فمَنْ صدق بقلبه ولم يقر بلسانه لا لعذر منعه ولا لإباء، بل اتفق له ذلك، فهو مؤمن عند الله غير مؤمن في الأحكام الدنيوية. أما المعذور إذا قامت قرينة على إسلامه بغير النطق ؛ كالإشارة، فهو مؤمن فيهما . وأما الآبي ؛ بأن طلب منه النطق بالشهادتين فأبى، فهو كافر فيهما (١)، ولو أذعن
And his saying: 'condition ... etc.' means: outside its essence, and this is the statement of the verifying scholars of the Ash'aris and Maturidis and others. And the majority understood that their intent is that it is a condition for applying the rulings of believers to him: of inheritance, marriage, prayer behind him, and upon him, and burial in Muslim cemeteries, and requiring him to perform prayers and alms and other than that; because inward assent, even if it is faith, is but hidden and concealed, so it must have an apparent sign indicating it, so that those rulings may be attached (i.e., connected) to it. So whoever affirms in his heart and does not confess with his tongue, neither due to an excuse preventing him nor due to refusal, but it happens thus to him, then he is a believer before Allah, not a believer in worldly rulings. As for the excused, if there is evidence of his Islam other than speech, like a gesture, then he is a believer in both. And as for the refuser, such that he is asked to utter the two testimonies and he refuses, then he is a disbeliever in both (1), even if he acquiesces.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage defines the condition of verbal confession (shart) in relation to the essence (mahiyya) of faith. The commentator explains that the phrase 'shart...' means the condition is outside the essence of faith, and this is the view of the verifying scholars among the Ash'aris and Maturidis. The majority of scholars understood that the purpose of the condition is to apply worldly rulings to a believer, such as inheritance, marriage, praying behind him, burial, and religious obligations like prayer and zakat. The reason is that inner assent (tasdiq qalbi) is hidden, so an outward sign is needed to anchor those rulings. The passage then explains three cases: 1) A person who believes in heart but does not verbally confess without any excuse or refusal—he is a believer before Allah but not in worldly rulings. 2) The excused person (ma'dhur) who has some evidence of Islam other than speech, like a gesture—he is a believer in both worlds (here and the afterlife). 3) The refuser (abi) who is asked to utter the testimony of faith and refuses—he is a disbeliever in both worlds, even if he internally acquiesces.

شَرْط (shart)
ماهِيَّة (mahiyya)
تصديق (tasdiq)
إقرار (iqrar)
مؤمن (mu'min)
كافر (kafir)
معذور (ma'dhur)
آبٍ (abi)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the condition of verbal confession is part of the essence of iman.
Correction: Verbal confession is a condition for worldly rulings, not part of the inner essence of faith (tasdiq qalbi).

Checkpoint

B) He is a believer before Allah but not a believer in worldly rulings.
C) He is a disbeliever in both worlds.
D) He is considered a hypocrite.

Key Takeaway
Verbal confession is a condition for worldly rulings, not the essence of faith; the rulings vary based on presence or absence of excuse and refusal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

This passage forces you to see that outward signs matter for the community's judgment. Are you content with being judged only by your outward signs, or do you strive for inward sincerity?

Ghazali's View on the Refuser: Faith is Assent
Ghazali defends the view that the refuser is a believer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam al-Ghazali's argument that a person who assents in his heart but refuses to utter the testimony is still a believer, and why he considers the issue a jurisprudential one.

Core Idea
Faith is pure assent; the tongue is its interpreter, not its essence.

Imam al-Ghazali addresses a critical boundary case: a person who truly believes in his heart yet refuses to utter the testimony of faith. Is such a person a believer? Ghazali argues yes, treating the matter as a fiqhi issue analogous to refraining from prayer. This passage presents his reasoning from the Ihya' and distinguishes his view from the extremist Murji'a.

Guided Path
1
Read Ghazali's passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall argument.
Notice how Ghazali quotes from his Ihya'.
2
Identify Ghazali's thesis
Find the sentence where Ghazali states his view on the refuser being a believer.
It is at the beginning: 'والذي استظهره إمامنا الغزالي أن الآبي مؤمن'.
3
Understand his analogy
Ghazali compares abstaining from utterance to abstaining from prayer. What does this imply about the status of the refuser?
4
Note his definition of faith
He defines faith as pure assent (tasdiq mahd). How does this support his conclusion?
5
Distinguish from Murji'a
Read the last sentence where Ghazali distinguishes his view from the Murji'a. Why is this important?

والذي استظهره إمامنا الغزالي أن الآبي مؤمن والمسألة فقهية وعبارته في إحيائه» (۱۱۸/۱): (الدرجة الخامسة : أن يصدق بالقلب ويساعده من العمر مهلة النطق بكلمتي الشهادة، وعلم وجوبها، ولكنه لم ينطق بها، فيحتمل أن يجعل امتناعه عن النطق كامتناعه عن الصلاة، ونقول : هو مؤمن غير مخلَّدٍ في النار، والإيمان هو التصديق المحض، واللسان ترجمان الإيمان، فلا بدَّ أن يكون الإيمان موجوداً بتمامه قبل اللسان حتى يترجمه اللسان، وهذا هو الأظهر؛ إذ لا مستند إلا اتباع موجبِ الألفاظ، ووضع اللسان أن الإيمان هو عبارة عن التصديق بالقلب، وقد قال : يخرج من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من الإيمان ، ولا ينعدم الإيمان من القلب بالسكوت عن النطق الواجب، كما لا ينعدم بالسكوت عن الفعل الواجب. وقال قائلون: القول ركن ؛ إذ ليس كلمتا الشهادة إخباراً عن القلب، بل هو إنشاء عقد آخر، وابتداء شهادة والتزام والأول أظهر، وقد غلا في هذا طائفة المرجئة فقالوا: هذا لا يدخل النار أصلاً وقالوا إن المؤمن وإن عصى فلا يدخل النار، وسنبطل ذلك عليهم). : وعلى هذا القول لا داعي أصلاً للشروط المذكورة في لفظ الشهادة كما لا يخفى، ولكن يبقى أن يقال من آمن بقلبه وأبى النطق بما يدل على إيمانه، فهو مؤمن عنده، ومن قال يقوله ولكن عند الله ، لا في الدنيا، أما إن اقترن بدليل دال على الإيمان؛ كأن قال: آمنت بما آمن به - الإلهيات في قلبه فلا ينفعُهُ ذلك ولو في الآخرة (۱) ، ومن أقرَّ بلسانه ولم يصدق بقلبه كالمنافق، المسلمون، فيكون ناجياً في الدنيا والآخرة، وعلى هذا القول جرى أهل التحقيق كما سينقل عن الرملي . ونص العلامة الشيخ أحمد زيني دحلان في أسنى المطالب) (ص) (۹) أن مسألة الآبي المقصود من الإباء فيها هو الإباء عن الإسلام، لا الإباء عن النطق، وهو خلاف الجاري في كتب الكلام. وقال الإمام الشعراني في اليواقيت والجواهر» (۲۰۷/۲) : (وصاحب التوحيد سعيد بأي وجه كان توحيده) . (۱) ونزيد في مسألة الآبي بسطاً بنقل ما قاله العلامة الرملي الكبير في فتاويه» (٣٩١/٤)، وهذا نص السؤال والجواب: (سُئل عن شخص بلغته دعوة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فآمن بالله بقلبه ولم يتلفظ بالشهادتين مع القدرة على ذلك إلى أن مات فهل هذا الإيمان ينفعُهُ ويكون في الجنة أو لا؟ وإذا قلتم : ينفعه، فما وجب عن قول الإمام النووي في شرح مسلم) حيث قال: واتفق أهل السنة من المحدثين والفقهاء والمتكلمين على أن المؤمن الذي يحكم بأنه من أهل القبلة لا يخلد في النار، لا يكون إلا من اعتقد بقلبه دين الإسلام اعتقاداً جازماً خالياً من الشكوك، ونطق بالشهادتين، فإن اقتصر على أحدهما ، لم يكن من أهل القبلة أصلاً، إلا إذا عجز عن النطق لخلل في لسانه، أو لعدم التمكن منه لمعالجة المنيَّة أو بغير ذلك؟ فأجاب : بأنه مؤمن في أحكام الآخرة دون الدنيا ؛ لأن الإيمان في الشرع تصديق القلب بما عُلم منه ضرورة مجيء الرسول من عند الله به، وقد اختلفوا في أن الإقرار بالشهادتين من المتمكّن م شرط لإجراء أحكام الإيمان عليه أو جزء منه؟ فذهب جمهور المحققين على الأول، وقد قال السعد التفتازاني في شرح المقاصد: أما إذا جعلنا الإيمان اسماً للتصديق فقط، وأن الإقرار شرط لإجراء الأحكام في الدنيا من الصلاة عليه وخلفه والدفن في مقابر المسلمين، والمطالبة بالعشر والزكوات ونحو ذلك، فهو مؤمن في أحكام الآخرة. انتهى. وقال غيره: من عجز عن التلفظ بالشهادتين لخرس أو اخترام منية قبل التمكن، صح إيمانه، قال الإمام الرازي: قطعاً، وقال في الشفاء»: على الصحيح، وإن عرض عليه الإسلام فأبى مع القدرة عليه كأبي طالب، لم يكن مؤمناً بالاتفاق، وكذلك إن لم يعرض عليه عند الجمهور، وقال الغزالي: إنه يكفيه، وقال: كيف يعذَّبُ مَنْ قلبه مملوء بالإيمان؟! وهو المقصود الأصلي، غير أنه لخفاء أنيط الحكم بالإقرار الظاهر، وعلى هذا فهو مؤمن عند الله تعالى، غير مؤمن في أحكام الدنيا عكس المنافق، وهذا ظاهرُ كلام إمام الحرمين في «الإرشاد» أيضاً). بل نقل الإمام الشعراني عن شيخه سيدي علي الخواص في الجواهر والدرر» أن من استفرغ وسعَهُ في النظر ولم يصل للمعرفة، فهو ناج هذا على التسليم بوقوع هذه الصورة، وتقدم أنها مفروضة ولا وجود لها من حيث النقل .
And what our Imam al-Ghazali favored is that the refuser is a believer and the issue is fiqhi; his expression in his 'Ihya'' (1/118): (The fifth degree: that he affirms with his heart and his life grants him time to utter the two testimonies, and he knows their obligation, yet he does not utter them. So it is possible to make his abstention from utterance like his abstention from prayer, and we say: he is a believer, not eternally in the Fire. Faith is pure assent, and the tongue is the interpreter of faith; so faith must exist in its entirety before the tongue so that the tongue may interpret it. This is the apparent view, for there is no basis except following the implications of words, and the linguistic convention that faith is expression of assent with the heart. And He said: 'There will come out from the Fire he who has in his heart the weight of a mustard seed of faith,' and faith does not vanish from the heart by remaining silent about the obligatory utterance, just as it does not vanish by remaining silent about the obligatory deed. And some said: Utterance is a pillar, for the two testimonies are not an informing about the heart, but rather they are the establishment of another contract and the initiation of testimony and commitment. The first is more apparent. And a group of the Murji'a exaggerated in this matter, saying: this one will not enter the Fire at all, and they said that the believer, even if he disobeys, will not enter the Fire. We will refute that against them). Then he said: On this view, there is no need at all for the aforementioned conditions regarding the wording of the testimony, as is not hidden, but it remains to be said: whoever believes in his heart and refuses to utter what indicates his faith, then he is a believer according to him, and some say: it is said, but before Allah, not in this world. But if there is evidence indicating his faith, like if he says: I believe in what he believed in— al-Ilahiyyat (The Divine Matters) in his heart, that will not benefit him even in the afterlife (1). And whoever confesses with his tongue but does not affirm with his heart, like the hypocrite, among the Muslims, then he is saved in this world and the afterlife. And on this view proceeded the people of verification, as will be quoted from al-Ramli. And the text of the scholar Shaykh Ahmad Zayni Dahlan in 'Asna al-Matalib' (p. 9) that the issue of the refuser: what is intended by 'refusal' here is refusal of Islam, not refusal of utterance, contrary to what is current in books of kalam. And Imam al-Sha'rani said in 'al-Yawaqit wa al-Jawahir' (2/207): (The possessor of tawhid is happy by whatever aspect his tawhid is). (1) And we add elaboration on the issue of the refuser by quoting what the great scholar al-Ramli said in his 'Fatawa' (4/391); this is the text of the question and answer: (He was asked about a person who the call of the Prophet (peace be upon him) reached, and he believed in Allah with his heart but did not utter the two testimonies while able to do so until he died: does this faith benefit him and will he be in Paradise or not? And if you say: it benefits him, then what about the statement of Imam al-Nawawi in 'Sharh Muslim' where he said: The Ahl al-Sunnah from the hadith scholars, jurists, and theologians agree that the believer who is judged to be among the people of the qibla will not abide eternally in the Fire, only he who believes in his heart the religion of Islam with firm belief free from doubts and utters the two testimonies; if he confines himself to one of them, he is not among the people of the qibla at all, except if he is unable to utter due to a defect in his tongue, or due to inability caused by the throes of death or otherwise? He answered: that he is a believer in the rulings of the afterlife but not of this world; because faith in the Sacred Law is the assent of the heart to what is known of the Prophet's bringing of it from Allah necessarily. And they disagreed about whether confessing the two testimonies for the one who is able is a condition for applying the rulings of faith to him or a part of it? The majority of verifying scholars adopted the first. And al-Sa'd al-Taftazani said in 'Sharh al-Maqasid': If we make faith a name for mere assent, and that confession is a condition for applying the rulings in this world, such as praying over him and behind him and burial in Muslim cemeteries and demanding the tithe and alms and the like, then he is a believer in the rulings of the afterlife. End quote. And others said: Whoever is unable to utter the two testimonies due to dumbness or death before being able, his faith is valid. Imam al-Razi said: absolutely, and in 'al-Shifa' it is said: according to the sound view. And if Islam is presented to him and he refuses while able, like Abu Talib, he is not a believer by consensus. Similarly, if it is not presented to him, according to the majority. And al-Ghazali said: it suffices for him. And he said: How can one whose heart is filled with faith be punished?! And he is the primary intention; but due to his hiddenness, the ruling is attached to outward confession. On this basis, he is a believer before Allah Almighty, not a believer in the rulings of this world, opposite of the hypocrite. And this is apparently the statement of Imam al-Haramayn in 'al-Irshad' as well). Rather, Imam al-Sha'rani narrated from his shaykh Sayyidi 'Ali al-Khawas in 'al-Jawahir wa al-Durar' that whoever exhausts his capacity in reflection and does not arrive at knowledge, he is saved. This is upon the admission of the occurrence of this scenario, and it was mentioned earlier that it is merely hypothetical and has no existence according to transmitted evidence.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion of the refuser (abi) and related issues. It begins by presenting Imam al-Ghazali's preferred view that the refuser is a believer, treating the matter as a fiqhi (jurisprudential) rather than a doctrinal one. The text quotes Ghazali's 'Ihya' where he describes the 'fifth degree': a person who believes in heart, has time to utter the testimony, knows it is obligatory, but does not utter. Ghazali analogizes this abstention to abstaining from prayer, concluding the person is a believer not eternally in the Fire. He argues that faith is pure assent (tasdiq mahd) and the tongue is its interpreter; faith must exist before the tongue can interpret. The Quranic hadith 'there will come out from the Fire he who has the weight of a mustard seed of faith' supports his view. He notes that some scholars consider utterance a pillar (rukn), but Ghazali sees that view as contrary to the linguistic understanding. Then the passage mentions the Murji'a who exaggeratedly claim such a person will not enter the Fire at all, which Ghazali promises to refute. The commentary then clarifies that on Ghazali's view, the conditions attached to the testimony are unnecessary; but there remains the case of a person who believes but refuses to express it—he is a believer in God's sight, not in this world's rulings, unless accompanied by evidence. The text then moves to page 128, discussing a person who believes in heart without utterance: it says if a person believes in heart but does not benefit (even in the afterlife) according to some views. The passage then clarifies the view of the 'people of verification' (ahl al-tahqiq) as transmitted from al-Ramli. It also quotes Shaykh Ahmad Zayni Dahlan that the 'refusal' in the abi case is refusal of Islam, not refusal of utterance, contrary to standard kalam texts. Imam al-Sha'rani is quoted saying that the possessor of tawhid is happy regardless of the aspect of his tawhid. Next, the passage gives an extended fatwa from al-Ramli on a person who believes but never utters the testimony: al-Ramli answers that such a person is a believer in the afterlife but not in this world, citing Taftazani. The fatwa also discusses the case of those unable to utter (due to dumbness or death) as valid, and the case of Abu Talib who refused when able is kufr by consensus. Ghazali's view that belief suffices is reiterated. Finally, the passage concludes with a narration from al-Sha'rani that one who exhausts his capacity in speculation but does not reach knowledge is saved, though this scenario is hypothetical and does not occur in transmitted evidence.

Key Terms
آبٍ (abi)
إيمان (iman)
تصديق (tasdiq)
فقهية (fiqhiya)
مرجئة (Murji'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Ghazali's view is the same as the Murji'a.
Correction: Ghazali explicitly distinguishes his view from the Murji'a, who claim the refuser never enters the Fire.

Checkpoint
According to Ghazali, what is the analogy for the refuser's abstention from utterance?
A) abstention from charity
B) abstention from prayer
C) abstention from fasting
D) abstention from hajj

Key Takeaway
Ghazali argues that faith is assent of the heart, so the refuser who believes is a believer, though his refusal to utter is sinful.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever reduced your faith to outward statements, assuming that simply saying the shahada is enough without inner conviction? In light of Ghazali's teaching, what would you say to yourself about the state of your heart's assent? Examine whether your verbal confession matches your inner tasdiq—and if not, what will you change today?
?
Ghazali argues that the refuser who believes but does not speak is still a believer, albeit sinful. Does this truth comfort you or unsettle you? Are there areas of your life where you know the truth but refuse to act or speak it, thinking it doesn't affect your faith? How will you respond to that tension right now?
?
The Murji'a claimed that sin does not endanger a believer's ultimate salvation. Have you ever relied on a similar false security, assuming your faith alone saves you regardless of your actions? Confront that assumption with Ghazali's insistence that the refuser is sinful—what does this reveal about the urgency of obedience in your own life?

Faith and Disbelief
intermediate
5 min
Al-Ramli's Fatwa: Faith Without Utterance
Al-Ramli gives a fatwa regarding the person who believes but does not utter the testimony.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the distinction between rulings of this world and the afterlife regarding faith, and why al-Ramli considered the person who believes without utterance a believer in the afterlife but not in worldly law.

Core Idea
Faith is inward; utterance is a condition for worldly rulings, not for salvation.

Building on Ghazali's view, al-Ramli's fatwa addresses a practical question: what about a person who believes in his heart but dies without uttering the testimony? Al-Ramli distinguishes between the rulings of this world (where utterance is required) and the afterlife (where inward faith suffices). This passage also clarifies the positions of other scholars on inability cases.

Guided Path
1
Read the transition paragraph
Start with the paragraph after Ghazali's quote. It summarizes the implications and introduces al-Ramli's fatwa.
2
Read the fatwa question
Read the question posed to al-Ramli. What is the specific scenario?
3
Study al-Ramli's answer
Focus on his distinction between rulings of this world and the afterlife. Find the key sentence.
4
Identify the shart vs rukn debate
The fatwa mentions disagreement about whether utterance is a condition or a pillar. What is the majority view according to Taftazani?
5
Note the special cases
Read the examples: dumbness, deathbed, Abu Talib. How do they illustrate the principle?

والذي استظهره إمامنا الغزالي أن الآبي مؤمن والمسألة فقهية وعبارته في إحيائه» (۱۱۸/۱): (الدرجة الخامسة : أن يصدق بالقلب ويساعده من العمر مهلة النطق بكلمتي الشهادة، وعلم وجوبها، ولكنه لم ينطق بها، فيحتمل أن يجعل امتناعه عن النطق كامتناعه عن الصلاة، ونقول : هو مؤمن غير مخلَّدٍ في النار، والإيمان هو التصديق المحض، واللسان ترجمان الإيمان، فلا بدَّ أن يكون الإيمان موجوداً بتمامه قبل اللسان حتى يترجمه اللسان، وهذا هو الأظهر؛ إذ لا مستند إلا اتباع موجبِ الألفاظ، ووضع اللسان أن الإيمان هو عبارة عن التصديق بالقلب، وقد قال : يخرج من كان في قلبه مثقال ذرة من الإيمان ، ولا ينعدم الإيمان من القلب بالسكوت عن النطق الواجب، كما لا ينعدم بالسكوت عن الفعل الواجب. وقال قائلون: القول ركن ؛ إذ ليس كلمتا الشهادة إخباراً عن القلب، بل هو إنشاء عقد آخر، وابتداء شهادة والتزام والأول أظهر، وقد غلا في هذا طائفة المرجئة فقالوا: هذا لا يدخل النار أصلاً وقالوا إن المؤمن وإن عصى فلا يدخل النار، وسنبطل ذلك عليهم). : وعلى هذا القول لا داعي أصلاً للشروط المذكورة في لفظ الشهادة كما لا يخفى، ولكن يبقى أن يقال من آمن بقلبه وأبى النطق بما يدل على إيمانه، فهو مؤمن عنده، ومن قال يقوله ولكن عند الله ، لا في الدنيا، أما إن اقترن بدليل دال على الإيمان؛ كأن قال: آمنت بما آمن به - الإلهيات في قلبه فلا ينفعُهُ ذلك ولو في الآخرة (۱) ، ومن أقرَّ بلسانه ولم يصدق بقلبه كالمنافق، المسلمون، فيكون ناجياً في الدنيا والآخرة، وعلى هذا القول جرى أهل التحقيق كما سينقل عن الرملي . ونص العلامة الشيخ أحمد زيني دحلان في أسنى المطالب) (ص) (۹) أن مسألة الآبي المقصود من الإباء فيها هو الإباء عن الإسلام، لا الإباء عن النطق، وهو خلاف الجاري في كتب الكلام. وقال الإمام الشعراني في اليواقيت والجواهر» (۲۰۷/۲) : (وصاحب التوحيد سعيد بأي وجه كان توحيده) . (۱) ونزيد في مسألة الآبي بسطاً بنقل ما قاله العلامة الرملي الكبير في فتاويه» (٣٩١/٤)، وهذا نص السؤال والجواب: (سُئل عن شخص بلغته دعوة النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ، فآمن بالله بقلبه ولم يتلفظ بالشهادتين مع القدرة على ذلك إلى أن مات فهل هذا الإيمان ينفعُهُ ويكون في الجنة أو لا؟ وإذا قلتم : ينفعه، فما وجب عن قول الإمام النووي في شرح مسلم) حيث قال: واتفق أهل السنة من المحدثين والفقهاء والمتكلمين على أن المؤمن الذي يحكم بأنه من أهل القبلة لا يخلد في النار، لا يكون إلا من اعتقد بقلبه دين الإسلام اعتقاداً جازماً خالياً من الشكوك، ونطق بالشهادتين، فإن اقتصر على أحدهما ، لم يكن من أهل القبلة أصلاً، إلا إذا عجز عن النطق لخلل في لسانه، أو لعدم التمكن منه لمعالجة المنيَّة أو بغير ذلك؟ فأجاب : بأنه مؤمن في أحكام الآخرة دون الدنيا ؛ لأن الإيمان في الشرع تصديق القلب بما عُلم منه ضرورة مجيء الرسول من عند الله به، وقد اختلفوا في أن الإقرار بالشهادتين من المتمكّن م شرط لإجراء أحكام الإيمان عليه أو جزء منه؟ فذهب جمهور المحققين على الأول، وقد قال السعد التفتازاني في شرح المقاصد: أما إذا جعلنا الإيمان اسماً للتصديق فقط، وأن الإقرار شرط لإجراء الأحكام في الدنيا من الصلاة عليه وخلفه والدفن في مقابر المسلمين، والمطالبة بالعشر والزكوات ونحو ذلك، فهو مؤمن في أحكام الآخرة. انتهى. وقال غيره: من عجز عن التلفظ بالشهادتين لخرس أو اخترام منية قبل التمكن، صح إيمانه، قال الإمام الرازي: قطعاً، وقال في الشفاء»: على الصحيح، وإن عرض عليه الإسلام فأبى مع القدرة عليه كأبي طالب، لم يكن مؤمناً بالاتفاق، وكذلك إن لم يعرض عليه عند الجمهور، وقال الغزالي: إنه يكفيه، وقال: كيف يعذَّبُ مَنْ قلبه مملوء بالإيمان؟! وهو المقصود الأصلي، غير أنه لخفاء أنيط الحكم بالإقرار الظاهر، وعلى هذا فهو مؤمن عند الله تعالى، غير مؤمن في أحكام الدنيا عكس المنافق، وهذا ظاهرُ كلام إمام الحرمين في «الإرشاد» أيضاً). بل نقل الإمام الشعراني عن شيخه سيدي علي الخواص في الجواهر والدرر» أن من استفرغ وسعَهُ في النظر ولم يصل للمعرفة، فهو ناج هذا على التسليم بوقوع هذه الصورة، وتقدم أنها مفروضة ولا وجود لها من حيث النقل .
And what our Imam al-Ghazali favored is that the refuser is a believer and the issue is fiqhi; his expression in his 'Ihya'' (1/118): (The fifth degree: that he affirms with his heart and his life grants him time to utter the two testimonies, and he knows their obligation, yet he does not utter them. So it is possible to make his abstention from utterance like his abstention from prayer, and we say: he is a believer, not eternally in the Fire. Faith is pure assent, and the tongue is the interpreter of faith; so faith must exist in its entirety before the tongue so that the tongue may interpret it. This is the apparent view, for there is no basis except following the implications of words, and the linguistic convention that faith is expression of assent with the heart. And He said: 'There will come out from the Fire he who has in his heart the weight of a mustard seed of faith,' and faith does not vanish from the heart by remaining silent about the obligatory utterance, just as it does not vanish by remaining silent about the obligatory deed. And some said: Utterance is a pillar, for the two testimonies are not an informing about the heart, but rather they are the establishment of another contract and the initiation of testimony and commitment. The first is more apparent. And a group of the Murji'a exaggerated in this matter, saying: this one will not enter the Fire at all, and they said that the believer, even if he disobeys, will not enter the Fire. We will refute that against them). Then he said: On this view, there is no need at all for the aforementioned conditions regarding the wording of the testimony, as is not hidden, but it remains to be said: whoever believes in his heart and refuses to utter what indicates his faith, then he is a believer according to him, and some say: it is said, but before Allah, not in this world. But if there is evidence indicating his faith, like if he says: I believe in what he believed in— al-Ilahiyyat (The Divine Matters) in his heart, that will not benefit him even in the afterlife (1). And whoever confesses with his tongue but does not affirm with his heart, like the hypocrite, among the Muslims, then he is saved in this world and the afterlife. And on this view proceeded the people of verification, as will be quoted from al-Ramli. And the text of the scholar Shaykh Ahmad Zayni Dahlan in 'Asna al-Matalib' (p. 9) that the issue of the refuser: what is intended by 'refusal' here is refusal of Islam, not refusal of utterance, contrary to what is current in books of kalam. And Imam al-Sha'rani said in 'al-Yawaqit wa al-Jawahir' (2/207): (The possessor of tawhid is happy by whatever aspect his tawhid is). (1) And we add elaboration on the issue of the refuser by quoting what the great scholar al-Ramli said in his 'Fatawa' (4/391); this is the text of the question and answer: (He was asked about a person who the call of the Prophet (peace be upon him) reached, and he believed in Allah with his heart but did not utter the two testimonies while able to do so until he died: does this faith benefit him and will he be in Paradise or not? And if you say: it benefits him, then what about the statement of Imam al-Nawawi in 'Sharh Muslim' where he said: The Ahl al-Sunnah from the hadith scholars, jurists, and theologians agree that the believer who is judged to be among the people of the qibla will not abide eternally in the Fire, only he who believes in his heart the religion of Islam with firm belief free from doubts and utters the two testimonies; if he confines himself to one of them, he is not among the people of the qibla at all, except if he is unable to utter due to a defect in his tongue, or due to inability caused by the throes of death or otherwise? He answered: that he is a believer in the rulings of the afterlife but not of this world; because faith in the Sacred Law is the assent of the heart to what is known of the Prophet's bringing of it from Allah necessarily. And they disagreed about whether confessing the two testimonies for the one who is able is a condition for applying the rulings of faith to him or a part of it? The majority of verifying scholars adopted the first. And al-Sa'd al-Taftazani said in 'Sharh al-Maqasid': If we make faith a name for mere assent, and that confession is a condition for applying the rulings in this world, such as praying over him and behind him and burial in Muslim cemeteries and demanding the tithe and alms and the like, then he is a believer in the rulings of the afterlife. End quote. And others said: Whoever is unable to utter the two testimonies due to dumbness or death before being able, his faith is valid. Imam al-Razi said: absolutely, and in 'al-Shifa' it is said: according to the sound view. And if Islam is presented to him and he refuses while able, like Abu Talib, he is not a believer by consensus. Similarly, if it is not presented to him, according to the majority. And al-Ghazali said: it suffices for him. And he said: How can one whose heart is filled with faith be punished?! And he is the primary intention; but due to his hiddenness, the ruling is attached to outward confession. On this basis, he is a believer before Allah Almighty, not a believer in the rulings of this world, opposite of the hypocrite. And this is apparently the statement of Imam al-Haramayn in 'al-Irshad' as well). Rather, Imam al-Sha'rani narrated from his shaykh Sayyidi 'Ali al-Khawas in 'al-Jawahir wa al-Durar' that whoever exhausts his capacity in reflection and does not arrive at knowledge, he is saved. This is upon the admission of the occurrence of this scenario, and it was mentioned earlier that it is merely hypothetical and has no existence according to transmitted evidence.
Source pages p. 127

Commentary
This passage is an extended discussion of the refuser (abi) and related issues. It begins by presenting Imam al-Ghazali's preferred view that the refuser is a believer, treating the matter as a fiqhi (jurisprudential) rather than a doctrinal one. The text quotes Ghazali's 'Ihya' where he describes the 'fifth degree': a person who believes in heart, has time to utter the testimony, knows it is obligatory, but does not utter. Ghazali analogizes this abstention to abstaining from prayer, concluding the person is a believer not eternally in the Fire. He argues that faith is pure assent (tasdiq mahd) and the tongue is its interpreter; faith must exist before the tongue can interpret. The Quranic hadith 'there will come out from the Fire he who has the weight of a mustard seed of faith' supports his view. He notes that some scholars consider utterance a pillar (rukn), but Ghazali sees that view as contrary to the linguistic understanding. Then the passage mentions the Murji'a who exaggeratedly claim such a person will not enter the Fire at all, which Ghazali promises to refute. The commentary then clarifies that on Ghazali's view, the conditions attached to the testimony are unnecessary; but there remains the case of a person who believes but refuses to express it—he is a believer in God's sight, not in this world's rulings, unless accompanied by evidence. The text then moves to page 128, discussing a person who believes in heart without utterance: it says if a person believes in heart but does not benefit (even in the afterlife) according to some views. The passage then clarifies the view of the 'people of verification' (ahl al-tahqiq) as transmitted from al-Ramli. It also quotes Shaykh Ahmad Zayni Dahlan that the 'refusal' in the abi case is refusal of Islam, not refusal of utterance, contrary to standard kalam texts. Imam al-Sha'rani is quoted saying that the possessor of tawhid is happy regardless of the aspect of his tawhid. Next, the passage gives an extended fatwa from al-Ramli on a person who believes but never utters the testimony: al-Ramli answers that such a person is a believer in the afterlife but not in this world, citing Taftazani. The fatwa also discusses the case of those unable to utter (due to dumbness or death) as valid, and the case of Abu Talib who refused when able is kufr by consensus. Ghazali's view that belief suffices is reiterated. Finally, the passage concludes with a narration from al-Sha'rani that one who exhausts his capacity in speculation but does not reach knowledge is saved, though this scenario is hypothetical and does not occur in transmitted evidence.

Key Terms
شرط (shart)
ركن (rukn)
مرجئة (Murji'a)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: If the refuser is a believer, then utterance is completely unnecessary.
Correction: Al-Ramli clarifies that utterance is a condition for worldly rulings; the refuser is a believer only in the afterlife, not in this world's law.

Checkpoint
According to al-Ramli, a person who believes in heart but does not utter the testimony while able is:
A) a disbeliever in both worlds
B) a believer in both worlds
C) a believer in the afterlife but not in worldly rulings
D) a hypocrite

Key Takeaway
Al-Ramli's fatwa establishes that inward faith alone suffices for salvation, but outward testimony is required for the application of Islamic law in this world.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If your outward practice—the ‘utterance’ of your faith—were stripped away, would your heart alone be enough to save you? What would you need to change in your inner life to be sure?
?
The refuser in this fatwa believed yet remained silent. Are there truths about your faith you know but have not spoken—whether from fear, comfort, or neglect? What will you do about that silence starting today?
?
Al-Ramli shows that the hypocrite is ‘saved’ in this world but lost in the next. Examine your own worship: do you ever do what you do for the eyes of others? How can you purify your intention so that your heart matches your tongue?

Faith and Disbelief
beginner

The One Who Exhausts His Capacity: A Hypothetical Case
Al-Sha'rani narrates that one who exhausts his capacity in reflection without attaining knowledge is saved, though hypothetical.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the view that a person who exhausts his capacity in seeking knowledge but fails to attain it may be saved, and why this scenario is considered hypothetical.

Core Idea
Sincere effort in seeking truth may bring salvation, even if knowledge is not attained.

The final part of this discussion raises an intriguing hypothetical: what about someone who diligently seeks knowledge of God but, due to intellectual limitation, does not arrive at proper understanding? Imam al-Sha'rani narrates from his teacher that such a person is saved. However, the passage notes that this scenario is merely hypothetical and has no actual occurrence according to transmitted evidence.

Guided Path
1
Read the narration
Read the short passage from al-Sha'rani. What does it say about the one who exhausts his capacity?
2
Understand the qualification
The passage adds that this scenario is hypothetical and does not occur. Why is this qualification important?
3
Reflect on the principle
Consider the broader principle: sincere effort is rewarded even if knowledge is not attained. How does this relate to God's justice?
