الخلاف في زيادة الإيمان ونقصه
٢١ - وَرُجِّحَتْ زِيَادَةُ الْإِيمَانِ بِمَا تَزِيدُ طَاعَةُ الْإِنْسَانِ
٢٢ - وَنَقْصُهُ بِنَقْصِهَا وَقِيلَ: لَا وَقِيلَ: لَا خُلْفَ كَذَا قَدْ نُقِلَا

قوله: (وَرُجِّحَتْ زِيَادَةُ الْإِيمَانِ ... إلخ): تقدَّمَ أن العمل من كمال الإيمان عند أهل السنة، وقد ذكر المصنف هنا أنه يزيد بزيادته وينقصُ بنقصه، فقال: (وَرُجِّحَتْ زِيَادَةُ الْإِيمَانِ ... إلى آخره؛ أي: رَجَّحَ جماعةٌ من العلماء وهم جمهورُ الأشاعرة القول بزيادة الإيمان؛ لأنه لا معنى لترجيح زيادة الإيمان إلا ترجيح القول بها. وقوله: بِمَا تَزِيدُ طَاعَةُ الْإِنْسَانِ أي: بسبب زيادة طاعة الإنسان، فالباء سببية، و(ما) مصدرية، والطاعةُ: فعلُ المأمور به، واجتناب المنهي عنه.
[The chapter on] the disagreement over the increase and decrease of faith. 21 - And the increase of faith is given preponderance by what the obedience of man increases. 22 - And its decrease by its decrease, and it was said: no, and it was said: no disagreement, thus it has been transmitted. His saying: 'And the increase of faith is given preponderance... etc.': It has preceded that action is from the perfection of faith according to Ahl al-Sunnah, and the author mentioned here that it increases by its increase and decreases by its decrease. So he said: 'And the increase of faith is given preponderance... to the end; meaning: a group of scholars, who are the majority of the Ash'aris, gave preponderance to the statement that faith increases; because there is no meaning to giving preponderance to the increase of faith except giving preponderance to the statement of it. And His saying: 'by what the obedience of man increases' means: due to the increase of man's obedience; so the ba' is causative, and 'ma' is masdariyya, and obedience is: doing what is commanded and refraining from what is forbidden.
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage addresses a major theological issue: whether faith can increase and decrease. The commentator begins by quoting two lines from the matn (the poem) which state that the preponderant view is that faith increases when obedience increases and decreases when obedience decreases, and that some say there is no change, but the transmitted view is that there is no real disagreement (i.e., the difference is terminological). The commentator then explains that, according to Ahl al-Sunnah, actions are part of the perfection of faith. The author of the matn indicates that faith increases with obedience and decreases with sin, and a group of scholars (the majority of Ash'aris) have given preponderance to the view that faith actually increases, because speaking of 'increase of faith' only makes sense if faith can increase. He then analyzes the phrase 'by what the obedience of man increases' (bima tazidu ta'atu al-insani): the letter ba' is sababiyya (causative) and 'ma' is masdariyya (making the phrase a verbal noun), so the meaning is 'due to the increase of man's obedience'. Obedience itself is defined as doing what is commanded and avoiding what is forbidden.

Key Terms
إيمان
زيادة
نقص
طاعة

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some may think that the Ash'ari view reduces faith to mere actions, disregarding belief.
Correction: The Ash'aris maintain that faith includes both belief and actions; actions increase the perfection of faith, not its essence.

Checkpoint

A) By increase of knowledge only.
B) By increase of obedience.
C) By increase of wealth.
D) By acquisition of new beliefs.

Key Takeaway
Faith increases with obedience and decreases with disobedience, according to the majority of Ash'aris.

The Increase and Decrease of Faith (Iman)
Commentator explains increase and decrease of iman based on obedience and divine will.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that according to the majority of Ash'aris, faith (iman) increases with obedience and decreases with disobedience, and that this change is ultimately under Allah's will.

Core Idea
Faith grows with obedience and shrinks with disobedience.

In this passage, the commentator explains the well-known Ash'ari position on the increase and decrease of iman. He clarifies that actions are part of the perfection of faith, so obedience increases faith and disobedience decreases it. However, he also notes that Allah may increase or decrease faith by His sheer will without any cause. This lesson covers the general principle and its grounding in the poem.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim
Read the first lines of the poem and commentary to see that the increase of faith is preponderated by increased obedience. Note that the 'ba' in 'bima tazidu' is causative. Ask: what does this imply about the relationship between faith and actions?
The commentator stresses that this is the view of the majority of Ash'aris.
2
Understand the nuances
Notice that the commentator adds that Allah may increase or decrease faith without any cause. This balances human agency with divine omnipotence. Reflect on why this nuance matters.
The text says: 'وإلا فقد يزيده المولى وينقصه بمحض اختياره من غير سبب يقتضيه'.
3
Apply the principle
Consider how this principle applies to ordinary believers. Then ask: does it apply to prophets and angels? This prepares for the next lesson.
The text transitions to limit the scope: 'فمحله في غير إيمان الأنبياء والملائكة'.

On the disagreement concerning the increase and decrease of faith. 21 - And the increase of faith is preponderated by what? – He said: by the increase of human obedience. 22 - And its decrease by its decrease. And it is said: no, and it is said: no disagreement, thus it has been transmitted. His saying: 'And the increase of faith is preponderated... etc.': It has preceded that action is from the perfection of faith according to Ahl al-Sunnah. And the author mentioned here that it increases with its increase and decreases with its decrease. So he said: (And the increase of faith is preponderated... to the end); meaning: a group of scholars, namely the majority of Ash'aris, preponderated the statement that faith increases; because there is no meaning to preponderating the increase of faith except preponderating the statement of it. And his saying: 'by what the obedience of man increases' means: due to the increase of human obedience, so the 'ba' is causative and 'ma' is masdariyya. And obedience is: doing what is commanded and avoiding what is forbidden. And his saying: 'and its decrease by its decrease' means: and the aforementioned group preponderated the statement of the decrease of faith due to the decrease of obedience. This is with respect to the matter, otherwise Allah may increase it and decrease it by His mere choice without any cause that necessitates it. And if we say that faith increases and decreases, its place is other than the faith of prophets and angels. As for the faith of prophets, it increases because the perfect accepts perfection, and it does not decrease. But it is objected that prophets experience a great unveiling at times, as on the night of the Mi'raj, so faith after it is not in the same station as before. And it is answered that this does not entail a disparity in their faith. Among what indicates that the faith of prophets increases is the statement of our master Ibrahim, peace be upon him and our Prophet: 'But that my heart may be at rest' [Al-Baqarah 260]. And in 'Mafatih al-Khazain al-'Aliyya' by Sayyidi Ali Wafa: the meaning of His saying 'Did you not believe?' is: Is your faith not sufficient? And he said: yes, but that my heart may be at rest from his restlessness at seeing the modality. And the meaning of what is reported in the Sahih: 'We are more deserving of doubt than Ibrahim' is: that if doubt had occurred to him, it would occur to us all the more, considering the state of the ummah, not his state, or considering his state and it is humility. As for the faith of angels, it neither increases nor decreases, as the author mentioned in his 'Kabir' from Ibn al-Qayyim, and this is the well-known view; because their faith is innate by original nature, and what is innate does not vary. And Shaykh 'Abd al-Barr al-Ajhuri mentioned that the faith of angels increases and does not decrease, thus he made it like the faith of prophets, that they advance by [؟].
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the lines of the poem that deal with the increase and decrease of faith (iman). The commentator first explains that according to Ahl al-Sunnah, actions are part of the perfection of faith, so faith increases with increased obedience and decreases with decreased obedience. He clarifies that the majority of Ash'aris preponderate the view that faith increases, and this is what the poem indicates. Then he explains that the increase is caused by increased obedience (the 'ba' is causative, 'ma' is masdariyya). He then notes that while the general rule is that faith increases and decreases with deeds, Allah may also increase or decrease it by His sheer will without any external cause. Next, the commentator specifies that this increase and decrease applies to the faith of ordinary believers, not to prophets or angels. Prophets' faith only increases, because the perfect accepts more perfection, and it never decreases. He addresses an objection: the prophets experience great unveilings that might suggest a change in their faith. The answer is that this does not entail actual variation in the substance of their faith. He supports this with the example of Ibrahim (Abraham) asking to see how Allah revives the dead, which was not due to doubt but to seek tranquility of heart. He explains the hadith 'We are more deserving of doubt than Ibrahim' as either referring to the state of the ummah or as an expression of humility from the Prophet. Finally, he discusses the faith of angels: the well-known view (from Ibn al-Qayyim) is that it neither increases nor decreases because it is innate (jibilli) and what is innate does not vary. However, a minority view (from al-Ajhuri) holds that angels' faith does increase, like that of prophets.

Key Terms

The Faith of Prophets and Angels
Commentator explains faith of prophets and angels with proofs and objections.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that the faith of prophets only increases and never decreases, while the well-known view is that angels' faith is innate and does not change, though some scholars hold it increases.

Core Idea
Prophets' faith only grows; angels' faith is innate and unchanging.

The commentator now specifies that the increase and decrease of faith applies only to ordinary believers. Prophets' faith only increases because the perfect can always receive more perfection. Angels, by contrast, have innate (jibilli) faith that does not vary. This lesson examines the proofs and objections related to these special cases.

Guided Path
1
Understand the rule for prophets
Read the text about prophets: 'فمحله في غير إيمان الأنبياء والملائكة. وأما إيمان الأنبياء فيزيد ; لأن الكامل يقبلُ الكمال، ولا ينقص'. Then consider the objection about the Mi'raj and the answer.
2
Examine the proof from Ibrahim
The commentator uses the story of Ibrahim (AS) asking to see the revival of the dead. It was not due to doubt but to seek tranquility. This supports increase of faith. How does this relate?
The text quotes Quran 2:260 and explains it.
3
Understand the hadith about doubt
The hadith 'We are more deserving of doubt than Ibrahim' is interpreted as either about the ummah or as humility. Why is this important?
It removes any implication of doubt in prophets.
4
Analyze the angels' faith
The well-known view is that angels' faith does not change because it is innate. But al-Ajhuri says it increases. Which one is presented as the main view?
The text says 'وهو المشهور' for the view that it does not increase or decrease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الخلاف في زيادة الإيمان ونقصه
٢١ - وَرُجُحَتْ زيَادَةُ الإِيمَانِ بِمَا تَزِيدُ طَاعَةُ الإِنْسَانِ
٢٢ - وَنَقْصُهُ بِنَقْصِهَا وَقِيلَ: لَا وَقِيلَ: لَا خُلْفَ كَذَا قَدْ نُقِلَا
قوله : (وَرُبِّحَتْ زيَادَةُ الإِيمَانِ ... إلخ) : تقدَّمَ أن العمل من كمال الإيمان عند أهل السنة، وقد ذكر المصنف هنا أنه يزيد بزيادته وينقصُ بنقصه، فقال: (ورجحت زيادة الإيمان ... إلى آخره؛ أي: ورجّحَ جماعةٌ من العلماء وهم جمهورُ الأشاعرة القول بزيادة الإيمان؛ لأنه لا معنى لترجيح زيادة الإيمان إلا ترجيح القول بها . وقوله : بِمَا نَزِيدُ طَاعَةُ الإِنْسَانِ أي : بسبب زيادة طاعة الإنسان، فالباء سببية، و(ما) مصدرية، والطاعةُ : فعلُ المأمور به، واجتناب المنهي عنه
وقوله : (وَنَقْصُهُ بِنَقْصِهَا أي: وربَّحَ الجماعةُ المتقدمون القول بنقص الإيمان سبب نقص الطاعة، وهذا بالنظر للشأن، وإلا فقد يزيده المولى وينقصه بمحض اختياره من غير سبب يقتضيه .
وإذا قلنا بأن الإيمان يزيد وينقصُ، فمحله في غير إيمان الأنبياء والملائكة، وأما إيمانُ الأنبياء فيزيد ؛ لأن الكامل يقبلُ الكمال، ولا ينقص، لكن يرد أن الأنبياء يحصل لهم تجل عظيمٌ في بعض الأحيان كما كان ليلة المعراج، فالإيمان بعده ليس بمنزلته قبله ويجاب بأن هذا لا يستلزم تفاوتاً في إيمانهم. وممَّا يشير إلى أن إيمان الأنبياء يزيد قولُ سيدنا إبراهيم عليه وعلى نبينا الصلاة والسلام: وَلَكِن لِيَطْمَينَ فَلَى [البقرة: ٢٦٠] ، وفي مفاتيح الخزائن العلية» لسيدي علي وفا : معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿أَوَلَمْ تُؤْمِنُ ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٢٦٠] أولم يكفك إيمانُكَ؟ وَقَالَ بَلَى (۱) ولكن لِيَطْمَينَ فَلَى [البَقَرَة: ٢٦٠] من قلقه لرؤية الكيفية) (١) . وَلَكِن ومعنى ما ورد في الصحيح: «نحنُ أحقُّ بالشك من إبراهيم (٢) : أنَّه لو لحقه شكٍّ لطرق لنا بالأولى ؛ نظراً لحال الأمة ، لا لحاله ، أو نظراً لحاله ويكون تواضعاً . وأما إيمان الملائكة فلا يزيد ولا ينقصُ كما ذكرَهُ المصنف في «كبيره» عن ابن القيم، وهو المشهور ؛ لأن إيمانهم جبلي بأصل الطبيعة، وما كان بأصل الطبيعة لا يتفاوت.
وذكر الشيخ عبد البرِّ الأجهوري : أن إيمان الملائكة يزيد ولا ينقصُ، فجعلَهُ كإيمان الأنبياء (٣) أنه يترقون بإشارة
On the disagreement concerning the increase and decrease of faith. 21 - And the increase of faith is preponderated by what? – He said: by the increase of human obedience. 22 - And its decrease by its decrease. And it is said: no, and it is said: no disagreement, thus it has been transmitted. His saying: 'And the increase of faith is preponderated... etc.': It has preceded that action is from the perfection of faith according to Ahl al-Sunnah. And the author mentioned here that it increases with its increase and decreases with its decrease. So he said: (And the increase of faith is preponderated... to the end); meaning: a group of scholars, namely the majority of Ash'aris, preponderated the statement that faith increases; because there is no meaning to preponderating the increase of faith except preponderating the statement of it. And his saying: 'by what the obedience of man increases' means: due to the increase of human obedience, so the 'ba' is causative and 'ma' is masdariyya. And obedience is: doing what is commanded and avoiding what is forbidden. And his saying: 'and its decrease by its decrease' means: and the aforementioned group preponderated the statement of the decrease of faith due to the decrease of obedience. This is with respect to the matter, otherwise Allah may increase it and decrease it by His mere choice without any cause that necessitates it. And if we say that faith increases and decreases, its place is other than the faith of prophets and angels. As for the faith of prophets, it increases because the perfect accepts perfection, and it does not decrease. But it is objected that prophets experience a great unveiling at times, as on the night of the Mi'raj, so faith after it is not in the same station as before. And it is answered that this does not entail a disparity in their faith. Among what indicates that the faith of prophets increases is the statement of our master Ibrahim, peace be upon him and our Prophet: 'But that my heart may be at rest' [Al-Baqarah 260]. And in 'Mafatih al-Khazain al-'Aliyya' by Sayyidi Ali Wafa: the meaning of His saying 'Did you not believe?' is: Is your faith not sufficient? And he said: yes, but that my heart may be at rest from his restlessness at seeing the modality. And the meaning of what is reported in the Sahih: 'We are more deserving of doubt than Ibrahim' is: that if doubt had occurred to him, it would occur to us all the more, considering the state of the ummah, not his state, or considering his state and it is humility. As for the faith of angels, it neither increases nor decreases, as the author mentioned in his 'Kabir' from Ibn al-Qayyim, and this is the well-known view; because their faith is innate by original nature, and what is innate does not vary. And Shaykh 'Abd al-Barr al-Ajhuri mentioned that the faith of angels increases and does not decrease, thus he made it like the faith of prophets, that they advance by [؟].
Source pages p. 136

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the lines of the poem that deal with the increase and decrease of faith (iman). The commentator first explains that according to Ahl al-Sunnah, actions are part of the perfection of faith, so faith increases with increased obedience and decreases with decreased obedience. He clarifies that the majority of Ash'aris preponderate the view that faith increases, and this is what the poem indicates. Then he explains that the increase is caused by increased obedience (the 'ba' is causative, 'ma' is masdariyya). He then notes that while the general rule is that faith increases and decreases with deeds, Allah may also increase or decrease it by His sheer will without any external cause. Next, the commentator specifies that this increase and decrease applies to the faith of ordinary believers, not to prophets or angels. Prophets' faith only increases, because the perfect accepts more perfection, and it never decreases. He addresses an objection: the prophets experience great unveilings that might suggest a change in their faith. The answer is that this does not entail actual variation in the substance of their faith. He supports this with the example of Ibrahim (Abraham) asking to see how Allah revives the dead, which was not due to doubt but to seek tranquility of heart. He explains the hadith 'We are more deserving of doubt than Ibrahim' as either referring to the state of the ummah or as an expression of humility from the Prophet. Finally, he discusses the faith of angels: the well-known view (from Ibn al-Qayyim) is that it neither increases nor decreases because it is innate (jibilli) and what is innate does not vary. However, a minority view (from al-Ajhuri) holds that angels' faith does increase, like that of prophets.

ملائكة
جبلي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Prophets' faith can decrease because they experience varying states of closeness to Allah.
Correction: The commentator argues that such variations do not entail disparity in the substance of their faith; their faith only increases.

Checkpoint
According to the well-known view mentioned in this passage, what is the nature of the faith of angels?
A) It increases and decreases like that of ordinary believers.
B) It increases but does not decrease.
C) It neither increases nor decreases because it is innate.
D) It decreases but does not increase.

Key Takeaway
Prophets' faith only increases; angels' faith is innate and does not change according to the well-known view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Since prophets' faith only increases, and yours often wavers, what does that reveal about your relationship with your Lord? Will you let this lesson convict you to pray daily for an increase in iman, starting tonight?
?
Angels have innate unchanging faith, but you are human with fluctuating faith. Where have you accepted a decrease in your worship as 'just the way it is'? What specific step can you take this week to push against that acceptance and seek increase?
?
Ibrahim—a prophet—still asked for his heart to be at rest. When did you last genuinely cry out to Allah for tranquility in your faith, not just repeat empty words? Write down a dua you will make after this reflection.

Classification of Iman's Increase and Decrease
The author classifies iman into three categories regarding increase and decrease.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of iman regarding increase and decrease, and how the iman of prophets, angels, and the community differ.

Core Idea
Iman varies in its capacity for increase and decrease across different groups.

This passage from Tuhfat al-Murid presents a detailed classification of iman based on whether it can increase and/or decrease. The author, after establishing that iman does increase and decrease for the general community, examines the special cases of prophets and angels, leading to a three-part division that also accounts for the state of sinners.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to get an overview of the classification.
Pay attention to the structure: the author first discusses prophets, then angels, then summarizes.
2
Identify the three categories
At the end of the passage, the author lists three categories: iman that increases and decreases, iman that neither increases nor decreases, and iman that increases but does not decrease. Notice which group each refers to.
The fourth category (sinners) is added by some and not always included.
3
Examine the evidence for prophets
The author supports the increase of prophets' iman with the story of Ibrahim (Quran 2:260) and the hadith about doubt. Understand how these are interpreted to avoid implying doubt or deficiency.
Notice the objection and answer about the Night of Ascension.
4
Understand the angelic iman
The author presents two views on angels' iman: the well-known view that it is static (neither increases nor decreases) because it is innate, and a minority view that it increases like prophets.
The innate nature (jibilli) is key to the majority position.
5
Reflect on the fourth category
Some scholars add a fourth category for sinners: iman that decreases but does not increase. Consider how this fits with the other categories and the overall classification.
This category is not always accepted.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا قلنا بأن الإيمان يزيد وينقصُ، فمحله في غير إيمان الأنبياء والملائكة، وأما إيمانُ الأنبياء فيزيد ؛ لأن الكامل يقبلُ الكمال، ولا ينقص، لكن يرد أن الأنبياء يحصل لهم تجل عظيمٌ في بعض الأحيان كما كان ليلة المعراج، فالإيمان بعده ليس بمنزلته قبله ويجاب بأن هذا لا يستلزم تفاوتاً في إيمانهم. وممَّا يشير إلى أن إيمان الأنبياء يزيد قولُ سيدنا إبراهيم عليه وعلى نبينا الصلاة والسلام: وَلَكِن لِيَطْمَينَ فَلَى [البقرة: ٢٦٠]، وفي مفاتيح الخزائن العلية» لسيدي علي وفا : معنى قوله تعالى: ﴿أَوَلَمْ تُؤْمِنُ ﴾ [البَقَرَة : ٢٦٠] أولم يكفك إيمانُكَ؟ وَقَالَ بَلَى (۱) ولكن لِيَطْمَينَ فَلَى [البَقَرَة: ٢٦٠] من قلقه لرؤية الكيفية) (١) . وَلَكِن ومعنى ما ورد في الصحيح: «نحنُ أحقُّ بالشك من إبراهيم (٢) : أنَّه لو لحقه شكٍّ لطرق لنا بالأولى ؛ نظراً لحال الأمة ، لا لحاله ، أو نظراً لحاله ويكون تواضعاً . وأما إيمان الملائكة فلا يزيد ولا ينقصُ كما ذكرَهُ المصنف في «كبيره» عن ابن القيم، وهو المشهور ؛ لأن إيمانهم جبلي بأصل الطبيعة، وما كان بأصل الطبيعة لا يتفاوت. وذكر الشيخ عبد البرِّ الأجهوري : أن إيمان الملائكة يزيد ولا ينقصُ، فجعلَهُ كإيمان الأنبياء. فتلخص أن الأقسام ثلاثة : يزيد وينقصُ : وهو إيمانُ الأمة إنساً وجنا . ولا يزيد ولا ينقصُ : وهو إيمانُ الملائكة على المشهور. ويزيدُ ولا ينقصُ : وهو إيمانُ الأنبياء. وزاد بعضُهم قسماً رابعاً : وهو الذي ينقصُ ولا يزيد، وهو إيمان الفساق.
And if we say that iman increases and decreases, then its place is other than the iman of the prophets and angels. As for the iman of the prophets, it increases, because the perfect accepts perfection and does not decrease. But it is objected that the prophets experience a great manifestation at times, as on the Night of Ascension, so iman after it is not like it before. And it is answered that this does not entail variation in their iman. Among what indicates that the iman of the prophets increases is the saying of our master Ibrahim, peace be upon him and upon our Prophet: 'But that my heart may be at rest' [al-Baqara 2:260]. And in Mafatih al-Khaza'in al-'Aliyya by Sayyidi 'Ali Wafa: the meaning of His saying 'Have you not believed?' [al-Baqara 2:260] is 'Has not your iman sufficed you?' And he said 'Yes, but that my heart may be at rest' [al-Baqara 2:260] due to his restlessness at seeing the 'how'. And the meaning of what is reported in the Sahih: 'We are more deserving of doubt than Ibrahim' is that if doubt had occurred to him, it would have occurred to us all the more, considering the state of the community, not his state, or considering his state and it would be humility. As for the iman of the angels, it does not increase or decrease, as the author mentioned in his 'Kabir' from Ibn al-Qayyim, and it is the well-known view, because their iman is innate by the original nature, and what is by the original nature does not vary. And Shaykh 'Abd al-Barr al-Ujhuri mentioned that the iman of the angels increases and does not decrease, and he made it like the iman of the prophets. So it is summarized that the divisions are three: (1) It increases and decreases: that is the iman of the community, humans and jinn. (2) It neither increases nor decreases: that is the iman of the angels on the well-known view. (3) It increases but does not decrease: that is the iman of the prophets. And some added a fourth division: that which decreases but does not increase, and that is the iman of the sinners.
Source pages p. 137

Commentary
This passage is a classification of iman (faith) regarding increase and decrease. The author begins by stating that when we say iman increases and decreases, this applies to other than the prophets and angels. He then explains the case of the prophets: their iman only increases because the perfect is capable of receiving more perfection, but it does not decrease. An objection is raised that prophets experience great divine manifestations (like the Night of Ascension), which would imply variation. The answer is that this does not entail a difference in the essence of their iman. To support the increase of prophetic iman, the author cites Prophet Ibrahim's request to see how God revives the dead (Quran 2:260). He interprets it as a desire for tranquility regarding the 'how', not doubt. The hadith 'We are more deserving of doubt than Ibrahim' is explained as either considering the community's fragility or as humility from Ibrahim. Then the author discusses angels: their iman does not increase or decrease on the well-known view, because it is innate (jibilli) and by original nature, which does not vary. However, a minority view (Shaykh al-Ujhuri) holds that it increases like prophets. Finally, the author summarizes three divisions: iman that increases and decreases (community of humans and jinn), iman that neither increases nor decreases (angels, on the well-known view), and iman that increases but does not decrease (prophets). Some add a fourth: iman that decreases but does not increase (sinners). This classification establishes that iman is not a monolithic entity but varies across different categories of believers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: All iman is uniform and cannot change.
Correction: This passage shows that iman varies by category: prophets' iman only increases, angels' iman is static (on the well-known view), and the community's iman fluctuates.

Checkpoint

A) Prophets
B) Angels on the well-known view
C) Sinners
D) The community of humans and jinn

Key Takeaway
Iman is not a monolithic entity; it behaves differently for prophets, angels, and ordinary believers.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You now know that your iman can both increase and decrease. Look at your own heart: in the past week, have you felt your faith rising or falling? Which specific actions or neglect caused that change? Commit to one concrete action today that will increase your iman.
?
Prophets' iman only increases and never decreases. Compare your own spiritual trajectory: is your faith consistently moving upward, or do you find yourself in a cycle of gain and loss? What is one area where you have allowed spiritual decline, and what will you do this week to reverse it?
?
Angels have innate unchanging faith, but you must work for yours. Does that responsibility weigh on you, or does it motivate you? What is one way you have taken your iman for granted? Repent and set a daily practice to actively seek increase starting now.

Transmitted Proofs for Increase and Decrease of Iman
The author cites scriptural texts for increase and addresses an objection about decrease with a supplementary premise.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the transmitted proofs (Quran and hadith) demonstrate that iman increases and decreases, and how the supplementary premise addresses the objection regarding the prophets' iman.

Core Idea
Iman increases and decreases; supplementary premise proves decrease, except for prophets due to infallibility.

The author now presents the scriptural evidence for the increase of iman, then addresses a potential gap: the texts only mention increase. A logical supplement is introduced to infer decrease, but this raises an objection regarding prophets. Let's examine how he resolves this.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the scriptural proofs
Read the Arabic passage and its translation carefully. Note the Quranic verses and hadiths cited. They all speak about iman increasing, but do they mention decrease?
Observe that the first hadith (Ibn 'Umar) explicitly mentions both increase and decrease.
2
Notice the gap: only increase is explicit
The author points out that the verses and the second hadith (Abu Bakr) only indicate increase, not decrease. This is a key observation – the transmitted proofs alone do not directly prove decrease.
3
Understand the supplementary premise
To prove decrease, the author adds a logical premise: 'Everything that accepts increase accepts decrease.' This is a rational principle. Understand why this completes the proof.
This premise is not from scripture but from reason.
4
Consider the objection and answer
An objection is raised: if everything that increases also decreases, then prophets' iman could decrease. How does the author answer? He says prophets are excluded because of their constant infallibility that prevents decrease.
Think about why infallibility ('isma) is a valid exception.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النقليَّةُ : فهي النصوص الكثيرة الواردة في هذا المعنى ؛ كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ وَايَتُهُ زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَانًا ﴾ [الأنفال : ٢] وكقوله : لِيَزْدَادُوا إِيمَنًا مَعَ إِيمَنِهِمْ ﴾ [الفتح: ، وقوله: ﴿وَيَزْدَادَ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إيتا) [المدثر: ۳۱]، وقوله: ﴿ فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا فَزَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَنان [ التوبة : ١٢٤] . وكقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لابنِ عمرَ لمَّا سأله : الإيمان يزيد وينقص؟ قال : «نعم، يزيد حتى يُدخل صاحبَهُ الجنةَ ، وينقصُ حتى يُدخل صاحبَه الناره (۱). وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : لو وزن إيمان أبي بكر بإيمان هذهِ الأمَّةِ، لرجح به (۲)، وهذا الحديث - كالآيات السابقة - لا يدلُّ على أنه ينقصُ، فيضم إلى ذلك : وكلُّ ما يقبلُ الزيادةَ يقبلُ النقص، فيتمُّ الدليلُ، وأُوردَ على هذه الضميمةِ إيمانُ الأنبياء، وأجيب بأنه خرج لوجوب العصمة الدائمة المانعة من نقصه.
As for the transmitted proof, it is the abundant texts that have come concerning this meaning, such as His saying, the Most High: 'And when His verses are recited to them, they increase them in iman' [al-Anfal 8:2], and His saying: 'That they may increase iman along with their iman' [al-Fath 48:4], and His saying: 'And may increase those who believe in iman' [al-Muddaththir 74:31], and His saying: 'As for those who believe, it increased them in iman' [al-Tawba 9:124]. And like his saying, peace be upon him, to Ibn 'Umar when he asked: 'Does iman increase and decrease?' He said: 'Yes, it increases until it enters its possessor into Paradise, and decreases until it enters its possessor into Hellfire.' And his saying, peace be upon him: 'If the iman of Abu Bakr were weighed against the iman of this community, it would outweigh it.' And this hadith — like the previous verses — does not indicate that it decreases. So one adds to that: 'Everything that accepts increase accepts decrease.' Thus the proof is complete. And an objection was raised against this supplement concerning the iman of the prophets, and it was answered that it is excluded due to the necessity of constant infallibility that prevents its decrease.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted proofs (naqliyya) for the increase and decrease of iman, and then addresses an objection regarding the establishment of decrease. First, the author lists Quranic verses: Surah al-Anfal 8:2, al-Fath 48:4 (incomplete), al-Muddaththir 74:31, and al-Tawba 9:124, all of which speak of iman increasing. Then he cites a hadith where the Prophet answered Ibn 'Umar's question about iman increasing and decreasing, affirming both. Another hadith states that Abu Bakr's iman would outweigh that of the entire community. However, the author notes that these texts (verses and the Abu Bakr hadith) only indicate increase, not decrease. Therefore, a supplementary premise is added: 'Everything that accepts increase accepts decrease.' This completes the proof for both increase and decrease. An objection is then raised: if this supplement applies universally, then it would also apply to the prophets' iman, implying their iman could decrease, which is contrary to the established view that it only increases. The answer is that the iman of prophets is excluded from this rule because of their constant infallibility ('isma), which prevents any decrease. Thus the proof stands for all others, and the exception is justified by a special quality of prophethood.

نصوص
زيادة
نقص
ضميمة
عصمة
الأنبياء

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The scriptural texts alone directly prove both increase and decrease of iman.
Correction: The texts explicitly only mention increase; decrease is proven via a logical supplementary premise.

Checkpoint
Why is the iman of prophets excluded from the supplementary premise 'whatever accepts increase accepts decrease'?
A) Because prophets' iman is innate

D) Because the community agreed

Key Takeaway

The Prophet said iman can decrease until it leads a person to Hellfire. Is there any sin in your life that you have been neglecting to repent from, allowing it to slowly erode your faith? Will you turn back to Allah now?
?
The supplementary premise teaches that what can increase can also decrease. Are you taking your iman for granted, assuming it will always stay strong without effort? What will you do this week to actively guard against a decrease?

The Three Divisions of Faith
The author enumerates three (or four) divisions of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three categories of faith with respect to increase and decrease as outlined by the author.

Core Idea
Faith varies: it can increase, decrease, or remain constant depending on the believer.

This passage summarizes a key classification in Islamic theology: the different ways faith can change. The author presents three main categories—faith that increases and decreases (the general community), faith that is constant (angels), and faith that only increases (prophets). Some scholars also add a fourth category for sinners. Understanding these divisions helps clarify the nature of faith in Sunni thought.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the classification.
Notice the key terms like إيمان, زيادة, نقص.
2
Identify the three categories
Find the three main divisions and their descriptions: general community (humans and jinn), angels, and prophets.
3
Consider the fourth division
Note that some scholars added a fourth category for sinners. Think about its implications.
This addition shows scholarly difference over the classification.
4
Reflect on the significance
Ask why this classification matters for understanding faith. How does it relate to the concept of faith being variable?
This connects to debates on whether faith is created or uncreated, etc.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فتلخص أن الأقسام ثلاثة : يزيد وينقصُ : وهو إيمانُ الأمة إنساً وجنا . ولا يزيد ولا ينقصُ : وهو إيمانُ الملائكة على المشهور. ويزيدُ ولا ينقصُ : وهو إيمانُ الأنبياء. وزاد بعضُهم قسماً رابعاً : وهو الذي ينقصُ ولا يزيد، وهو إيمان الفساق.
It is concluded that the divisions are three: one that increases and decreases: that is the faith of the community, humans and jinn. One that neither increases nor decreases: that is the faith of the angels according to the well-known view. One that increases but does not decrease: that is the faith of the prophets. And some added a fourth division: one that decreases but does not increase, and that is the faith of the sinners.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage is a classification of different levels of faith in relation to increase and decrease. The author states that the divisions are three. First, the faith of the general community (both humans and jinn) which increases and decreases. Second, the faith of the angels which, according to the well-known view, neither increases nor decreases. Third, the faith of the prophets, which increases but does not decrease. Then he notes that some scholars added a fourth division: the faith of sinners, which decreases but does not increase. This classification sets the stage for the discussion on the nature of faith and its variability.

Correction: This classification shows that faith can vary in its potential for increase and decrease depending on the category of believer.

Key Takeaway

The Transmitted Proofs for the Increase of Faith
The author cites Qur'anic verses and hadiths demonstrating the increase of faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scriptural evidence for the increase of faith and how the potential objection regarding prophets' faith is resolved.

Core Idea
The Qur'an and Sunnah explicitly affirm that faith increases, and even a potential counterexample proves the rule.

Having established the rational possibility of faith increasing, the author now turns to the transmitted proofs. These are the conclusive texts from the Qur'an and Sunnah that explicitly mention the increase of faith. Through these verses and hadiths, and by addressing a subtle objection, the doctrine of variable faith is firmly grounded in revelation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the Qur'anic verses
Read the Arabic passage and translation. Note the four verses cited: Q8:2, Q48:4, Q74:31, Q9:124. Observe that each verse explicitly mentions increase in faith.
These verses are clear evidence for the increase of faith.
2
Examine the hadiths
The first hadith from Ibn ‘Umar states that faith increases and decreases. The second hadith about Abu Bakr only mentions increase. Notice that the author points out that the second hadith alone does not prove decrease.
The Ibn ‘Umar hadith is explicit about both increase and decrease.
3
Understand the supplement
The author adds a general principle: 'everything that admits of increase admits of decrease.' This completes the proof from the Abu Bakr hadith. Consider why this principle is reasonable.
This principle is based on logical consistency.
4
Consider the objection and answer
An objector points out that prophets' faith increases but does not decrease. The author responds that prophets are protected by perpetual infallibility (ʿiṣma), which prevents decrease. Reflect on how this exception actually confirms the rule.
The exception is due to a special protection, not a flaw in the general principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما النقليَّةُ : فهي النصوص الكثيرة الواردة في هذا المعنى ؛ كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَإِذَا تُلِيَتْ عَلَيْهِمْ وَايَتُهُ زَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَانًا ﴾ [الأنفال : ٢] وكقوله : لِيَزْدَادُوا إِيمَنًا مَعَ إِيمَنِهِمْ ﴾ [الفتح: ، وقوله: ﴿وَيَزْدَادَ الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا إيتا) [المدثر: ۳۱]، وقوله: ﴿ فَأَمَّا الَّذِينَ ءَامَنُوا فَزَادَتْهُمْ إِيمَنان [ التوبة : ١٢٤] . وكقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام لابنِ عمرَ لمَّا سأله : الإيمان يزيد وينقص؟ قال : «نعم، يزيد حتى يُدخل صاحبَهُ الجنةَ ، وينقصُ حتى يُدخل صاحبَه الناره» (۱). وقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام : لو وزن إيمان أبي بكر بإيمان هذهِ الأمَّةِ، لرجح به (۲)، وهذا الحديث - كالآيات السابقة - لا يدلُّ على أنه ينقصُ، فيضم إلى ذلك : وكلُّ ما يقبلُ الزيادةَ يقبلُ النقص، فيتمُّ الدليلُ، وأُوردَ على هذه الضميمةِ إيمانُ الأنبياء، وأجيب بأنه خرج لوجوب العصمة الدائمة المانعة من نقصه.
As for the transmitted proof: it consists of the numerous texts reported on this meaning, such as His saying the Exalted: 'And when His verses are recited to them, they increase them in faith' (Q8:2), and His saying: 'that they may increase in faith along with their faith' (Q48:4), and His saying: 'and it (the Qur'an) increases those who believe in faith' (Q74:31), and His saying: 'but as for those who believe, it increases them in faith' (Q9:124). And such as his saying, peace and blessings upon him, to Ibn ‘Umar when he asked: 'Does faith increase and decrease?' He said: 'Yes, it increases until it enters its possessor into Paradise, and decreases until it enters its possessor into Hellfire.' And his saying, peace and blessings upon him: 'If the faith of Abu Bakr were weighed against the faith of this ummah, it would outweigh it.' And this hadith—like the previous verses—does not prove that it decreases, so it is supplemented by [the premise]: everything that admits of increase admits of decrease. Thus the proof is completed. And an objection was raised regarding this supplement: the faith of the prophets (since it increases but does not decrease). And it was answered that it is excluded due to the necessity of perpetual infallibility which prevents its decrease.
Source pages p. 138

Commentary
This passage presents the transmitted (naqli) proofs for the increase of faith. It cites four Qur'anic verses that explicitly mention faith increasing. Then it cites two hadiths: one with Ibn Umar where the Prophet states faith increases and decreases, and another where the Prophet says Abu Bakr's faith outweighs the entire ummah's faith. The author notes that the hadith about Abu Bakr does not explicitly mention decrease, but it is supplemented by the general principle that whatever can increase can also decrease. However, an objection arises: the faith of prophets increases but does not decrease. The response is that prophets have perpetual infallibility (ʿiṣma) that prevents their faith from decreasing. The passage thus strengthens the case for the variability of faith using authoritative texts and resolves a potential counterexample.

Correction: The author clarifies that this hadith only mentions increase; the proof for decrease comes only when combined with the logical principle that increase implies decrease.

Key Takeaway

Faith Fixed According to Abu Hanifa
The author presents the position that faith is fixed and its defense.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand Imam Abu Hanifa's argument that faith does not increase or decrease, and how his followers reinterpret scriptural evidence to support this view.

Core Idea
Faith is a fixed ultimate affirmation; variation points to beliefs or deeds, not faith itself.

This lesson explores a major theological debate: can faith increase or decrease? Imam Abu Hanifa and his school argue that faith is an unwavering affirmation of the heart, which by its very nature cannot admit degrees. But how do they reconcile this with verses and hadith that seem to describe increase in faith? The passage presents their reasoning and their interpretive strategy.

Guided Path
1
Understand the definition of faith
Read how Abu Hanifa defines faith as affirmation (taṣdīq) reaching the ultimate level of certainty (jazm) and submission (idh‘ān). Notice why this ultimate level has no degrees.
This is the core of the argument.
2
Grasp the objection
The text presents an objection: affirmation itself appears to have degrees, from blind following to deep spiritual absorption. Identify the five levels mentioned.
3
See how the defense reinterprets verses
The followers of Abu Hanifa interpret verses about increase as referring to the object of faith (mu’man bihi), not the faith itself. The Companions believed new revelations as they came.
4
See how the defense reinterprets hadiths
They interpret hadiths about increase and decrease as referring to actions ('a'māl), not the essence of faith (taṣdīq). This preserves the fixed nature of faith.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَقِيلَ: (لا) أي : وقال جماعة أعظمُهم الإمام أبو حنيفة ـ وهو النعمان بن ثابت - : لا يزيد ولا ينقصُ ؛ لأنه اسم للتصديق البالغ نهاية الجزم والإذعان، وهذا لا يتصور فيه ما ذُكرَ ؛ لأن تلك النهاية لا مراتب لها . وبحث فيه بأن التصديق مراتب، فإن تصديق المقلّد ليس كتصديق العارف بالدليل، وهو ليس كتصديق المراقب، وهو ليس كتصديق المشاهد، وهو ليس كتصديق المستغرقِ الذي لا يُشاهدُ إلا الله وتأوَّلَ هؤلاء الجماعةُ الآيات السابقة بأن الزيادة إنما هي في المؤمَنِ به؛ لأن الصحابة كانوا آمنوا بما أنزل على النبي الا الله وكانَتِ الشريعة لم تتم، وكانت الأحكام تنزلُ شيئاً فشيئاً، فكانوا يؤمنون بكل ما يتجدد وتأوَّلوا الأحاديث السابقة بأن الزيادة والنقص يرجعُ كلَّ منهما إلى الأعمال لا التصديق.
His saying: 'And it is said: (No)' means: And a group, the greatest of whom is Imam Abu Hanifa—he is al-Nu‘man ibn Thabit—said: It (faith) neither increases nor decreases, because it is a name for affirmation (taṣdīq) reaching the ultimate level of certainty and submission, and what was mentioned (increase and decrease) cannot be conceived in it, because that ultimate level has no degrees. And an objection was raised against this: that affirmation has degrees, for the affirmation of a blind follower (muqallid) is not like the affirmation of one who knows by proof, and it is not like the affirmation of the contemplative (murāqib), and it is not like the affirmation of the witness (mushāhid), and it is not like the affirmation of the absorbed one who witnesses only God. And this group interpreted the previous verses as meaning that the increase is only in what is believed (al-mu’man bihi), because the Companions believed what was revealed to the Prophet, but the law had not yet been completed, and rulings were revealed little by little, so they believed each new thing as it came. And they interpreted the previous hadiths as meaning that both increase and decrease refer to actions, not to affirmation.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents the view that faith does not increase or decrease, attributed primarily to Imam Abu Hanifa. The argument is that faith is by definition taṣdīq (affirmation) that has reached the ultimate degree of certainty (jazm) and submission (idh‘ān). Such a pinnacle has no gradations, so increase or decrease is impossible. However, an objection (baḥth) is raised: taṣdīq itself can be of varying levels. The objector lists five levels: the blind follower, the knower of proofs, the contemplative, the witness, and the one completely absorbed in God. To defend their view, this group (followers of Abu Hanifa) interpret the scriptural proofs that seem to show increase. They say the increase refers to the object of faith (mu’man bihi), not the faith itself: the early Muslims kept believing in new revelations as they came. And they interpret the hadiths about increase and decrease as referring to deeds, not to the essence of faith (taṣdīq). Thus they harmonize their position with the revealed texts.

Key Terms

جزم
إذعان
تقليد
مراقب

مستغرق
تأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Faith can increase or decrease in the same way deeds do.
Correction: Abu Hanifa argues that faith as ultimate affirmation is fixed; variations are in beliefs about new content or in actions, not in the essence of faith.

Checkpoint
How do followers of Abu Hanifa interpret verses that mention increase in faith?
A) They say the increase is in the affirmation itself
B) They say the increase is in the object of faith (what is believed)
C) They reject the authenticity of those verses
D) They say the increase is in the number of believers

Key Takeaway
Imam Abu Hanifa maintained that faith is a fixed, ultimate affirmation; Scriptural references to increase are about what is believed or about actions, not the essence of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?

?
Abu Hanifa teaches that increase in faith is actually increase in what you believe—new truths you accept. When was the last time you accepted a truth from Allah that actually transformed your life? If it's been a while, what are you afraid of losing?

Faith and Disbelief

Al-Khattabi's Tripartite Faith and the Negation
Al-Khattabi's tripartite analysis and the alternative parsing of the negation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Khattabi's division of faith into three components and how it relates to the issue of increase and decrease.

Core Idea
Faith's increase is certain; its decrease must be understood through its components.

The author explores an alternative reading of the poem's negation, suggesting it applies only to decrease. This leads to al-Khattabi's detailed analysis, where faith is divided into speech, action, and belief—each with a different rule of increase and decrease.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analysis. Then read the translation. Notice how the author suggests an alternative interpretation.
Pay attention to the phrase 'ويحتمل أن يكون النفي'.
2
Identify al-Khattabi's three components
Find the three components of faith mentioned by al-Khattabi: qawl, amal, i'tiqad. Note the property of each regarding increase and decrease.
Al-Khattabi says: 'قول لا يزيد ولا ينقص، وعمل يزيد وينقص، واعتقاد يزيد ولا ينقص'.
3
Reflect on the nuance
Consider why al-Khattabi's analysis is important. It shows faith is not monolithic; different aspects have different rules.
This helps reconcile differing views on increase and decrease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحتمل أن يكون النفي في كلام المصنف راجعاً إلى أقرب مذكور، وهو قوله : (ونقصه بنقصها، فكأنه قال :وقيل : لا ينقص فيكون مراده بهذا القيل أن الإيمان يزيد ولا ينقصُ، كما ذهب إليه الخطابي ؛ حيث قال: (الإيمانُ الكامل ثلاثة أمور: قول وهو لا يزيد ولا ينقصُ، وعمل وهو يزيد وينقصُ، واعتقاد وهو يزيد ولا ينقصُ، فإن نقص ذهب) . قوله : (وَقِيلَ: لَا خُلْفَ) استئناف لا عطف كما قاله المصنف، ويحتمل أن يكون معطوفاً على مقدر مفهوم من السياق، والتقديرُ : قد اشتهر أن بين القوم خلافاً حقيقيًّا ، وقيل : (لا خلفٌ) أي : وقال جماعةٌ منهم الفخر الرازي وإمام الحرمين: ليس الخلاف بين الفريقين حقيقيًّا، بل لفظيًّا ، ونفي الخلاف على الإطلاق لا يصح،
And it is possible that the negation in the author's speech refers to the nearest mentioned, namely his saying: 'and its decrease by its decrease', as if he said: 'and it is said: it does not decrease'. So his intention with this 'qīl' is that faith increases but does not decrease, as al-Khattabi held, for he said: 'Perfect faith consists of three things: speech which neither increases nor decreases, action which increases and decreases, and belief which increases but does not decrease; if it decreases, it is gone.' His saying: 'And it is said: no disagreement' is a new beginning, not conjoined, as the author stated, and it is possible that it is conjoined to an understood [phrase] from the context, the estimate being: 'It is well-known that there is real disagreement among the people, and it is said: no disagreement' meaning: a group, among them Fakhr al-Razi and Imam al-Haramayn, said: The disagreement between the two parties is not real, but verbal. And the absolute denial of disagreement is not correct.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage contains two further points. First, an alternative interpretation of the phrase in the poem: the negation (lā) may actually refer to decrease only, meaning that faith increases but does not decrease. This is the view of al-Khattabi, who divides faith into three components: speech (qawl) – immutable; action (ʿamal) – varies; and belief (iʿtiqād) – increases but cannot decrease without vanishing. Second, the author addresses the phrase 'wa qīla: lā khulf' (and it is said: no disagreement). He explains that it could be construed as a new independent statement, or as a continuation of a suppressed premise: 'It is well-known that there is real disagreement, but it is said there is no real disagreement.' He attributes the view that the dispute is merely verbal (lafẓī) to Fakhr al-Razi and Imam al-Haramayn. However, he warns that a blanket denial of disagreement is not correct, implying that some aspects of the dispute are substantive.

Key Terms
خطابي
قول
عمل
اعتقاد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think faith can neither increase nor decrease at all.
Correction: Al-Khattabi shows that only the verbal profession is fixed; belief and action can increase, and belief cannot decrease without losing faith.

Checkpoint
According to al-Khattabi, which component of faith neither increases nor decreases?
A) Speech (qawl)
B) Action (amal)
C) Belief (i'tiqad)
D) All three

Key Takeaway
Al-Khattabi's analysis resolves the issue by distinguishing the immutable profession from the dynamic components of faith.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You have learned that belief increases but cannot decrease without vanishing. Examine your own heart: is there any area of your belief—about Allah, His attributes, or the Hereafter—that feels weaker today than before? What does this passage compel you to do about it?
?
Al-Khattabi said action is part of perfect faith and it both increases and decreases. Reflect on your actions over the past week: did your prayers, charity, or other deeds increase or decrease? What one action will you commit to today to ensure your faith is rising, not falling?
?
The core utterance of faith (shahada) is fixed, but belief and action fluctuate. Have you ever recited the shahada mechanically while your heart was distant? What would it take for your belief to truly increase so that your tongue and heart align?

The Verbal Nature of the Dispute
The assertion that the dispute is merely verbal and the author's qualification.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that some scholars consider the disagreement over faith's increase and decrease to be merely verbal, and why the author cautions against a blanket denial of disagreement.

Core Idea
Not all disagreement is real; some is just words.

The author now addresses the phrase 'and it is said: no disagreement'. He clarifies that this claim is attributed to notable scholars like Fakhr al-Razi and Imam al-Haramayn, who argued the dispute over increase and decrease is merely verbal. However, the author immediately warns that denying all disagreement is incorrect.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the syntactic analysis of the phrase 'wa qīla: lā khulf'.
The author explains two possible constructions.
2
Identify the scholars mentioned
Find the names Fakhr al-Razi and Imam al-Haramayn. Understand their position: the dispute is lafzī (verbal).
This is a significant claim.
3
Understand the author's qualification
The author says 'Nafy al-khilāf ʿalā al-iṭlāq lā yaṣiḥḥ' (the absolute denial of disagreement is not correct). Reflect on why he adds this.
This shows the author does not fully endorse the verbal view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويحتمل أن يكون النفي في كلام المصنف راجعاً إلى أقرب مذكور، وهو قوله : (ونقصه بنقصها، فكأنه قال :وقيل : لا ينقص فيكون مراده بهذا القيل أن الإيمان يزيد ولا ينقصُ، كما ذهب إليه الخطابي ؛ حيث قال: (الإيمانُ الكامل ثلاثة أمور: قول وهو لا يزيد ولا ينقصُ، وعمل وهو يزيد وينقصُ، واعتقاد وهو يزيد ولا ينقصُ، فإن نقص ذهب) . قوله : (وَقِيلَ: لَا خُلْفَ) استئناف لا عطف كما قاله المصنف، ويحتمل أن يكون معطوفاً على مقدر مفهوم من السياق، والتقديرُ : قد اشتهر أن بين القوم خلافاً حقيقيًّا ، وقيل : (لا خلفٌ) أي : وقال جماعةٌ منهم الفخر الرازي وإمام الحرمين: ليس الخلاف بين الفريقين حقيقيًّا، بل لفظيًّا ، ونفي الخلاف على الإطلاق لا يصح،
And it is possible that the negation in the author's speech refers to the nearest mentioned, namely his saying: 'and its decrease by its decrease', as if he said: 'and it is said: it does not decrease'. So his intention with this 'qīl' is that faith increases but does not decrease, as al-Khattabi held, for he said: 'Perfect faith consists of three things: speech which neither increases nor decreases, action which increases and decreases, and belief which increases but does not decrease; if it decreases, it is gone.' His saying: 'And it is said: no disagreement' is a new beginning, not conjoined, as the author stated, and it is possible that it is conjoined to an understood [phrase] from the context, the estimate being: 'It is well-known that there is real disagreement among the people, and it is said: no disagreement' meaning: a group, among them Fakhr al-Razi and Imam al-Haramayn, said: The disagreement between the two parties is not real, but verbal. And the absolute denial of disagreement is not correct.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage contains two further points. First, an alternative interpretation of the phrase in the poem: the negation (lā) may actually refer to decrease only, meaning that faith increases but does not decrease. This is the view of al-Khattabi, who divides faith into three components: speech (qawl) – immutable; action (ʿamal) – varies; and belief (iʿtiqād) – increases but cannot decrease without vanishing. Second, the author addresses the phrase 'wa qīla: lā khulf' (and it is said: no disagreement). He explains that it could be construed as a new independent statement, or as a continuation of a suppressed premise: 'It is well-known that there is real disagreement, but it is said there is no real disagreement.' He attributes the view that the dispute is merely verbal (lafẓī) to Fakhr al-Razi and Imam al-Haramayn. However, he warns that a blanket denial of disagreement is not correct, implying that some aspects of the dispute are substantive.

Key Terms
خلاف لفظي
فخر الرازي
إمام الحرمين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the entire debate over increase and decrease is meaningless or purely verbal.
Correction: The author says absolute denial of disagreement is not correct, indicating substantive aspects remain.

Checkpoint
According to the author, who among the following held that the dispute over increase and decrease of faith is merely verbal?
A) Al-Khattabi
B) Fakhr al-Razi and Imam al-Haramayn
C) Imam Abu Hanifa
D) The author himself

Key Takeaway
While some scholars view the dispute as verbal, the author reminds us that not all disagreement can be dismissed as such.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you encounter a difference of opinion in your faith or among scholars, do you immediately dismiss it as 'just a verbal dispute' to avoid the discomfort of real disagreement? How does this lesson challenge you to take such disagreements more seriously? Commit to researching one disputed issue this week with the intention of understanding, not dismissing.
?
Is your desire for unity in the community sometimes an excuse to gloss over real theological differences? Reflect on a time when you avoided a difficult discussion because it was easier to call it 'just a difference of wording'. What would it cost you to engage with the real substance instead? This lesson warns that absolute denial of disagreement is incorrect — will you embrace the truth even when it creates tension?
?
The author carefully distinguishes between two grammatical interpretations before clarifying his position. How often do you rush to a conclusion about a religious issue without analyzing the precise wording of the sources? In what area of your belief or practice do you need to slow down and examine the actual text rather than accept a simplified version? Make a concrete plan to study one disputed point directly from the primary sources this week.

Does Faith Increase? Abu Hanifa's View and Its Defense
The author presents the view that iman does not increase or decrease, the objection, and the response.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the argument that iman does not increase or decrease, the objection based on levels of attestation, and the response that interprets scriptural evidence as referring to the object of belief or actions.

Core Idea
Faith is either complete or absent; only its objects increase.

This passage presents a classic disagreement in Islamic theology: can iman (faith) increase or decrease? The great Hanafi Imam Abu Hanifa held that it cannot, because true faith is a state of complete certainty and submission. But others pointed out that people's conviction clearly varies. How can these positions be reconciled? The passage gives both the objection and a sophisticated answer based on interpretation of scripture.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing, then read the translation. Pay attention to the flow: statement, objection, response.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's definition and reasoning
Find where Abu Hanifa defines iman as 'attestation reaching the ultimate degree of certainty and acquiescence.' Notice why he concludes it cannot increase: ultimate degrees have no levels.
This is the core of his argument.
3
Examine the objection: levels of attestation
The objection lists several levels: muqallid, one who knows by proof, muraqib, mushahid, mustaghriq. Ask yourself: does this show that iman itself varies?
4
Understand the ta'wil response
The group reinterpreted the verses and hadith that mention increase. For verses: increase is in the object of belief (new revelations). For hadith: increase and decrease refer to actions, not the core attestation.
This defends the view that iman itself does not change.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَقِيلَ: (لا)) أي : وقال جماعة أعظمُهم الإمام أبو حنيفة ـ وهو النعمان بن ثابت ـ : لا يزيد ولا ينقصُ ؛ لأنه اسم للتصديق البالغ نهاية الجزم والإذعان، وهذا لا يتصور فيه ما ذُكرَ ؛ لأن تلك النهاية لا مراتب لها .
وبحث فيه بأن التصديق مراتب، فإن تصديق المقلّد ليس كتصديق العارف بالدليل، وهو ليس كتصديق المراقب، وهو ليس كتصديق المشاهد، وهو ليس كتصديق المستغرقِ الذي لا يُشاهدُ إلا الله
وتأوَّلَ هؤلاء الجماعةُ الآيات السابقة بأن الزيادة إنما هي في المؤمَنِ به؛ لأن الصحابة كانوا آمنوا بما أنزل على النبي الا الله وكانَتِ الشريعة لم تتم، وكانت الأحكام تنزلُ شيئاً فشيئاً، فكانوا يؤمنون بكل ما يتجدد وتأوَّلوا الأحاديث السابقة بأن الزيادة والنقص يرجعُ كلَّ منهما إلى الأعمال لا التصديق.
His statement: 'And it was said: (No)' meaning: A group, the greatest of whom is Imam Abu Hanifa — and he is al-Nu'man ibn Thabit — said: Faith does not increase nor decrease; because it is a name for the attestation that reaches the ultimate degree of certainty and acquiescence, and in this what was mentioned cannot be imagined; because that ultimate degree has no levels. And it was objected that attestation has levels, for the attestation of a blind follower is not like the attestation of one who knows by proof, and it is not like the attestation of one who watches, and it is not like the attestation of the witness, and it is not like the attestation of the absorbed one who witnesses nothing but God. And these people interpreted the previous verses [indicating increase] by saying that the increase is in the object of belief; because the Companions believed in what was revealed to the Prophet [؟] and the Law was not yet complete, and the rulings were revealed gradually, so they believed in everything new that occurred; and they interpreted the previous hadiths by saying that the increase and decrease each refer to actions, not to attestation.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents a view and then an objection and response. It begins with the position of Abu Hanifa and others that iman (faith) does not increase or decrease. They define iman as attestation (tasdiq) that has reached the ultimate level of certainty (jazm) and submission (idhan). Since it is at the ultimate level, it cannot have degrees; therefore increase or decrease is impossible. Then a discussion (bahth) is raised: attestation does have levels. The author gives examples: the attestation of a blind follower (muqallid) is not like that of one who knows by proof; that of one who watches (muraqib) is not like that of one who witnesses (mushahid); and that is not like the one who is completely absorbed in witnessing God alone. So there are varying degrees. In response, the group that denied increase and decrease reinterpreted (ta'wīl) the verses that mention increase. They said the increase is in the object of belief (mu'man bihi), not in the act of belief itself. The early Muslims increased in what they believed as new revelations came. Similarly, they reinterpreted hadiths by saying that the increase and decrease refer to actions, not to the inner attestation. This defends their view that the essence of iman does not change.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الجزم
الإذعان
التقليد
المراقب
المشاهد
المستغرق
الزيادة والنقص
التأويل

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The objection that attestation has levels disproves Abu Hanifa's view that iman does not increase or decrease.
Correction: The objection is answered by ta'wil that shifts the meaning of increase to the object of belief or to actions, preserving the view that the essence of iman is unchanging.

Checkpoint
How did the group that denies increase and decrease interpret the verses that mention increase in faith?
A) They said the increase is in the attestation itself.
B) They said the increase is in the object of belief.
C) They said the increase is in actions.
D) They said the verses are abrogated.

Key Takeaway
Abu Hanifa and his followers defend the view that iman does not increase or decrease by defining it as ultimate certainty and reinterpreting scriptural evidence as referring to the object of belief or actions.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Abu Hanifa defines iman as the ultimate degree of certainty. Have you ever examined your own faith to see if it reaches that level? What specific doubts or uncertainties still linger in your heart, and what are you doing to remove them?
?
The Companions' faith increased in scope as new revelations came. When was the last time your understanding of what you believe actually grew? Were you actively seeking new knowledge about your Lord, or have you been stagnant?
?
If faith is not measured by actions, does that comfort you or alarm you? Are you using this belief as an excuse to be negligent in worship, or does it drive you to deepen your certainty so that your actions naturally follow?

The Verbal Dispute Over Iman's Increase and Decrease
The author presents the verbal dispute view and explains its reasoning, then distances himself.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the view that the disagreement about whether iman increases is merely verbal, and why the author distances himself from that view.

Core Idea
The conflict over iman's increase may be only verbal, but the heart's attestation truly varies in strength.

Some scholars argue that the apparent disagreement over whether faith increases is really about different aspects of faith—its essence versus its perfection. This lesson explores that verbal dispute and the author's caution about adopting it.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic and translation
First, read the Arabic passage carefully without over-analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the basic meaning.
Notice the structure: the author quotes a saying and then comments on it.
2
Identify the two positions and reconciliation
Look for the two groups: one says iman increases/decreases, the other says it doesn't. The verbal dispute reconciles them by attributing each to a different aspect of faith.
The reconciliation: increase refers to actions (kamaal), constancy refers to essence (asl, inner tasdeeq).
3
Understand the author's qualification
The author uses the phrase 'kadha qad nuqila' to disclaim responsibility. He signals that this view is merely transmitted, not necessarily correct.
He then states the correct view: inner tasdeeq does increase with reflection and divine manifestation.
4
Reflect on the true nature of iman's increase
Consider why the author insists that faith truly increases, giving the example of the siddiqeen (veracious) whose faith is stronger and impervious to doubts.
This reinforces that the disagreement is real, not merely verbal.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (وَقِيلَ: لَا خُلْفَ) استئناف لا عطف كما قاله المصنف، ويحتمل أن يكون معطوفاً على مقدر مفهوم من السياق، والتقديرُ : قد اشتهر أن بين القوم خلافاً حقيقيًّا، وقيل : (لا خلفٌ) أي : وقال جماعةٌ منهم الفخر الرازي وإمام الحرمين: ليس الخلاف بين الفريقين حقيقيًّا، بل لفظيًّا، ونفي الخلاف على الإطلاق لا يصح، ووجه كون الخلاف لفظيًّا : أن القول بأنه يزيد وينقص، محمول على ما به كماله وهو الأعمال، والقول بأنه لا يزيد ولا ينقص محمول على أصله وهو التصديق الباطني. وقوله : (كَذَا قَدْ نُقِلَا) راجع للقيل الأخير، لا لجميع ما سبق، وأشار بذلك إلى التبرِّي من عُهْدة صحةِ هذا القيل؛ لأن الأصح أن التصديق القلبي يزيد وينقص بكثرة النظر ووضوح الأدلة وعدمهما، وقد يزيد أيضاً بمحض التجلي كما سبق، ولهذا كان إيمان الصديقين أقوى من إيمان غيرهم ؛ بحيث لا تعتريه الشُّبَه، على أن هذا القيل خلافُ المعروف بين القوم من أن الخلاف حقيقي.
His statement: 'And it was said: No disagreement' is a new beginning and not a conjunction, as the author said. And it is possible that it is conjoined to an understood element from the context, the estimation being: It is famous that there is a real disagreement among the people, and it was said: 'No disagreement' meaning: A group among them Fakhr al-Razi and the Imam al-Haramayn said: The disagreement between the two groups is not real, but verbal. And denying disagreement absolutely is not correct. The reason for it being verbal is that the statement that it (faith) increases and decreases is carried upon that which perfects it, which is actions, and the statement that it does not increase nor decrease is carried upon its essence, which is inner attestation. And his statement: 'Thus it has been transmitted' refers to the last saying, not to all that preceded. And by that he indicated disavowal of responsibility for the soundness of this saying; because the most correct is that the heart's attestation increases and decreases with the abundance of reflection and clarity of proofs and their lack, and it may also increase by sheer divine manifestation as mentioned, and for this reason the faith of the veracious is stronger than the faith of others, to the extent that doubts do not befall it, although this saying contradicts what is known among the people that the disagreement is real.
Source pages p. 139

Commentary
This passage presents the view that the dispute over whether iman increases or decreases is merely verbal (lafzī), not real. The author explains the structure of the expression (qīla: la khulf). Then the content: some scholars like Fakhr al-Razi and the Imam al-Haramayn hold that the disagreement is not substantial. The reason: those who say iman increases and decreases are referring to its perfection (actions), while those who say it does not increase or decrease are referring to its essence (inner tasdiq). Thus there is no real contradiction. The author then comments on the phrase 'kadhā qad nuqilā' saying it refers only to this last saying, and the author disclaims responsibility for its soundness, because the correct view is that the heart's attestation does increase and decrease with reflection and clarity of proofs, and even by divine manifestation. This is why the faith of the siddiqin is stronger. Nevertheless, this saying contradicts the known fact that the disagreement is real.

Key Terms
الخلاف اللفظي
الخلاف الحقيقي
التصديق الباطني
الكمال
الأصل
التجلي
الصديقين

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The author endorses the verbal dispute view and denies that iman can increase.
Correction: The author explicitly distances himself from the verbal dispute view and affirms that iman (inner tasdiq) does increase with reflection, proofs, and divine manifestation.

Checkpoint
According to the verbal dispute view, what does the statement that iman increases refer to?
A) The essence of faith (inner attestation)
B) The actions that perfect faith
C) The outward declaration
D) The number of beliefs

Key Takeaway
The verbal dispute theory reconciles disagreements about iman by attributing increase to actions and constancy to essence, but the author maintains that iman truly increases in the heart.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The author says the faith of the siddiqin is stronger, immune to doubts. Does your own iman allow you to face doubts without wavering? What step can you take today to strengthen your heart's attestation so that doubts lose their power over you?
?
The verbal dispute theory might seem to resolve tension, but the author insists iman truly varies. How often do you treat your own iman as static, assuming it's fine as it is? What would change if you truly believed it could increase through reflection and seeking clear proofs?
?
The passage mentions that iman increases by sheer divine manifestation. Have you ever experienced a moment of spiritual clarity that you knew was a gift? How can you prepare yourself to receive such moments?

The Author's Conclusion on the Nature of Faith
The author states the relied-upon view: iman is only inner attestation, nutq is for worldly rulings, and it increases and decreases.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the author's relied-upon position that iman is only inner attestation, that verbal profession is only for worldly rulings, and that iman does increase and decrease.

Core Idea
Iman is inner attestation; it increases and decreases.

In this concluding passage, the author summarizes the correct view on the definition of iman (faith). After discussing various opinions, he states the relied-upon position: iman is exclusively inner attestation (tasdiq). He clarifies that the verbal profession (nutq) is not part of iman but is required for worldly legal rulings. He also affirms that iman can increase and decrease, which is consistent with its nature as attestation. This lesson will unpack these three points and their significance.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage and its translation. Notice the three distinct claims made by the author.
2
Identify the three points
The passage states: (1) iman is only tasdiq, (2) nutq is a condition for worldly rulings, (3) iman increases and decreases. Understand each point.
3
Understand the nuance
The author reconciles different views by separating the essence of iman (tasdiq) from its effects (nutq) and its variability (increase/decrease).
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Consider how this definition addresses common misconceptions about faith and actions in theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فتحصَّلَ أن المعتمد أن الإيمان هو التصديق فقط، وأن النطق شرط في إجراء الأحكام الدنيوية، وأن الإيمان يزيد وينقص كما هو التحقيق؛ فاستفده، والله ولي التوفيق .
Thus it is concluded that the relied-upon view is that faith is only attestation, and that verbal utterance is a condition for the application of worldly legal rulings, and that faith increases and decreases as is verified; so benefit from it, and Allah is the Grantor of success.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This brief passage is the author's own conclusion to the discussion on the nature of iman. He states three points: (1) The relied-upon (mu'tamad) position is that iman is exclusively inner attestation (tasdiq). (2) The verbal profession (nutq) is a condition for the implementation of worldly rulings (like inheritance, marriage, etc.) but is not part of the essence of iman. (3) Despite being only attestation, iman does increase and decrease, as is the verification (tahqīq). This harmonizes the views: iman's essence is constant, but its strength varies.

Key Terms
المعتمد
التصديق
النطق
الأحكام الدنيوية
الزيادة والنقص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that if iman is only inner attestation, it cannot increase or decrease.
Correction: The author clarifies that iman does increase and decrease in intensity, even though its essence is attestation.

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon view according to the author regarding the definition of iman?
A) Iman is inner attestation and actions.
B) Iman is only inner attestation.
C) Iman is only verbal profession.
D) Iman is attestation and profession.

Key Takeaway
The author's final position is that iman is only inner attestation, but it can increase and decrease, and verbal profession is required only for worldly legal rulings.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Your faith is defined as inner attestation alone. If your faith were tested today by your inner conviction alone—not by your external practices—would you still be confident that your tasdiq is true? What would you need to change inside your heart to make that attestation real?
?
The author says faith increases and decreases. When was the last time you felt your faith decrease? Did you do anything about it, or did you let it slide? What specific step will you take today to increase your tasdiq?
?
Verbal profession is only for worldly rulings, but your tongue says 'La ilaha illa Allah' daily. Does your heart's attestation match your tongue's profession? If not, which one is lying—your tongue or your heart? What will you do about that gap?
