Faith and Disbelief
beginner
5 min
Resolving the Verbal Disagreement on Faith's Increase
Commentator explains and resolves the verbal dispute on faith's increase.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the disagreement about faith increasing and decreasing is verbal and how it is resolved by distinguishing between the essence of faith and its perfection through actions.

Core Idea
The dispute is verbal: faith itself doesn't change, but its perfection through actions does.

The commentator explains a long-standing theological controversy: does faith increase or decrease? He shows that the disagreement is only apparent, rooted in different referents of the word 'faith'. This lesson unpacks his resolution.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once to get its flow, then the translation. Notice the two opposing views mentioned.
2
Identify the two positions
The passage contrasts 'it increases and decreases' (applied to actions/works) with 'it does not increase or decrease' (applied to inward belief).
3
Understand the verbal nature
The commentator says the disagreement is verbal (lafẓī) because each side means something different by 'faith'. The sound view is that belief itself can increase with evidence.
Notice the final established view: faith is belief, but it does increase and decrease.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ووجه كون الخلاف لفظيًّا : أن القول بأنه يزيد وينقص، محمول على ما به كماله وهو الأعمال، والقول بأنه لا يزيد ولا ينقص محمول على أصله وهو التصديق الباطني. وقوله : (كَذَا قَدْ نُقِلَا) راجع للقيل الأخير، لا لجميع ما سبق، وأشار بذلك إلى التبرِّي من عُهْدة صحةِ هذا القيل؛ لأن الأصح أن التصديق القلبي يزيد وينقص بكثرة النظر ووضوح الأدلة وعدمهما (١) ، وقد يزيد أيضاً بمحض التجلي كما سبق، ولهذا كان إيمان الصديقين أقوى من إيمان غيرهم ؛ بحيث لا تعتريه الشُّبَه، على أن هذا القيل خلافُ المعروف بين القوم من أن الخلاف حقيقي. فتحصَّلَ أن المعتمد أن الإيمان هو التصديق فقط، وأن النطق شرط في إجراء الأحكام الدنيوية، وأن الإيمان يزيد وينقص كما هو التحقيق؛ فاستفده، والله ولي التوفيق . في الاقتصاد حول هذه المسألة (وهذا الاختلافُ منشؤُهُ الجهلُ بكون الاسم مشتركاً ؛ أعني : اسم الايمان، وإذا فصل مسميات هذا اللفظ ارتفع الخلاف، وهو مشترك بين ثلاثة معان؛ إذ قد يُعبر به عن التصديق اليقيني البرهاني، وقد يُعبَّر به عن الاعتقاد التقليدي إذا كان جزماً ، وقد يُعبَّرُ به عن تصديق معه العمل بموجب التصديق . قال إمامنا الغزالي في «الاقتصاد»: إن أطلق الإيمان بمعنى التصديق البرهاني لم يتصور زيادته ولا نقصانه، بل اليقينُ إن حصل بكماله فلا مزيد عليه، وإن لم يحصل بكماله فليس بيقين، وهي خطَّةٌ واحدة، ولا يتصوَّرُ فيها زيادة ونقصان، إلا أن يُراد به زيادة وضوح؛ أي : زيادة طمأنينة النفس إليه ؛ بأن النفس تطمئن إلى اليقينيات النظرية في الابتداء إلى حد ما، فإذا تواردت الأدلة على شيء واحد أفاد بظاهر الأدلة زيادة طمأنينة، وكلُّ من مارس العلوم أدرك تفاوتاً في طمأنينة نفسه إلى العلم الضروري.
And the explanation of the disagreement being verbal is that the statement that it increases and decreases is applied to that by which its perfection is achieved, which is actions, and the statement that it does not increase or decrease is applied to its origin, which is inward belief. And his statement: (thus it has been transmitted) refers to the latter saying, not to all that preceded, and by that he indicated disclaiming responsibility for the correctness of this saying; because the more correct view is that heart belief increases and decreases with much reflection and clarity of evidence and their absence (1), and it may also increase by pure manifestation as previously mentioned, and for this reason the faith of the truthful ones is stronger than the faith of others such that doubts do not affect them, although this saying contradicts what is known among the people that the disagreement is real. So the result is that the relied-upon view is that faith is only belief, and that verbal utterance is a condition for applying worldly rulings, and that faith increases and decreases as is the verification; so benefit from it, and Allah is the Grantor of success. In al-Iqtisad concerning this issue (and this disagreement originates from ignorance of the name being polysemous; I mean: the name al-iman, and if the referents of this word are distinguished the disagreement disappears, and it is polysemous among three meanings: for it may be used for certain demonstrative belief, and it may be used for traditional conviction if it is firm, and it may be used for belief accompanied by action in accordance with the belief. Our Imam al-Ghazali said in al-Iqtisad: If al-iman is used in the sense of demonstrative belief, neither its increase nor its decrease can be conceived; rather certainty if it is attained completely there is no increase beyond it, and if it is not attained completely then it is not certainty, and it is a single level, and increase and decrease cannot be conceived in it, unless what is meant is increase in clarity; that is, increase in the soul's tranquility towards it; because the soul has tranquility towards theoretical certainties initially to a certain extent, and when evidences concur on one thing, due to overt evidences it gives additional tranquility, and whoever practices the sciences perceives a disparity in his soul's tranquility towards necessary knowledge.
Source pages p. 140

Commentary
This passage is a doctrinal discussion resolving the disagreement about whether faith (al-iman) increases and decreases. The commentator begins by explaining that the dispute is verbal: those who say faith increases and decreases refer to its perfection through works, while those who deny increase refer to its essence, which is inward belief. He then clarifies that the poet's expression 'thus it has been transmitted' applies only to the latter view, distancing himself from its validation, as the sound opinion is that heart belief does increase and decrease with the frequency and clarity of evidences. He supports this with the fact that the faith of the truthful is stronger and immune to doubts. The passage concludes with the established view: faith is essentially belief, verbal confession is a condition for worldly rulings, and faith indeed increases and decreases. A supporting quote from al-Ghazali's Iqtisad follows, explaining that demonstrative belief cannot increase in certainty but can increase in tranquility.

Key Terms
الإيمان
التصديق
الزيادة والنقصان
الخلاف اللفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the disagreement is real and irreconcilable.
Correction: The commentator shows it is merely verbal and can be resolved by distinguishing the referents of 'iman'.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the relied-upon view regarding faith and its increase?
A) Faith does not increase or decrease at all.
B) Faith increases and decreases in its essence (inward belief).
C) Faith increases and decreases in its perfection through works, while inward belief remains unchanged.
D) Faith increases only in outward works, not in belief.

Key Takeaway
The controversy on faith's increase is resolved by understanding that faith in its essence (belief) does increase with evidence, while actions are its perfection.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you actively seek to increase your faith by reflecting on evidence, or do you rely on routine? When was the last time you felt your belief strengthen through careful thought?
?
The passage says the faith of the truthful is so strong that doubts do not affect them. What doubts have shaken you recently, and what concrete step can you take this week to build your certainty so that doubts lose their power?
?
If verbal confession is only for worldly rulings, but the essence is inward belief, are you content with a faith that is merely outward? What would it take for your inner conviction to match—or surpass—your public practice?

Faith and Disbelief

Al-Ghazali on Increase in Tranquility of Faith
Al-Ghazali distinguishes three meanings of 'iman' and explains increase in tranquility.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Ghazali's argument that demonstrative belief does not increase in certainty but can increase in tranquility.

Core Idea
Certainty is all-or-nothing; only the heart's tranquility deepens.

Imam al-Ghazali, in his Iqtisad, offers a nuanced perspective on the increase of faith. He argues that if faith means demonstrative certainty, it cannot increase because true certainty is one level. However, the soul's tranquility towards that certainty can grow with repeated evidences. This lesson explores that distinction.

Guided Path
1
Read al-Ghazali's passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice he lists three meanings of 'iman' and then focuses on demonstrative belief.
2
Distinguish certainty from tranquility
Al-Ghazali says certainty is indivisible: either you have it completely or you don't. But tranquility of the soul in that certainty can vary.
Tranquility (ṭumaʾnīna) is a psychological calmness.
3
Reflect on the role of evidence
Repeated evidence does not increase certainty itself but increases the heart's attachment and ease with the truth.
This is how 'increase' can be applied to demonstrative belief.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

?

?

Based on this lesson, will you now take a different approach to strengthen your faith? What evidence from revelation or creation can you meditate on this week to increase your soul's tranquility?
?

Discrete Quantity in Actions and Refutation of Mu'tazila
Defines and negates discrete quantity; refutes Mu'tazila.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the concept of the discrete quantity in actions and how it is negated by the oneness of actions, thereby refuting the Mu'tazila claim that humans create their own actions.

Core Idea
The discrete quantity in actions is the false idea that someone other than God brings actions into existence.

Sanusi introduces a subtle but critical distinction: actions are attributed to humans only in the mode of acquisition (kasb) and choice, not creation. This passage clarifies the concept of the discrete quantity—the erroneous notion that anyone other than Allah can originate an act. It then uses this principle to refute the Mu'tazila who claim that humans create their own voluntary actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
Notice the term 'الكسب' (acquisition) appears here.
2
Understand the definition of discrete quantity
Examine how the author defines the discrete quantity in actions: that someone other than God has an action in the mode of bringing into existence. Contrast it with the true attribution through acquisition and choice.
3
Recognize the refutation
See how the principle of oneness of actions negates this discrete quantity. Then apply it to the Mu'tazila: their claim that humans create actions is refuted because only God creates.
The Mu'tazila are not deemed disbelievers because they acknowledge that God gives them the power (iqdar) over actions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والكم المنفصلُ في الأفعال : وهو أن يكون لغير الله فعل من الأفعال على وجه الإيجادِ، وإنَّما ينسب الفعلُ له على وجه الكسب والاختيار، وهذا الكم منفي بوحدانية الأفعال، وفي ذلك ردّ على المعتزلة القائلين بأن العبد يخلق أفعال نفسه الاختبارية، وإنما لم يكفروا بذلك لاعترافهم بأن إقدارَهُ عليها من الله تعالى، وبعضُهم كفَّرَهم، وجعل المجوس أسعد حالاً منهم ؛ إذ المجوس قالوا بمؤثرين)، وهؤلاء أثبتوا ما لا حصر له، لكن الراجح عدم كفرهم.
And the discrete quantity in actions: That someone other than God has an action in the mode of bringing into existence. Rather, the action is attributed to him in the mode of acquisition and choice. This quantity is negated by oneness of actions. In that is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who say that the servant creates his own voluntary actions. They were not deemed disbelievers because of that due to their acknowledgment that enabling him over them is from God. Some deemed them disbelievers and considered the Magians more fortunate than them, since the Magians said there are two effectors, while these [Mu'tazila] affirmed what is limitless. But the correct view is their non-disbelief.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila doctrine that humans create their own voluntary actions. It identifies this as the discrete quantity in actions—the idea that someone other than God brings actions into existence. However, the author notes that actions are attributed to humans only in the mode of kasb (acquisition) and choice, not creation. This is negated by oneness of actions. The passage then discusses the ruling on the Mu'tazila: they are not considered disbelievers because they acknowledge that God gives them the power (iqdar) over their actions. Some scholars did declare them disbelievers, even saying the Magians (dualists) are better off because they only posit two effectors, while the Mu'tazila posit innumerable effectors (each human creating his own actions). But the preferable view (al-rajih) is that they are not disbelievers.

Key Terms
الكم المنفصل
الإيجاد
الكسب
الاختيار
وحدانية الأفعال

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think the Mu'tazila are automatically kafir for their doctrine.
Correction: The text clarifies they are not disbelievers because they acknowledge God's enabling (iqdar).

Checkpoint
Why does the text say the Mu'tazila were not deemed disbelievers?
A) Because they denied God's existence
B) Because they acknowledged that God gives them power over actions
C) Because they affirmed free will
D) Because they were Muslims

Key Takeaway
The discrete quantity in actions is false, and the Mu'tazila claim is refuted, but they are not deemed disbelievers due to their acknowledgment of God's enabling.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Do you truly believe that every action you perform, even the ones you choose, is created by God alone? How does that reshape your understanding of your own achievements and failures? Will you pause today to thank God for the very ability to act?
?
The Mu'tazila acknowledged God's enabling power, yet still fell into a serious error. Are there any beliefs you hold that might seem almost right but subtly shift credit away from God's sole creation? What would it take to uproot that error from your heart?
?
When you sin, do you blame your free will as if you acted independently, or do you remember that God is the Creator of that sin? Can you repent with both humility for your choice and awe of God's ultimate power, seeking His forgiveness and help to avoid the same sin?

Ruling on the Mu'tazila: Disbelief or Not?
Discusses takfir ruling on Mu'tazila; preferred view is non-disbelief.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the differing scholarly opinions on whether the Mu'tazila are considered disbelievers for their doctrine of human creation of actions, and the preferred view that they are not.

Core Idea
The correct view is that the Mu'tazila are not disbelievers despite their error on actions.

After refuting the Mu'tazila doctrine, the text turns to the serious question of takfir. Some scholars declared them disbelievers, even comparing them unfavorably to the Magians. However, the author presents the preferred view (al-rajih) that they are not disbelievers. This lesson examines that ruling and its basis.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Notice the strong comparison to the Magians.
The Arabic includes a closing parenthesis issue but meaning is clear.
2
Understand the two opinions
Identify the two positions: some declared the Mu'tazila disbelievers, others (the preferred view) did not.
The reasoning for takfir is that the Mu'tazila posit countless creators.
3
Grasp the preferred view's reasoning
The preferred view (al-rajih) holds they are not disbelievers, likely because they still affirm God's enabling of actions.
This aligns with the earlier statement that they were not deemed disbelievers due to their acknowledgment of iqdar.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And the discrete quantity in actions: That someone other than God has an action in the mode of bringing into existence. Rather, the action is attributed to him in the mode of acquisition and choice. This quantity is negated by oneness of actions. In that is a refutation of the Mu'tazila who say that the servant creates his own voluntary actions. They were not deemed disbelievers because of that due to their acknowledgment that enabling him over them is from God. Some deemed them disbelievers and considered the Magians more fortunate than them, since the Magians said there are two effectors, while these [Mu'tazila] affirmed what is limitless. But the correct view is their non-disbelief.
Source pages p. 158

Commentary
This passage is a refutation of the Mu'tazila doctrine that humans create their own voluntary actions. It identifies this as the discrete quantity in actions—the idea that someone other than God brings actions into existence. However, the author notes that actions are attributed to humans only in the mode of kasb (acquisition) and choice, not creation. This is negated by oneness of actions. The passage then discusses the ruling on the Mu'tazila: they are not considered disbelievers because they acknowledge that God gives them the power (iqdar) over their actions. But the preferable view (al-rajih) is that they are not disbelievers.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some people think the Mu'tazila are definitely disbelievers.
Correction: The text says the correct view is that they are not disbelievers (al-rajih 'adam kufrihim).

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why did some scholars consider the Magians more fortunate than the Mu'tazila?
A) The Magians had a simpler theology
B) The Magians believed in one God
C) The Magians only posited two effectors, while the Mu'tazila posited limitless
D) The Magians were not Muslims

Key Takeaway
The preferred scholarly position is that the Mu'tazila are not considered disbelievers, despite their grave error in attributing creation to humans.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever been quick to label someone as misguided or outside Islam due to a theological error? How does the preferred view here—despite the severity of the error—call you to more careful judgment? What would it take for you to adopt that same caution?
?
When you consider the Mu'tazila's belief that humans create their own actions, what does that reveal about your own understanding of God's sovereignty? Are there areas in your life where you subtly act as if you are the ultimate creator of your deeds? How can you repent from that?
?
This lesson shows that even a grave error does not automatically expel someone from faith. How does this challenge your attitude towards Muslims with whom you disagree theologically? Will you now treat them with more humility and less certainty about their final state?

The Ruling on Saying 'In Sha Rabbi' and the Ash'ari-Maturidi Verbal Difference
The rule of saying 'In sha rabbi' and the verbal difference between Ash'aris and Maturidis

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the scholarly ruling on saying 'إن شاء ربي' when declaring faith, and why the disagreement between Ash'aris and Maturidis on this issue is considered verbal rather than substantive.

Core Idea
Saying 'if Allah wills' about one's faith is either a blessing or doubt—only the latter is forbidden.

This passage tackles a common phrase among Muslims: 'if my Lord wills' when declaring one's faith. Is it permissible? The answer depends on intention. The lesson also clarifies that the well-known difference between Ash'aris and Maturidis on this point is merely verbal, not real.

Guided Path
1
Read the full passage and translation
Start by reading the Arabic and English side by side to get an overview of the discussion.
Pay attention to the poetic section, as it summarizes key rulings.
2
Distinguish between the two intentions
Notice that the passage divides cases into those intending blessing (تبرك) and those intending doubt (شك). The ruling changes accordingly.
Blessing is permissible by consensus; doubt is forbidden by consensus.
3
Follow the poetic summary
The poem from the text summarizes the positions of Malik, Hanafi, and Shafi'i scholars. Identify the ruling for each and the consensus points.
The poem also introduces a third scenario where the intention is unclear—this is the locus of disagreement.
4
Understand the verbal difference
The passage concludes that the Ash'ari and Maturidi disagreement is only about wording, not actual ruling. Reflect on why this matters for inter-school debates.
They agree on the rulings but differ on the meaning of 'felicity' and 'misery'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو التبرك، وإلا امتنع في الأول إجماعاً، وجاز في الثاني كذلك، وقد نظم بعضُ الأفاضل حاصل هذا، فقال: [من الرجز] مَنْ قَالَ: إِنِّي مُؤْمِنٌ يَمْنَع مِنْ مَقَالِهِ إِنْ شَاءَ رَبِّيْ) يَا فَطِنْ وَذَا لِمَالكِ، وَبَعْضُ تَابِعِيه يُوجِبُ أَنْ يَقُولَ هَذَا يَا نَبِية وَمِثْلُ مَا لِمَالِكِ للحَنَفِي والشَّافِعِي جَوْزَ هَذَا فَاعْرِفِ وَامْنَعْهُ إِجْمَاعاً إِذَا أَرَادَ بِهْ الشَّكَ فِي إِيْمَانِهِ يَا مُنْتَبِهْ كَعَدَمِ المَنْعِ إِذَا بِهِ يُرَادْ تَبَرُّكُ بِذِكْرِ خَالِقِ العِبَادُ فَالخُلْفَ حَيْثُ لَمْ يُرِدْ شَكًا وَلَا تَبَرُّكاً فَكُنْ بِذَا مُحْتَفِلَا أو يقطعه، وتارة يشك هل يكون مؤمناً عند الموت أو لا ، فإن قصد التبرك جازت المشيئة بلا خلاف وإن قصد التعليق مع الصورة الأولى للشك امتنع بلا خلاف، فتبين أن محل الخلاف ما لو أطلق أو قصد التعليق مع صورة الشك الثانية. هذا ما ظهر. انتهى أجهوري. وبالجملة فالخلاف بين الأشاعرة والماتريدية لفظي ؛ لأنَّهم اختلفوا في المراد من لفظ السعادة، ولفظ الشقاوة مع الاتفاق في الأحكام.
Or blessing, and if not, it is forbidden in the first by consensus, and permissible in the second likewise. And some virtuous ones have composed the gist of this, saying: [in rajaz] 'Whoever says: I am a believer is prevented from his statement if he says: if my Lord wills, O clever one, and this is for Malik. And some of his followers obligate that he says this, O prophet, and like what is for Malik. For the Hanafi and Shafi'i, this is permissible, so know, and forbid it by consensus if he intends by it doubt in his faith, O attentive one. Like the absence of prohibition if by it is intended blessing by mentioning the Creator of servants. So disagreement is where he does not intend doubt nor blessing, so be careful with this.' Or he cuts it off, and sometimes he doubts whether he will be a believer at death or not. If he intends blessing, the conditional is permissible without disagreement, and if he intends conditioning with the first image of doubt, it is forbidden without disagreement. So it becomes clear that the locus of disagreement is when he is absolute or intends conditioning with the second image of doubt. This is what appears. End of Ajhuri. And in summary, the disagreement between the Ash'aris and Maturidis is verbal, because they differed regarding the intended meaning of the word 'felicity' and the word 'misery' while agreeing on the rulings.
Source pages p. 231

Commentary
This passage discusses the permissibility of saying 'if my Lord wills' when declaring faith. It begins by stating that if the intention is blessing, it is allowed, otherwise it is forbidden by consensus. Then it presents a poetic summary of the different positions among scholars (Malik, Hanafi, Shafi'i). The poem explains that if the speaker intends doubt, it is forbidden; if he intends blessing, it is allowed. The commentary then clarifies that the disagreement is only about cases where neither doubt nor blessing is intended. The footnote adds details about conditional statements regarding doubt about future belief. Finally, the passage notes that the difference between Ash'aris and Maturidis on this issue is merely verbal, as they agree on the rulings but differ on the terminology of 'felicity' and 'misery'.

Key Terms
إن شاء ربي
التبرك
الخلاف اللفظي

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That the difference between Ash'aris and Maturidis is a substantive, deep theological disagreement.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that the disagreement is verbal (لفظي); they actually agree on the rulings but differ in the interpretation of the terms 'felicity' and 'misery'.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is saying 'إن شاء ربي' in declaring faith unanimously forbidden?
A) When intending blessing.
B) When intending doubt.
C) When absolute.
D) When conditioning for the second image of doubt.

Key Takeaway
The permissibility of saying 'if my Lord wills' about faith depends on whether one intends blessing or doubt, and the Ash'ari-Maturidi dispute over this is verbal, not doctrinal.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Have you ever uttered 'if Allah wills' about your faith without checking your heart? What was your true intention—was it to seek blessing or did it hide a doubt you're afraid to face? This week, before you speak such words, pause and ask Allah to purify your intention.
?
The scholars warn that doubting one's current faith is forbidden. Is there any belief you hold that you secretly question but avoid examining? What would it cost you to honestly confront that doubt and seek knowledge to resolve it? Commit tonight to write down one area of uncertainty and a reliable source to study.
?
The Ash'ari-Maturidi difference is called 'verbal,' yet they debated it vigorously. Are you more attached to the labels of your school than to the substance of your heart's conviction? How many arguments have you won that left your soul unchanged? Before you next debate theology, ask yourself: 'Does this bring me closer to Allah or just feed my ego?'

The Two Testimonies: Core of Faith Requiring Understanding
Author states that the shahadatayn contain all beliefs and must be understood.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand why the two testimonies are the core of faith and why understanding their meaning is essential for valid iman.

Core Idea
The shahada is the key to faith, but only if you know what it means.

This passage reveals the profound significance of the two testimonies. While they are brief utterances, they encapsulate every belief of Islam. The Lawgiver made them the formal declaration of faith, but mere pronunciation is not enough; understanding is required. Let's explore why.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once, then its translation. Notice how the author presents the comprehensive nature of the shahada.
2
Identify the two key claims
The passage makes two main points: (1) the shahadatayn encompass all beliefs, and (2) understanding their meaning is necessary. Locate each claim in the text.
3
Reflect on the necessity of understanding
Ask yourself: Why can't mere utterance suffice? What does understanding add to faith? The scholars' explicit statement clarifies this.
This connects to the learning objective.
4
Consider a common error
Some think just saying the shahada is enough. The passage corrects this: without understanding, no benefit. Note how this guards against superficial Islam.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فقد بان لك تضمن كلمتي الشهادة لجميع العقائد المتقدّمة، ولعلهما لهذا المعنى مع اختصارهما جعلهما الشارع ترجمة عمَّا في القلب من الإيمان، ولم يقبل من أحدٍ الإيمان إلا بهما مع القدرة عليهما، وقد نصَّ العلماء على أنه لا بد من فهم معناهما ولو إجمالاً، وإلا لم ينتفع الناطق بهما.
It has become clear to you that the two words of testimony encompass all the preceding beliefs. Perhaps it is for this meaning, despite their brevity, that the Lawgiver made them a translation of what is in the heart of faith, and He does not accept faith from anyone except with them if he is able to utter them. And the scholars have explicitly stated that it is necessary to understand their meaning, even if summarily, otherwise the speaker does not benefit from them.
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a statement about the two testimonies (kalimatay al-shahada). The author points out that they encompass all the previously mentioned beliefs. Despite being brief, the Lawgiver (al-Shari') made them the expression of inner faith (iman). No one's faith is accepted without uttering them if able. The scholars affirm that understanding their meaning, even in a general sense, is essential; otherwise, mere utterance is not beneficial. Thus, comprehension is a condition for the shahada to be valid faith.

Key Terms

الإيمان
فهم المعنى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that merely pronouncing the shahada is enough for faith.
Correction: The passage explicitly states that understanding the meaning, even summarily, is necessary; otherwise, the speaker does not benefit. So mere utterance is insufficient.

Key Takeaway
The two testimonies are the foundation of faith, but they only benefit the one who understands their meaning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?

?
The shahada is the translation of what is in your heart. If someone examined your actions and beliefs, would they see that your heart truly declares what your tongue utters?

The Foundations of Tawakkul
Hadith, saying, and preference of rich grateful over poor patient.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the encouragement to cut off to Allah, the meaning of true tawakkul as exemplified by Sulayman al-Khawwas, and the preference of the rich grateful over the poor patient.

Core Idea
True tawakkul makes one independent of creation and brings Allah's sufficiency.

The commentator begins by citing a powerful hadith about relying solely on Allah, then reinforces it with a saying from a renowned ascetic, and finally highlights the author's preference for the grateful rich over the patient poor. This sets the stage for a nuanced discussion about the relationship between reliance and earning.

Guided Path
1
Read the hadith and its translation
Read the Arabic hadith from al-Quda'i once without over-analyzing. Then read the literal translation to grasp the promise of sufficiency for those who cut off to Allah.
Notice the contrast between cutting off to Allah vs. to the world.
2
Reflect on the saying of al-Khawwas
Consider the profound statement: if one truly relied on Allah, even princes would need him. Ask yourself what this says about the power of sincere tawakkul.
This ties to the rich/poor discussion later.
3
Understand the preference between rich grateful and poor patient
The author of the poem (and commentator) preponderates the rich grateful over the poor patient. Think about why gratitude with wealth might be superior to patience in poverty.
This preference is further detailed in the next lesson.
4
Prepare for the detailed view
End by reflecting on how these foundations set up the need for a detailed classification of tawakkul vs. kasb.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقد أخرج القضاعيُّ: مَنِ انقطعَ إِلى اللهِ كفاهُ كلَّ مُوْنَةٍ، ورزقه من حيث لا يحتسب، ومَن انقطع إلى الدنيا وَكَلَهُ اللهُ إليها ) ، قال سليمان الخواص : لو أن رجلاً توكَّل على الله بصدق النية لاحتاج إليه الأمراء ومن دونهم، وكيف يحتاج هو إلى أحدٍ ومولاه الغني الحميد؟ وفي شرح المصنف ترجيح تفضيل الغني الشاكر على الفقير الصابر. وقوله : (والرَّاجِحُ التَّفْصِيلُ حَسْبَمَا عُرِفْ أي والراجح القول بالتفصيل، حسبما عرف من كتب القوم ؛ كـ «الإحياء» للغزالي، و«الرسالة» للقشيري . وحاصلُ التفصيل أنهما يختلفان باختلاف أحوال الناس، فمن يصبر عند ضيق معيشته بحيث لا يتسخط ولا يتطلَّع لسؤال أحد فالتوكل في حقه أرجح، لما فيه من مجاهدة النفس على ترك شهواتها ولذاتها والصبر على شدتها، ومن لم يكن كذلك فالاكتساب حقه أرجح حذراً من التسخط وعدم الصبر، بل ربما وجب الاكتساب في حقه، وهذا كله إنما يتمشى على أن التوكل ينافي الكسب، كما هو طريقة أبي جعفر الطبري ومن وافقه، بخلافه على طريقة الجمهور وهو أن التوكل لا ينافي الكسب، فقد يكون متوكلاً، وهو : يكتسب ؛ لأن حقيقة التوكل على هذه الطريقة الثقة بالله تعالى والاعتماد عليه، واعتقاد أن الأمر منه وإليه ، ولو مع مباشرة الأسباب كما كان يفعله (۲) فائدةٌ : قال الغزالي: (أخذُ الزاد في السفر بنية عون المسلم أفضل، والأفضل تركه لمنفرد قوي القلب يشغله الزاد عن عبادة الله . وقد كان المصطفى وأصحابه والسلف الصالح يحملون الزاد بنيات الخير (۱) ذكره الحكيم (١٣/٤) ، وأخرجه البيهقي في شعب الإيمان) (۱۲۰/۲) . وأخرجه أيضاً : الطبراني في الأوسط» (٣٤٦/٣). قال الهيثمي (۳۰۳/۱۰) : وفيه إبراهيم بن الأشعث صاحب الفضيل، وهو ضعيف، وقد ذكره ابن حبان في الثقات وقال : يغرب ويخطئ ويخالف وبقية رجاله ثقات وفي الصغير» (۲۰۱/۱)، والشهاب القضاعي في المسند (۲۹۸/۱). قاله العراقي في تخريج أحاديث الإحياء»، كتاب التوحيد (٣٠١/٤) . (٢) أخرج الترمذي (۲۵۱۷) عن أنس رضي الله عنه : قال رجل: يا رسول الله أعقلها وأتوكل أو أطلقها وأتوكل ؟ قال : اعقلها وتوكل لا لميل قلوبهم إلى الزاد عن الله تعالى والمعتبرُ القصد، فكم حامل زاداً وقلبه مع الله، وكم تارك زاداً وقلبه مع الزاد والدخول في البوادي بلا زاد توكلاً بدعةٌ لم تُنقل عن أحدٍ من السلف؛ لأنه مخاطرة بالروح، وقد قال تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تُلْقُوا بِأَيْدِيكُمْ إِلَى التَهْلُكَةِ [البقرة: ١٩٥) .
Al-Quda'i reported: Whoever cuts himself off to God, God suffices him all need and provides him from where he does not expect, and whoever cuts himself off to this world, God entrusts him to it. Sulayman al-Khawwas said: If a man relied on God with sincere intention, the princes and those below them would need him; how would he need anyone while his Master is the Rich, the Praiseworthy? And in the commentary of the author there is a preponderance of preferring the rich grateful one over the poor patient one. And his saying: 'And the preponderant is the detailed view, as is known' meaning the preponderant is the detailed statement, as is known from the books of the people, such as al-Ghazali's Ihya and al-Qushayri's Risala. The summary of the detail is that the two [states] differ according to the different conditions of people. Whoever is patient in straitened circumstances such that he does not complain nor seek from anyone, then tawakkul is preponderant for him, because of the struggle of the soul in leaving its desires and pleasures and patience in its severity. Whoever is not like that, then earning is preponderant for him, out of caution against complaining and lack of patience. Rather, earning might become obligatory for him. All this proceeds on the basis that tawakkul is incompatible with earning, as is the way of Abu Ja'far al-Tabari and those who agree with him. Contrary to the way of the majority, which is that tawakkul is not incompatible with earning, so one can be mutawakkil while he earns. For the reality of tawakkul according to this way is trust in God Almighty and reliance upon Him, and the belief that the matter is from Him and to Him, even while directly undertaking the means, as he used to do. (2) Benefit: al-Ghazali said: 'Taking provisions on a journey with the intention of helping a Muslim is better, and leaving them is better for a solitary person of strong heart whose provisions distract him from the worship of God.' And the Chosen One (the Prophet) and his Companions and the righteous predecessors used to carry provisions with good intentions. (1) Mentioned by al-Hakim (4/13) and al-Bayhaqi in Shu'ab al-Iman (2/120). Also al-Tabarani in al-Awsat (3/346). Al-Haythami said (10/303): In it is Ibrahim ibn al-Ash'ath, companion of al-Fudayl, and he is weak, but Ibn Hibban mentioned him in al-Thiqat and said: He is gharib, makes errors, and contradicts; the rest of his narrators are trustworthy. And in al-Saghir (1/201) and al-Shihab al-Quda'i in al-Musnad (1/298). Al-Iraqi said in his Takhrij of Ihya, Book of Tawhid (4/301). (2) Al-Tirmidhi (2517) narrated from Anas (may God be pleased with him): A man said: O Messenger of God, should I tie her and rely, or let her go and rely? He said: Tie her and rely. Not because of the inclination of their hearts towards provision away from God Almighty, and what matters is the intention. How many a carrier of provisions while his heart is with God, and how many a leave of provisions while his heart is with the provisions. Entering the deserts without provisions as tawakkul is an innovation not transmitted from any of the Salaf, because it is a risk to the soul, and God Almighty said: 'And do not throw yourselves into destruction' [al-Baqara: 195].
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the relationship between tawakkul (reliance on God) and kasb (earning a livelihood). The commentator begins by citing a hadith from al-Quda'i about relying on God. Then he quotes Sulayman al-Khawwas on the benefits of tawakkul. The commentator then mentions the preference of the author (of the poem) for the rich grateful over the poor patient. He then explains the saying 'the preponderant is the detailed view', i.e., a detailed approach is taken from books like al-Ghazali's Ihya and al-Qushayri's Risala. The detailed view is that the preference between tawakkul and earning depends on the person's state: if a person can patiently endure hardship without complaining or seeking from others, tawakkul is better because it involves struggling against the desires. If not, earning is better to avoid complaint. Sometimes earning may become obligatory. This detailed view is based on the opinion of Abu Ja'far al-Tabari, who holds that tawakkul is incompatible with earning. However, the majority (jumhur) holds that tawakkul is not incompatible with earning; one can be trusting while earning, because the reality of tawakkul is trust in God and belief that the outcome is from Him, even while using means. The commentator then cites a benefit from al-Ghazali about taking provisions on a journey and mentions that the Prophet and Salaf carried provisions with good intentions. He includes a footnote verifying a hadith chain. He then continues with a saying: entering deserts without provisions as tawakkul is an innovation because it risks the soul, citing the Quranic verse against self-destruction. The passage thus covers both the theoretical classification and practical guidance.

Key Terms
توكل (tawakkul)
صبر (sabr)
كسب (kasb)
غني شاكر (ghani shakir)
فقير صابر (faqir sabir)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that tawakkul means passivity and rejecting all worldly means.
Correction: The hadith and the preference show that tawakkul leads to Allah's provision, but the preference for the rich grateful indicates that wealth is not inherently bad; gratitude elevates it.

Checkpoint
According to the hadith cited in this passage, what happens to the person who cuts himself off to Allah?
A) He becomes poor and dependent on others.
B) Allah suffices him all need and provides from unexpected sources.
C) He must abandon all earning.
D) He is left to the world's trials.

Key Takeaway
Sincere reliance on Allah brings His sufficiency and independence from creation, and gratitude with wealth can be superior to patience in poverty.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
This lesson tells you that whoever cuts himself off to Allah will be sufficed all needs. Look at your own life: what is one attachment to the world that you are holding onto because you doubt Allah's sufficiency? What specific step can you take today to sever that attachment and rely on Him alone?
?
Sulayman al-Khawwas said that a true mutawakkil would be needed by princes. Search your heart: do you live in a way that others need you because of your reliance on Allah, or do you find yourself needing others for validation and provision? What would change in your daily life if you truly believed that Allah's sufficiency makes you independent of everyone?
?
The author prefers the rich grateful over the poor patient. Be honest: if you were wealthy, would you be truly grateful, or would you be distracted? Which state—gratitude or patience—do you find easier right now, and why? What is one practical way you can cultivate sincere gratitude today, regardless of your financial situation?

The Detailed View on Tawakkul and Kasb
Detailed view (tafsil), two opinions on compatibility, and practical guidance with warning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the detailed classification of when tawakkul is preferred over earning, the two scholarly positions on their compatibility, and the practical guidance on provisions and reckless tawakkul.

Core Idea
Whether tawakkul or earning is better depends on one's spiritual state, and tawakkul does not necessarily preclude earning.

After stating the preference for the rich grateful, the commentator now expounds the detailed view that the best course varies from person to person. He also contrasts the opinion that tawakkul and earning are incompatible with the majority view that they can coexist, and then provides practical guidance from al-Ghazali and a warning against reckless tawakkul.

Guided Path
1
Read the detailed view (tafsil)
Read the passage explaining the two conditions: the patient poor (tawakkul preferred) and the impatient (earning preferred or obligatory).
Note that this view assumes incompatibility between tawakkul and earning.
2
Contrast the two scholarly opinions
Compare the opinion of Abu Ja'far al-Tabari (incompatibility) with that of the majority (compatibility). Understand the basis for each.
The majority defines tawakkul as trust in Allah while using means.
3
Learn from al-Ghazali's benefit on provisions
Read the example of taking provisions on a journey. Note the nuance: carrying provisions can be better or worse depending on the person's heart.
The Prophet and Salaf carried provisions with good intentions.
4
Understand the warning against reckless tawakkul
Read the final part: entering the desert without provisions is an innovation and a risk to life, forbidden by the Quran.
This corrects the extreme view of abandoning all means.

وقد أخرج القضاعيُّ: مَنِ انقطعَ إِلى اللهِ كفاهُ كلَّ مُوْنَةٍ، ورزقه من حيث لا يحتسب، ومَن انقطع إلى الدنيا وَكَلَهُ اللهُ إليها ) ، قال سليمان الخواص : لو أن رجلاً توكَّل على الله بصدق النية لاحتاج إليه الأمراء ومن دونهم، وكيف يحتاج هو إلى أحدٍ ومولاه الغني الحميد؟ وفي شرح المصنف ترجيح تفضيل الغني الشاكر على الفقير الصابر. وقوله : (والرَّاجِحُ التَّفْصِيلُ حَسْبَمَا عُرِفْ أي والراجح القول بالتفصيل، حسبما عرف من كتب القوم ؛ كـ «الإحياء» للغزالي، و«الرسالة» للقشيري . وحاصلُ التفصيل أنهما يختلفان باختلاف أحوال الناس، فمن يصبر عند ضيق معيشته بحيث لا يتسخط ولا يتطلَّع لسؤال أحد فالتوكل في حقه أرجح، لما فيه من مجاهدة النفس على ترك شهواتها ولذاتها والصبر على شدتها، ومن لم يكن كذلك فالاكتساب حقه أرجح حذراً من التسخط وعدم الصبر، بل ربما وجب الاكتساب في حقه، وهذا كله إنما يتمشى على أن التوكل ينافي الكسب، كما هو طريقة أبي جعفر الطبري ومن وافقه، بخلافه على طريقة الجمهور وهو أن التوكل لا ينافي الكسب، فقد يكون متوكلاً، وهو : يكتسب ؛ لأن حقيقة التوكل على هذه الطريقة الثقة بالله تعالى والاعتماد عليه، واعتقاد أن الأمر منه وإليه ، ولو مع مباشرة الأسباب كما كان يفعله (۲) فائدةٌ : قال الغزالي: (أخذُ الزاد في السفر بنية عون المسلم أفضل، والأفضل تركه لمنفرد قوي القلب يشغله الزاد عن عبادة الله . وقد كان المصطفى وأصحابه والسلف الصالح يحملون الزاد بنيات الخير (۱) ذكره الحكيم (١٣/٤) ، وأخرجه البيهقي في شعب الإيمان) (۱۲۰/۲) . وأخرجه أيضاً : الطبراني في الأوسط» (٣٤٦/٣). قال الهيثمي (۳۰۳/۱۰) : وفيه إبراهيم بن الأشعث صاحب الفضيل، وهو ضعيف، وقد ذكره ابن حبان في الثقات وقال : يغرب ويخطئ ويخالف وبقية رجاله ثقات وفي الصغير» (۲۰۱/۱)، والشهاب القضاعي في المسند (۲۹۸/۱). قاله العراقي في تخريج أحاديث الإحياء»، كتاب التوحيد (٣٠١/٤) . (٢) أخرج الترمذي (۲۵۱۷) عن أنس رضي الله عنه : قال رجل: يا رسول الله أعقلها وأتوكل أو أطلقها وأتوكل ؟ قال : اعقلها وتوكل لا لميل قلوبهم إلى الزاد عن الله تعالى والمعتبرُ القصد، فكم حامل زاداً وقلبه مع الله، وكم تارك زاداً وقلبه مع الزاد والدخول في البوادي بلا زاد توكلاً بدعةٌ لم تُنقل عن أحدٍ من السلف؛ لأنه مخاطرة بالروح، وقد قال تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تُلْقُوا بِأَيْدِيكُمْ إِلَى التَهْلُكَةِ [البقرة: ١٩٥) .
Al-Quda'i reported: Whoever cuts himself off to God, God suffices him all need and provides him from where he does not expect, and whoever cuts himself off to this world, God entrusts him to it. Sulayman al-Khawwas said: If a man relied on God with sincere intention, the princes and those below them would need him; how would he need anyone while his Master is the Rich, the Praiseworthy? And in the commentary of the author there is a preponderance of preferring the rich grateful one over the poor patient one. And his saying: 'And the preponderant is the detailed view, as is known' meaning the preponderant is the detailed statement, as is known from the books of the people, such as al-Ghazali's Ihya and al-Qushayri's Risala. The summary of the detail is that the two [states] differ according to the different conditions of people. Whoever is patient in straitened circumstances such that he does not complain nor seek from anyone, then tawakkul is preponderant for him, because of the struggle of the soul in leaving its desires and pleasures and patience in its severity. Whoever is not like that, then earning is preponderant for him, out of caution against complaining and lack of patience. Rather, earning might become obligatory for him. All this proceeds on the basis that tawakkul is incompatible with earning, as is the way of Abu Ja'far al-Tabari and those who agree with him. Contrary to the way of the majority, which is that tawakkul is not incompatible with earning, so one can be mutawakkil while he earns. For the reality of tawakkul according to this way is trust in God Almighty and reliance upon Him, and the belief that the matter is from Him and to Him, even while directly undertaking the means, as he used to do. (2) Benefit: al-Ghazali said: 'Taking provisions on a journey with the intention of helping a Muslim is better, and leaving them is better for a solitary person of strong heart whose provisions distract him from the worship of God.' And the Chosen One (the Prophet) and his Companions and the righteous predecessors used to carry provisions with good intentions. (1) Mentioned by al-Hakim (4/13) and al-Bayhaqi in Shu'ab al-Iman (2/120). Also al-Tabarani in al-Awsat (3/346). Al-Haythami said (10/303): In it is Ibrahim ibn al-Ash'ath, companion of al-Fudayl, and he is weak, but Ibn Hibban mentioned him in al-Thiqat and said: He is gharib, makes errors, and contradicts; the rest of his narrators are trustworthy. And in al-Saghir (1/201) and al-Shihab al-Quda'i in al-Musnad (1/298). Al-Iraqi said in his Takhrij of Ihya, Book of Tawhid (4/301). (2) Al-Tirmidhi (2517) narrated from Anas (may God be pleased with him): A man said: O Messenger of God, should I tie her and rely, or let her go and rely? He said: Tie her and rely. Not because of the inclination of their hearts towards provision away from God Almighty, and what matters is the intention. How many a carrier of provisions while his heart is with God, and how many a leave of provisions while his heart is with the provisions. Entering the deserts without provisions as tawakkul is an innovation not transmitted from any of the Salaf, because it is a risk to the soul, and God Almighty said: 'And do not throw yourselves into destruction' [al-Baqara: 195].
Source pages p. 389

Commentary
This passage is a detailed discussion on the relationship between tawakkul (reliance on God) and kasb (earning a livelihood). The commentator begins by citing a hadith from al-Quda'i about relying on God. Then he quotes Sulayman al-Khawwas on the benefits of tawakkul. The commentator then mentions the preference of the author (of the poem) for the rich grateful over the poor patient. He then explains the saying 'the preponderant is the detailed view', i.e., a detailed approach is taken from books like al-Ghazali's Ihya and al-Qushayri's Risala. The detailed view is that the preference between tawakkul and earning depends on the person's state: if a person can patiently endure hardship without complaining or seeking from others, tawakkul is better because it involves struggling against the desires. If not, earning is better to avoid complaint. Sometimes earning may become obligatory. This detailed view is based on the opinion of Abu Ja'far al-Tabari, who holds that tawakkul is incompatible with earning. However, the majority (jumhur) holds that tawakkul is not incompatible with earning; one can be trusting while earning, because the reality of tawakkul is trust in God and belief that the outcome is from Him, even while using means. The commentator then cites a benefit from al-Ghazali about taking provisions on a journey and mentions that the Prophet and Salaf carried provisions with good intentions. He includes a footnote verifying a hadith chain. He then continues with a saying: entering deserts without provisions as tawakkul is an innovation because it risks the soul, citing the Quranic verse against self-destruction. The passage thus covers both the theoretical classification and practical guidance.

Key Terms
تفصيل (tafsil)
توكل (tawakkul)
كسب (kasb)
الثقة بالله (thiqah bi Allah)
بدعة (bid'ah)
مخاطرة (mukhatarah)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Tawakkul requires abandoning all worldly means and earning.
Correction: The majority view holds that tawakkul is trust in Allah and is compatible with earning; reckless abandonment is bid'ah.

Checkpoint
According to the majority view presented in this passage, what is the reality of tawakkul?
A) It is incompatible with earning a livelihood.
B) It is trust in Allah and reliance on Him while using means.
C) It requires leaving all provisions behind.
D) It is only for the poor and patient.

Key Takeaway
The detailed view shows that the preference between tawakkul and earning depends on one's patience, and the majority allows both, but reckless tawakkul is prohibited.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you face financial difficulty, do you find yourself complaining or seeking help from others as a first resort, rather than turning to Allah? What does the detailed view say about your state?
?
Have you ever used 'tawakkul' as an excuse to avoid responsibility, such as not taking proper means in your work or studies? How does the hadith of tying the camel challenge you?
?
Consider your heart: are you more attached to your provisions or to Allah? How many times have you planned a journey or project without considering the intention? What would it mean for you to carry provisions with the intention of helping others while keeping your heart with Allah?

Classification of Sins: Minor and Major
The author divides sins into minor and major and refutes three opposing groups.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Sunni classification of sins into minor and major, and how this differs from the positions of the Murji'ah, Khawarij, and those who deem all sins as major due to God's majesty.

Core Idea
Sins are not all equal — Islam distinguishes minor from major, avoiding excesses of the Murji'ah and Khawarij.

This passage tackles a crucial point in Islamic theology: the classification of sins. The author, following Ahl al-Sunnah, affirms that sins are of two kinds — minor and major — and then refutes three opposing views that either minimize or exaggerate sin's consequences. Understanding this balanced position is essential for grasping Sunni soteriology.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic and translation carefully, noting the key terms: صغائر and كبائر.
2
Identify the Sunni position
The passage states that sins are two types according to the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah. Recognize this as the mainstream view.
3
Learn the Murji'ah position
The Murji'ah held that all sins are minor and do not harm faith. See how the author refutes them with a poem.
4
Learn the Khawarij position
The Khawarij held that all sins are major and every major sin is kufr. Note the refutation.
5
Consider the third group
A third group said all sins are major due to God's majesty, but only specific acts cause kufr. Understand the nuance.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
١٢ - ثُمَّ الذُّنُوبُ عِنْدَنَا قِسْمَانِ صَغِيرَةٌ كَبِيرَةٌ فَالثَّانِي قوله : (ثُمَّ الذُّنُوبُ عِنْدَنَا قِسْمَانِ) أي: ثم الذنوب عند جمهور أهل السنة قسمان : صغائر وكبائر، كما سيذكره، خلافاً للمُرْجِئة حيث ذهبوا إلى أنها كلَّها صغائر، ولا تضرُّ مرتكبها ما دام على الإسلام، ولذلك قال شاعرهم : [من الكامل] مُسْلِماً ومِنَ الذُّنُوبِ فَلَا تَخَفْ حَاشَا المُهَيْمِنَ أَنْ يُرِي تَنْكِيدًا لَوْ رَامَ أَنْ يُصْلِيْكَ نَارَ جَهَنَّمِ مَا كَانَ أَلْهَمَ قَلْبَكَ التَّوْحِيدا وخلافاً للخوارج حيث ذهبوا إلى أنها كلها كبائر، وأن كل كبيرةٍ كُفْرٌ، وخلافاً لمن ذهب إلى أنها كلها كبائر نظراً لعظمة من عُصي بها، ولكن لا يكفر مرتكبها إلا بما هو كفر منها : كسجود لصنم، ورمي مصحف في قاذورة، ونحو ذلك .
12 - Then sins according to us are two types: minor and major, and the second... His statement: (Then sins according to us are two types) meaning: then sins according to the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah are two types: minor and major, as he will mention, contrary to the Murji'ah, who held that all of them are minor and do not harm the committer as long as he remains upon Islam. For that reason one of their poets said: [Complete meter] "A Muslim? Then from sins do not fear; far be it that the Sovereign should show hardship. If He intended to burn you in Hellfire, He would not have inspired your heart with tawhīd." And contrary to the Khawarij, who held that all of them are major and that every major is disbelief (kufr), and contrary to those who held that all of them are major in view of the majesty of the One who is disobeyed, but the committer does not disbelieve except by that which is disbelief among them, like prostrating to an idol, throwing a Quran into a filthy place, and the like.
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage classifies sins according to Ahl al-Sunnah. The verse states that sins are two kinds: minor and major. The commentary clarifies that this is the position of the majority of Ahl al-Sunnah, and then refutes three opposing groups: (1) The Murji'ah, who consider all sins as minor and that they do not harm the believer as long as faith remains; they are refuted by quoting a poem that exaggerates hope. (2) The Khawarij, who consider all sins as major and that every major sin is kufr (disbelief). (3) A third group who consider all sins as major due to the greatness of the One disobeyed, but they do not declare the committer a disbeliever unless the act itself constitutes disbelief, such as idolatry or defiling the Quran. The passage emphasizes the nuanced Sunni position that recognizes two categories of sin and carefully defines the conditions for excommunication.

Key Terms
الذنوب
صغائر
كبائر
المرجئة
الخوارج

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think Islam teaches that all sins are equally forgiven or equally damnable, ignoring the distinction between minor and major.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunnah affirms two categories of sin, avoiding the extremes of the Murji'ah (all minor) and Khawarij (all major = kufr).

Checkpoint
What is the position of the Murji'ah regarding sins as described in this passage?
A) All sins are major and lead to kufr
B) All sins are minor and do not harm the believer
C) Sins are divided into minor and major
D) Sins are forgiven without repentance

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunnah holds a middle ground: sins are either minor or major, and not all major sins constitute disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you tend to dismiss it as minor and feel safe because of your iman, or do you become overwhelmed with guilt as if you have committed kufr? Which of these extremes does the lesson warn against, and how does your heart lean?
?
The Murji'ah poet said not to fear sins as long as you have tawhīd. Have you ever used your faith as an excuse to be careless about sin? What would it mean to take sin seriously without losing hope in Allah's mercy?
?
The third group argued that any disobedience to God is major because of who He is. Do you treat all your sins with equal seriousness, or do you downplay some? How can you maintain reverence for God without falling into despair?

Sins: Minor and Major — Refuting False Views
The commentator divides sins into minor and major, refuting Murji'ah and Khawarij.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that Ahl al-Sunna divides sins into minor and major, and how this corrects both the extreme hope of the Murji'ah and the extreme fear of the Khawarij.

Core Idea
Sins are not all the same; the middle path avoids false extremes.

The commentator now addresses the classification of sins, a topic that separates Ahl al-Sunna from two extremist sects. Understanding that sins are not uniform helps maintain a balanced view of God's mercy and justice. This passage lays out the Sunni position and refutes the Murji'ah and Khawarij.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without pausing. Then read the translation. Let the author's own words come through before you analyse.
The passage has a clear three-part refutation structure.
2
Identify the three positions
Find the Sunni position, then the Murji'ah position, then the Khawarij position, and finally a third group. Notice how the commentator refutes each.
3
Reflect on the balance
Ask yourself why the middle position of Ahl al-Sunna is important for maintaining both hope in Allah's mercy and fear of His punishment.
This connects to the learning objective.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثُمَّ الذُّنُوبُ عِنْدَنَا قِسْمَانِ صَغِيرَةٌ كَبِيرَةٌ فَالثَّانِي
قوله : (ثُمَّ الذُّنُوبُ عِنْدَنَا قِسْمَانِ) أي: ثم الذنوب عند جمهور أهل السنة قسمان : صغائر وكبائر، كما سيذكره، خلافاً للمُرْجِئة حيث ذهبوا إلى أنها كلَّها صغائر، ولا تضرُّ مرتكبها ما دام على الإسلام، ولذلك قال شاعرهم : [من الكامل] مُسْلِماً ومِنَ الذُّنُوبِ فَلَا تَخَفْ حَاشَا المُهَيْمِنَ أَنْ يُرِي تَنْكِيدًا لَوْ رَامَ أَنْ يُصْلِيْكَ نَارَ جَهَنَّمِ مَا كَانَ أَلْهَمَ قَلْبَكَ التَّوْحِيدا وخلافاً للخوارج حيث ذهبوا إلى أنها كلها كبائر، وأن كل كبيرةٍ كُفْرٌ، وخلافاً لمن ذهب إلى أنها كلها كبائر نظراً لعظمة من عُصي بها، ولكن لا يكفر مرتكبها إلا بما هو كفر منها : كسجود لصنم، ورمي مصحف في قاذورة، ونحو ذلك .
الإرجاء على معنيين؛ أحدهما بمعنى التأخير، والثاني إعطاء الرجاء، وأما إطلاق اسم المرجئة على الجماعة بالمعنى الأول فصحيح؛ لأنهم كانوا يؤخّرون العمل عن النية والعقد، وأما بالمعنى الثاني فظاهر؛ لأنهم يقولون : لا تضرُّ مع الإيمان معصية، كما لا تنفع مع الكفر طاعة . وقيل : الإرجاء تأخير حكم صاحب الكبيرة إلى يوم القيامة . انظر الملل والنحل» (۱۳۹/۱).
Then sins according to us are two types: minor and major, and the second. His statement: 'Then sins according to us are two types' means: then sins according to the majority of Ahl al-Sunna are two types: minor and major, as he will mention, contrary to the Murji'ah who held that they are all minor and do not harm their committer as long as he remains upon Islam. Therefore their poet said: 'Being Muslim, from sins do not fear; far be it that the All-Protecting should cause you distress. If He intended to burn you in Hellfire, He would not have inspired your heart with tawhid.' And contrary to the Khawarij who held that they are all major, and that every major sin is disbelief. And contrary to those who held that they are all major considering the greatness of the One disobeyed, but its committer does not become a disbeliever except by what is disbelief among them, like prostration to an idol, throwing a Quran into a filthy place, and the like. Al-Irja' has two meanings: one meaning is postponement, and the second is giving hope. As for applying the name Murji'ah to the group in the first sense, it is correct because they used to postpone action from intention and commitment. As for the second sense, it is apparent because they say: 'Disobedience does not harm with faith, just as obedience does not benefit with disbelief.' And it was said: Al-irja' is postponing the judgment of the committer of a major sin until the Day of Resurrection. See al-Milal wa al-Nihal (1/139).
Source pages p. 393

Commentary
This passage is a classification and refutation. The commentator first states that sins are divided into two types: minor and major, contrary to the Murji'ah who consider all sins as minor and harmless as long as one has faith, citing a poem from one of them. Then he refutes the Khawarij who consider all sins as major and equate major sin with disbelief. He also mentions a third group who consider all sins major due to the majesty of the One disobeyed, but they do not declare the committer a disbeliever except for specifically disbelief acts. The footnote explains the term 'irja'' (postponement) and why the Murji'ah are so named: either because they postpone action from intention or because they give hope that sin does not harm with faith.

Key Terms
ذنوب (sins)
صغائر (minor sins)
كبائر (major sins)
مرجئة (Murji'ah)
خوارج (Khawarij)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: The Murji'ah belief that sins (including major ones) do not harm the believer as long as he has faith.
Correction: Ahl al-Sunna holds that while faith ultimately saves a believer from eternal punishment, sins do harm and may lead to punishment in Hell, and major sins require repentance.

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the position of the Khawarij on sins?
A) All sins are minor
B) All sins are major and every major sin is disbelief
C) Major sins do not harm the believer
D) Sins are of two types only

Key Takeaway
Ahl al-Sunna holds a balanced position: sins vary in gravity, and not every major sin is disbelief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you disobey Allah, do you tend to minimize the sin (like the Murji'ah) or fall into despair and doubt your faith (like the Khawarij)? Which tendency is stronger in your heart, and what would it mean for you to embrace the balanced view of Ahl al-Sunna in your daily repentance?
?
The Murji'ah poet felt secure in his tawhid, assuming sins don't matter. Examine your own life: are there sins you commit while feeling 'safe' because you believe you have faith? How can you cultivate true fear of Allah's displeasure without losing hope in His mercy?
?
The third group considered all sins major due to the greatness of the One disobeyed. Do you treat your small sins as trivial, or do you recognize that any disobedience is serious because of Who you are disobeying? What change would acknowledging this make in your daily awareness of Allah?

Definition and Indicators of Major Sins
Sanusi defines major sins and lists their indicators with examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how major sins are defined, their key indicators, and the principle that they vary in gravity.

Core Idea
Major sins are identified by clear signs, not by a fixed number.

Before we can distinguish between major and minor sins, we need a clear definition and reliable indicators. This lesson presents Ibn al-Salah's definition and four concrete signs that help identify major sins, along with examples of the gravest ones.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition of major sins
Start by reading the Arabic passage that defines major sins according to Ibn al-Salah. Notice that the definition is qualitative (based on magnitude), not quantitative.
The definition is: 'every sin that is great in magnitude such that it is correct to call it a major sin.'
2
Learn the four indicators
The passage lists four indicators that a sin is major: prescribed punishment, explicit threat, describing the doer as fasiq, and a divine curse. Study each one with its Quranic or hadith evidence.
The indicators are not exhaustive but serve as clear markers.
3
Understand the greatest major sins
Shirk and unjust killing are highlighted as the greatest. Then the commentator explains that other major sins can vary in gravity depending on circumstances.
When a sin is called 'the greatest', it often means 'among the greatest'.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وقوله : (صَغِيْرَةٌ كَبِيرَةٌ) بدل من قوله : (قسمان للتفصيل، وفيه حذف العاطف، والأصل: صغيرة وكبيرة، وليست الكبيرة منحصرةً في عدد.
وهي كما قال ابن الصلاح كل ذنبٍ كَبُر كِبَراً يصح معه أن يطلق عليه اسم الكبيرة، ولها أمارات منها إيجابُ الحدّ (۱) ، ومنها الإيعاد عليها بالعقاب (۲)، ومنها وصف فاعلها بالفسق (۳)، ومنها اللعن كلعن الله السارق (4) ، وأكبرها الشرك(ه) بالله، ثم قتل النفس التي حرَّم الله قتلها إلا بالحق ؛ وما سوى هذين منها كالزنا واللواط وعقوق الوالدين والسحر والقذف والفرار يوم الزحف وأكل الربا وغير ذلك، فيختلفُ أمرها باختلاف الأحوال والمفاسد المترتبة عليها ؛ فيقال لكل واحدة منها هي من أكبر الكبائر، وإن جاء في موضع أنها أكبر الكبائر، كان المراد منه أنها من أكبر الكبائر، كما قاله النووي.
(٦) ومن أكبر الكبائر أيضاً الكذب على رسول الله ) ، بل قال الشيخ أبو محمد الجويني: إن من تعمد الكذب عليه يكفر كُفراً يخرجه عن الملة، وتبعه على ذلك طائفة، وهو ضعيف .
وكل ما خرج عن حد الكبيرة وضابطها فهو صغيرة، وقد تُعطى حكم الكبيرة، لا أنها تنقلب كبيرةً، كما قاله ابن حجر في شرح الأربعين النووية»، وإن وقع في عبارة بعضهم أنها تنقلب كبيرةً بالإصرار عليها ؛ وهو معاودة الذنب مع نية العود إليه عند الفعل، فإن عاوده من غير نية العود لم يكن إصراراً على الأصح.
(1) كالقطع في سرقة ؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿ فَأَقْطَعُوا أَيْدِيَهُمَا ﴾ [المائدة: ۳۸]، والجَلْد لقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاجَلِدُوا كل وتهدر منهما مأنة جلد [النور: ٢].
(۲) كقوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَن يَقْتُلْ مُؤْمِنًا مُّتَعَمِّدًا فَجَزَاؤُهُ جَهَنَّمُ خَلدا فيها وَغَضِبَ الله عليه وَلَعَنَهُ ﴾ [النِّسَاء : ٩٣ ] .
(۳) كقوله تعالى: (وَالَّذِينَ يَرْمُونَ الْمُحْصَنَتِ ثُمَّ لَمْ يَأْتُوا بِأَرْبَعَةِ شُهَدَاءَ فَاجْلِدُوهُمْ ثَمَانِينَ جَلْدَةً وَلَا تَقْبَلُوا لَهُمْ شَهَادَةً ابداً وَأُولَئِكَ هُمُ الْفَاسِقُونَ) [النور: ٤].
(4) أخرجه البخاري (٦٤٠١) : لعن الله السارق يسرق البيضة فتقطع يده ويسرق الحبل فتقطع يده .
(5) في (أ) و (ب) و (ج) : (الكفر) .
(1) أخرجه البخاري (۱۰۷) ، ومسلم (۳) : من كذب علي فليتبوأ مقعده من الناره .
And His statement: 'Minor major' is a substitute for His statement: 'two types' for detailing, and there is a deletion of the conjunction, the original being: minor and major. And the major is not confined to a number. It is, as Ibn al-Salah said: every sin that is great in magnitude such that it is correct to call it a major sin. It has indicators: one is the imposition of a prescribed legal punishment; another is the threat of punishment for it; another is describing its doer as sinful (fasiq); another is cursing, like God's cursing of the thief. And the greatest of them is associating partners with God (shirk), then killing a soul that God has forbidden to kill except by right. Whatever besides these two, like adultery, sodomy, disobedience to parents, sorcery, slander, fleeing from battle, usury, and others, their status differs according to different circumstances and the evil consequences entailed. So each of them may be said to be among the major sins, and if it comes in a place that it is the greatest of major sins, what is meant is that it is among the greatest of the great sins, as al-Nawawi said. Among the greatest of the great sins also is lying about the Messenger of God. Rather, Shaykh Abu Muhammad al-Juwayni said: whoever deliberately lies about him commits disbelief that removes him from the religion. A group followed him on that, but it is weak. And whatever falls outside the boundary and standard of a major sin is a minor sin. It may be given the ruling of a major sin, not that it actually becomes a major sin, as Ibn Hajar said in Sharh al-Arba'in al-Nawawiyya. And if it occurs in the statement of some that it becomes a major sin by persistence (israr), that is: repeating the sin with the intention to return to it at the time of action. If one repeats it without intention to return, it is not considered persistence according to the most correct view. (1) Like cutting for theft, due to His saying: 'Cut off their hands' [al-Ma'ida: 38], and flogging due to His saying: 'flog each of them one hundred lashes' [al-Nur: 2]. (2) Like His saying: 'And whoever kills a believer intentionally, his recompense is Hell, abiding therein, and God has become angry with him and cursed him' [al-Nisa: 93]. (3) Like His saying: 'And those who accuse chaste women then do not bring four witnesses, flog them eighty lashes and never accept their testimony, and they are the sinful' [al-Nur: 4]. (4) Reported by al-Bukhari (6401): 'God curses the thief who steals an egg so his hand is cut off, and steals a rope so his hand is cut off.' (5) In copies (A), (B), (C): 'disbelief'. (6) Reported by al-Bukhari (107) and Muslim (3): 'Whoever lies about me, let him take his seat in Hellfire.'
Source pages p. 394

Commentary
This passage is a definition with indicators and rulings. The commentator explains that the poet's phrase 'minor major' is a substitute for 'two types' and clarifies that major sins are not limited to a specific number. He cites Ibn al-Salah's definition: a major sin is what is grave enough to be called major. Then he lists four indicators: (1) prescribed legal punishment (hadd), (2) explicit threat of punishment, (3) description of the doer as fasiq (sinner), (4) divine curse. The greatest major sin is shirk, then unjust killing. Other major sins vary in degree depending on context. The commentator then addresses a sub-issue: lying about the Prophet is among the greatest major sins, and al-Juwayni even considered it disbelief, but that view is deemed weak. Finally, he defines minor sins negatively: whatever is not major. He clarifies a subtle point: a minor sin may take the ruling of a major sin due to persistence (israr), but persistence requires repeating the sin with intention to return to it; if repeated without that intention, it is not persistence. This prevents misunderstanding that persistence automatically elevates a minor sin to a major sin in essence.

صغائر
أمارات الكبيرة
الحد

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT one of the indicators of a major sin mentioned in the passage?
A) Prescribed legal punishment
B) Explicit threat of punishment
C) Consensus of scholars
D) Describing the doer as fasiq

Key Takeaway
Major sins are identified by clear indicators, and their severity varies, with shirk and unjust killing being the greatest.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you sin, do you quickly reassure yourself it is small, or do you honestly check it against the four indicators—hadd, threat, being called fasiq, or curse? What does your answer reveal about your reverence for Allah's commands?
?
Which of the indicators frightens you most—that a sin may carry a prescribed punishment, that Allah has specifically threatened it, that it brands you as a fasiq, or that it brings a curse? How does that change your vigilance today?
?
If the severity of major sins varies by circumstance and consequences, where do you need to be more careful—not only in actions but in the situations you allow yourself to be in? Will you make a concrete change this week to avoid a circumstance that could lead to a major sin?

Minor Sins and the Effect of Persistence
The commentator defines minor sins, explains persistence, and discusses lying about the Prophet.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand what constitutes a minor sin, how persistence can give it the ruling of a major sin, and the specific condition for persistence.

Core Idea
Persistence can elevate a minor sin's ruling, but it requires intention to return.

After defining major sins, the commentator turns to minor sins and a critical nuance: can a minor sin become major through persistence? The answer clarifies that persistence (israr) has a precise technical meaning, and it does not change the essence of the sin.

Guided Path
1
Define minor sin
Read the passage that defines minor sin negatively: whatever is not a major sin. Also note that a minor sin can take the ruling of a major sin but does not change its nature.
Ibn Hajar is quoted: it 'may be given the ruling of a major sin, not that it actually becomes a major sin.'
2
Understand persistence (israr)
Learn the definition of persistence: repeating the sin with the intention to return to it at the time of action. Note the distinction between repeating with and without that intention.
If one repeats without intention to return, it is not considered persistence on the most correct view.
3
Consider the example of lying about the Prophet
The passage also addresses a related issue: lying about the Prophet is among the greatest major sins, and some scholars even considered it disbelief, but that view is weak.
This example illustrates how some sins are considered major by consensus.
