Among the things that help sincerity is the realization that other than God has nothing in its hand, and that everything is in the hand of God the Most High. The truthful one in his sincerity does not like people to see his good deeds, nor does he dislike people seeing his bad deeds, and he does not care about the loss of his status from the hearts of creation. One of them was seen in a dream after death saying: 'The Garden: its earth is faith, its trees are deeds, and its fruit is sincerity.' His saying: '(from showing off) with elongation; i.e., as a substitute for it, so 'min' is for substitution on the order of His saying: {Are you satisfied with the life of this world instead of the Hereafter} [al-Tawbah: 138]; i.e., as a substitute for it, and it is not for transition; because he did not express with 'salvation' or 'purity', but rather expressed with 'sincerity'. But showing off is that one performs a good deed for people to see him. As for making heard: it is that one performs the deed alone, then informs people about it for the sake of their veneration of him, or to attract good from them. And both showing off and making heard nullify reward while the deed is valid, contrary to what the Malikite masters have stated that it invalidates worship. And the saying of al-Hasan: 'Whoever gives another something out of shyness, he has a reward for it,' and the saying of Ibn Sirin: 'Whoever follows a funeral out of shyness of its family, he has a reward,' each of them is interpreted as intending to console the heart of the one he gave, and the family of the deceased for God, otherwise it is showing off. And in the sacred hadith: 'I am the most independent of partners from association; whoever does a deed in which he associates another with Me, I leave him and his partner' (1). And He said, the Most High: {So woe to those who pray, those who are heedless of their prayer, those who show off} [al-Ma'un: 4-6].
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition and proof text. It begins by citing a sacred hadith that emphasizes the necessity of action for hope in Paradise, then defines ikhlas (sincerity) as intending God alone in worship. The commentator states that ikhlas is a cause of salvation from the terrors of the Day of Judgment and an individual obligation on every morally responsible person in all acts of obedience. Proofs are then adduced: Quranic verse (al-Bayyinah: 5), a hadith from Anas, and a hadith from Thawban. The commentator then lists aids to sincerity, including realizing that nothing other than God possesses anything, and the true sincere person does not seek people's praise. A dream story illustrates that ikhlas is the fruit of deeds. Next, the commentator explains the phrase 'from showing off' (min al-riya'), noting that 'min' here means substitution, citing Quran 9:138. Riya' is defined as performing good deeds to be seen by people; tasmi' is performing a deed alone then telling people to gain veneration or benefit. Both nullify reward, contra the Malikite view that they invalidate the act itself. Exceptions are given for actions done out of shyness that aim to console others, otherwise they count as riya'. A sacred hadith and Quranic verse (al-Ma'un: 4-6) condemn showing off.

Key Takeaway
Ikhlas is the essential intention behind all worship, and it is the key to salvation and acceptance of deeds.

Riya' and Tasmi': The Vices That Nullify Reward
The commentator defines riya' and tasmi' and explains their ruling.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definitions of riya' (showing off) and tasmi' (making heard), their ruling on reward and validity, and when actions done out of shyness may be excused.

Core Idea
Riya' and tasmi' nullify the reward of good deeds without invalidating the deeds themselves, unless done with a pure intention to console.

The commentator now turns to the opposites of ikhlas. He carefully defines riya' and tasmi', their legal effect, and addresses apparent exceptions from early scholars. This clarifies when we must guard against seeking human approval.

Guided Path
1
Understand the phrase 'min ar-riya' and its substitution meaning
The commentator explains that 'min' in 'min ar-riya' means substitution, not transition, citing Quran 9:138. This sets the context.
The phrase means 'instead of showing off'.
2
Learn the definitions of riya' and tasmi'
Riya' is performing a good deed to be seen by people. Tasmi' is performing a deed alone then informing people to gain veneration or benefit.
Note the difference: riya' is visible during action; tasmi' involves later reporting.
3
Note the ruling: nullify reward but not deed
Both riya' and tasmi' nullify reward while the deed remains valid, contrary to the Maliki view that they invalidate the deed itself.
The deed is still valid but loses reward.
4
Analyze the exceptions and final warnings
Actions done out of shyness to console others are excused if the intention is for God, otherwise they are riya'. The passage ends with a sacred hadith and Quran verse condemning showing off.
Intention is key: consolation vs. seeking praise.

Source Text

وفي الحديث القدسي : مَا أَقلَّ حياءَ مَنْ يَطْمَعُ في جَنَّتي بغير عَمَلٍ، كيف أجودُ برحمتي على مَنْ بخل بِطَاعَتِي؟». قوله : (في الإِخْلاصِ أي في اتصافي به ؛ وهو قصد الله بالعبادة وحده، وهو سبب للخلاص من أهوال يوم القيامة، وهو واجب عيني على كل مُكلَّف في جميع الطاعات. قال تعالى: ﴿وَمَا أُمِرُوا إِلَّا لِيَعْبُدُوا اللهَ مُخْلِصِينَ لَهُ الدِّينَ) [البينة: ٥] ، وقال : إِنَّ اللهَ لا يقبلُ مِنَ العمل إلَّا ما كان خالصاً، وما ابتغي به وجهه (۱) ، وفي حديث أنس رضي الله تعالى عنه : قال رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم: «مَنْ فارق الدنيا على الإخلاص لله وحده لا شريك له، وإقام الصلاة، وإيتاء الزكاة.. فارقها والله عنه راض (۲) وعن ثوبان قال : سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول : طُوبَى للمخلصين، أولئك مصابيح الهدى تنجلي عنهم كلُّ فتنة ظلماء (۳)، وفي رواية: (قتماء)، وهي بمعنى ظلماء. وممَّا يعين على الإخلاص استحضار أن ما سوى الله لا شيء بيده، وأن كل شيء بيد الله تعالى، والصادق في إخلاصه لا يحبُّ اطلاع الناس على حُسْنِ عمله، ولا يكره أن يَطَّلِعَ الناس على سيئ عمله ولا يبالي بخروج قَدْره من قلوب الخلق، ورؤي بعضهم في المنام بعد الموت يقول : (الجنَّة أرضُها الإيمان، وشجرها الأعمال، وثمرُها الإخلاص). قوله : (مِنَ الرِّيَاءِ) بالمد؛ أي: بدله فـ (من) للبدل على حد قوله تعالى : أَرَضِيتُم بِالْحَيَوةِ الدُّنْيَا مِنَ الْآخِرَةُ [التوبة : ۱۳۸]؛ أي: بَدَلَها، وليست للتعدية؛ لأنه لم يُعبر بالخلاص أو الخلوص، بل عبر بالإخلاص. والرياء أن يعمل القُرية ليراه الناس . وأما التَّسْمِيعُ : فهو أن يعمل العمل وحده، ثم يُخبر به الناس لأجل تعظيمهم له، أو لجَلْبِ خير منهم، وكل من الرياء والتسميع مُحبط للثواب مع صحة العمل، خلافاً لما نصَّ عليه السادة المالكية من أنه مُبطل للعبادة. وقول الحسن : (مَنْ أعطى غيره شيئاً حياءً منه له فيه أجر)، وقول ابن سيرين: (مَنْ تَبِعَ جنازة حياءً من أهلها له أَجْرٌ)، كلٌّ منهما محمولٌ على ما إذا قصد جَبْرَ خاطرِ مَنْ أعطاه، وأهل الجنازةِ اللهِ، وإلا فهو رياء. وفي الحديث القدسي: أنا أغنى الشركاء عن الشركِ ؛ فمَنْ عمل عملاً أشرك فيه ،غيري، تركْتُهُ لشريكي (١) ، وقال تعالى: ﴿فَوَيْلٌ لِلْمُصَلِّينَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَاءُونَ ﴾ [الماعون : ٤-٦]
And in the sacred hadith: 'How little shame of the one who hopes for My Garden without action, how can I bestow My mercy on the one who is stingy with obedience to Me?' His saying: '(concerning sincerity) means concerning my being described with it; and it is intending God alone in worship, and it is a cause of salvation from the terrors of the Day of Resurrection, and it is an individual obligation on every morally responsible person in all acts of obedience. He said, the Most High: {And they were not commanded except to worship God, sincere to Him in religion} [al-Bayyinah: 5], and He said: 'Indeed God does not accept from action except that which is pure and intended for His Face.' In the hadith of Anas, may God be pleased with him: The Messenger of God, peace be upon him, said: 'Whoever leaves this world upon sincerity to God alone, with no partner, and establishing prayer, and giving zakat... leaves it while God is pleased with him.' From Thawban: I heard the Messenger of God, peace be upon him, say: 'Blessed are the sincere ones; they are lamps of guidance; every dark trial is dispelled from them.' In another narration: 'qatma'' which means 'darkness'. Among the things that help sincerity is the realization that other than God has nothing in its hand, and that everything is in the hand of God the Most High. The truthful one in his sincerity does not like people to see his good deeds, nor does he dislike people seeing his bad deeds, and he does not care about the loss of his status from the hearts of creation. One of them was seen in a dream after death saying: 'The Garden: its earth is faith, its trees are deeds, and its fruit is sincerity.' His saying: '(from showing off) with elongation; i.e., as a substitute for it, so 'min' is for substitution on the order of His saying: {Are you satisfied with the life of this world instead of the Hereafter} [al-Tawbah: 138]; i.e., as a substitute for it, and it is not for transition; because he did not express with 'salvation' or 'purity', but rather expressed with 'sincerity'. But showing off is that one performs a good deed for people to see him. As for making heard: it is that one performs the deed alone, then informs people about it for the sake of their veneration of him, or to attract good from them. And both showing off and making heard nullify reward while the deed is valid, contrary to what the Malikite masters have stated that it invalidates worship. And the saying of al-Hasan: 'Whoever gives another something out of shyness, he has a reward for it,' and the saying of Ibn Sirin: 'Whoever follows a funeral out of shyness of its family, he has a reward,' each of them is interpreted as intending to console the heart of the one he gave, and the family of the deceased for God, otherwise it is showing off. And in the sacred hadith: 'I am the most independent of partners from association; whoever does a deed in which he associates another with Me, I leave him and his partner' (1). And He said, the Most High: {So woe to those who pray, those who are heedless of their prayer, those who show off} [al-Ma'un: 4-6].
Source pages p. 422

Commentary
This passage is a combined definition and proof text. It begins by citing a sacred hadith that emphasizes the necessity of action for hope in Paradise, then defines ikhlas (sincerity) as intending God alone in worship. The commentator states that ikhlas is a cause of salvation from the terrors of the Day of Judgment and an individual obligation on every morally responsible person in all acts of obedience. Proofs are then adduced: Quranic verse (al-Bayyinah: 5), a hadith from Anas, and a hadith from Thawban. The commentator then lists aids to sincerity, including realizing that nothing other than God possesses anything, and the true sincere person does not seek people's praise. A dream story illustrates that ikhlas is the fruit of deeds. Next, the commentator explains the phrase 'from showing off' (min al-riya'), noting that 'min' here means substitution, citing Quran 9:138. Riya' is defined as performing good deeds to be seen by people; tasmi' is performing a deed alone then telling people to gain veneration or benefit. Both nullify reward, contra the Malikite view that they invalidate the act itself. Exceptions are given for actions done out of shyness that aim to console others, otherwise they count as riya'. A sacred hadith and Quranic verse (al-Ma'un: 4-6) condemn showing off.

Key Terms
الرياء
التسميع

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that any deed done with awareness of others is automatically invalid and without reward.
Correction: The passage clarifies that riya' and tasmi' nullify reward but the deed remains valid, and actions done out of shyness with pure intention to console may still be rewarded.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on both riya' and tasmi' concerning reward and the validity of the deed?
A) They nullify both reward and the deed itself.
B) They nullify reward but the deed remains valid.
C) They do not affect reward or validity.
D) They nullify the deed but reward remains.

Key Takeaway
Guard your intention: seeking human praise through riya' or tasmi' destroys the reward of your deeds, but a pure intention to console others does not.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent good deed you did. Was there any part of you that wanted others to know about it? How can you purify your intention for that deed starting today?
?
When you give charity or help someone out of shyness or social pressure, do you expect reward? The commentator says it depends on whether you intended to console the heart for God. Examine your last such act: was it for God or for human approval?
?
Have you ever told others about a good deed you did in private? That is tasmi'. What does that reveal about your heart's attachment to praise? Will you commit to not mentioning that deed again except for a genuine benefit?

Two Types of Riya': Conspicuous and Hidden
Classification of riya' into conspicuous and hidden with a supporting quote from al-Fudayl.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the difference between conspicuous and hidden riya', especially how inner joy at being seen is also a form of showing off.

Core Idea
Showing off isn't just about actions; hidden riya' lurks in the heart.

This lesson examines a key classification of riya' from classical Islamic theology. The commentator divides riya' into two types, and then quotes the early scholar al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad to deepen the spiritual diagnosis. Pay attention to the subtle distinction between doing deeds for people and feeling happy when they notice.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage
Read the Arabic passage carefully, then its translation. Let the author's words sink in before you analyze.
Notice the two types are introduced with 'قسمان'.
2
Identify the two types
Find the definitions of jali and khafi. How does each type manifest in behavior?
The first is purely external; the second is internal joy.
3
Reflect on al-Fudayl's quote
Read the quote and note the three statements: doing for people is shirk, leaving for people is riya', sincerity is being saved from both. Also note the exception about leaving an act to do it privately.
This quote clarifies that riya' is not only in action but also in intention and emotion.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرياء قسمان: جَلي، وخَفِيٌّ . فالأول : أن يفعل الطاعة بحضرة الناس لا غير فإن خلا بنفسه لا يفعلُ شيئاً . والثاني : أن يفعلها مطلقاً حضر الناس أو لا، لكن يفرح عند حضورهم. قال الفضيل بن عياض: العمل لأجل الناس شِرْكٌ، وترك العمل لأجل الناس هو الرياء، والإخلاصُ أَنْ يعافيك الله منهما ، فمَنْ عزم على عبادة فتركها خوف الناس فهو مُرَاء، إلا إن تركها ليفعلها في الخلوة، فهو مُستَحبُّ).
And showing off is of two types: conspicuous and hidden. The first: that one performs an act of obedience in the presence of people only; if he is alone he does nothing. The second: that one performs it absolutely, whether people are present or not, but he is happy when they are present. Al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad said: 'Doing deeds for the sake of people is shirk; leaving deeds for the sake of people is showing off; and sincerity is that God saves you from both. Whoever resolves to perform an act of worship and leaves it out of fear of people is a show-off, unless he leaves it to do it in private, then it is recommended.'
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is a classification. The commentator divides riya' (showing off) into two types: jali (conspicuous) and khafi (hidden). The conspicuous type is when a person only performs an act of worship when people are watching; otherwise they abandon it. The hidden type is when a person performs the act regardless of the presence or absence of people, but feels happiness and satisfaction when people notice them. Then, a quote from the early scholar al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad is given to deepen the understanding: doing deeds for the sake of people is shirk (associating partners with God), while abandoning deeds for the sake of people is itself riya' (because it shows concern for human opinion). True sincerity is when God protects the believer from both pitfalls. Al-Fudayl also clarifies an exception: if a person intends to perform an act of worship but leaves it out of fear of being seen by people, that is blameworthy riya'; but if they leave it in order to perform it later in private, away from people's eyes, then that is recommended (mustahabb) because it safeguards sincerity.

Key Terms
الرياء الجلي
الرياء الخفي
فضيل بن عياض

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Only the outward act of showing off matters; inner feelings don't count as riya'.
Correction: The passage shows that hidden riya' (khafi) includes feeling happy when people see you, even if you would have performed the act anyway.

Checkpoint
According to the classification, what characterizes the second (hidden) type of riya'?
A) The person only obeys when people are watching.
B) The person obeys regardless of people, but feels joy when seen.
C) The person never obeys even when people are present.
D) The person obeys only in private.

Key Takeaway
Riya' is not only about performing acts for others, but also about finding pleasure in their attention; true sincerity is being saved from both.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you perform a good deed, do you find yourself hoping someone notices? How does knowing that hidden riya' is the 'happiness at their presence' affect your next act of worship?
?
Al-Fudayl says that leaving a deed out of fear of people is riya' unless you do it to do it in private. Have you ever justified abandoning a good act because you were afraid of being seen? What will you do now?
?
Are you content with performing your acts of worship in secret, or do you crave recognition? What does your heart truly seek?

The Believer's Four Adversaries: Iblis, Dunya, Nafs, and Hawa
The commentator explains the poem line and quotes a verse listing four enemies.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four spiritual enemies that the believer must seek refuge from, as highlighted in the commentator's explanation.

Core Idea
The believer faces four relentless enemies: Iblis, dunya, nafs, and hawa.

In this passage, the commentator unpacks a line of the poem by explaining that the word 'then' here means 'and', and then he shares a beautiful poetic excerpt listing the four afflictions. This lesson focuses on identifying these four enemies and their threat to faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage once without analyzing. Then read the translation. Notice the commentator's grammatical point about 'then' meaning 'and'.
The poem quote is in the meter of kamil.
2
Identify the four enemies
From the poem quote, list the four afflictions the poet mentions. They are: Iblis, dunya, nafs, and hawa.
Iblis is Satan, dunya is the worldly life, nafs is the self, hawa is whimsical desire.
3
Reflect on the poet's plea
Notice how the poet despairs of any help except from Allah. This shows the severity of these enemies and the need for divine aid.
The poet says: 'I no longer hope for anyone besides You.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثُمَّ فِي الخَلاصِ ... إلخ) أي: وأرجو الله في الخلاص من هذه الأمور، فـ (ثم) هنا وفيما بعد بمعنى الواو، كما يدل عليه تعبير الناظم بالواو في قوله : (والهوى)، وما أحسن قول بعضهم في هذا المعنى: [من الكامل] إِنِّي بُلِيْتُ بِأَرْبَعِ تَرْمِيْتَنِي بالنَّبْلِ قَدْ نَصَبُوا عَلَيَّ شِرَاكَا إِبْلِيسُ وَالدُّنْيَا ونَفْسِي والهَوَى مِنْ أَيْنَ أَرْجُو بَيْنَهُنَّ فِكَاكَا؟! يَا رَبِّ سَاعِدْنِي بِعَفْوِكَ إِنَّنِي أَصْبَحْتُ لَا أَرْجُو لَهُنَّ سِوَاكَا ١٤١ - مِنَ الرَّحِيْمِ ثُمَّ نَفْسِي وَالهَوَى فَمَنْ يَمِلْ لِهَؤُلاءِ قَدْ غَوَى : قوله: (مِنَ الرَّحِيْمِ) أي من الوقوع في مكايدِ الشيطان. والرجيم بمعنى المرجوم؛ أي: المطرود عن رحمة الله تعالى؛ أو بمعنى الرَّاحِم للناس بوسوسته،
His saying: '(then in salvation... etc.)' i.e., and I hope in God for salvation from these matters, for 'then' here and afterwards has the meaning of 'and', as indicated by the poet's expression with 'and' in his saying: '(and desire).' How excellent is the saying of some in this meaning: [in the meter of kamil] 'I have been afflicted with four who have shot me with arrows; they have set a trap for me: Iblis, this world, my self, and desire. From where can I hope for deliverance from them? O Lord, help me with Your forgiveness, for I no longer hope for anyone besides You.' 141 - 'From the accursed, then my self and desire; whoever inclines to these has strayed.' His saying: '(from the Accursed)' i.e., from falling into the plots of Satan. And 'al-rajim' means the stoned one, i.e., the one expelled from the mercy of God the Most High; or it means the one who shows mercy to people through his whisperings.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is an interpretive commentary on a line of the poem. The commentator first explains the phrase 'then in salvation' as meaning hoping in God for deliverance from these four enemies. He notes that 'then' (thumma) here and in the poem functions like 'and' (waw), as shown by the poet pairing 'and desire' with 'and'. A supporting poetic quote is given, listing the four enemies: Iblis (Satan), dunya (this world), nafs (self), and hawa (whimsical desire). The poet laments being tested by all four and seeks refuge in God alone. Then the commentator glosses the word 'al-rajim' (the accursed) in the poem line 'min al-rajim'. He gives two interpretations: either it means 'the stoned one' i.e., expelled from God's mercy, or it could mean 'the one who shows mercy to people through his whisperings'—a surprising alternative meaning that suggests Satan's 'mercy' is actually his deceptive whisperings. The overall meaning is seeking refuge from falling into the traps of Satan, one's own ego, and desire, warning that whoever inclines to these has strayed from the path.

Key Terms
إبليس
الدُّنْيَا
النَّفْس
الهَوَى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what is the function of the word 'then' (ثم) in the poem line?
A) It indicates a sequence of events
B) It means 'and' (equivalent to الواو)
C) It is a particle of swearing
D) It means 'but'

Key Takeaway
The believer must seek refuge from the four great enemies: Iblis, dunya, nafs, and hawa.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the four enemies—Iblis, dunya, nafs, or hawa—do you sense is shooting most directly at your heart today? Be specific: what is the exact arrow, and what is your first step to seek God's deliverance from it?
?
The poet confessed he no longer hopes for anyone besides God. Where in your life have you been secretly relying on your own strength, worldly strategies, or even other people to overcome your inner battles? How can you transfer that hope to God alone starting now?
?
Imagine yourself trapped in a net woven by these four foes. You can’t escape by yourself. Are you willing to cry out to God for forgiveness and help this very moment, not just as a concept but as a desperate plea? What will that plea sound like in your own words?

Understanding 'Al-Rajim': The Accursed or the Deceptive Merciful?
The commentator glosses the word 'al-rajim' with two possible meanings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two possible meanings of 'al-rajim' (the accursed) in the poem line, as explained by the commentator.

Core Idea
Al-rajim can mean the accursed one or the one who shows false mercy through whisperings.

The poem line seeks refuge from 'al-rajim' (the accursed). The commentator offers two interpretations: the conventional meaning of the one expelled from mercy, and a surprising alternative that links it to mercy (rahm) – but a deceptive mercy through Satan's whisperings. This lesson explores both.

Guided Path
1
Read the poem line and commentary
Read the Arabic and translation of the poem line and the commentator's explanation. Note the two definitions given for 'al-rajim'.
The line also includes seeking refuge from self and desire.
2
Understand the first meaning
The first meaning is 'the stoned one' i.e., the one expelled from God's mercy. This is the common understanding of rajim.
The root r-j-m means to stone.
3
Understand the second meaning
The commentator also presents a second meaning: 'the one who shows mercy to people through his whisperings'. This is a striking interpretation linking to the root r-h-m (mercy), suggesting Satan's whisperings appear merciful but are traps.
This wordplay warns against deceptive whispers.
4
Reflect on the warning
Consider how this double meaning deepens the caution: not only is Satan accursed, but his whispers can seem like mercy, so believers must be vigilant.
The line ends: 'whoever inclines to these has strayed.'

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (ثُمَّ فِي الخَلاصِ ... إلخ) أي: وأرجو الله في الخلاص من هذه الأمور، فـ (ثم) هنا وفيما بعد بمعنى الواو، كما يدل عليه تعبير الناظم بالواو في قوله : (والهوى)، وما أحسن قول بعضهم في هذا المعنى: [من الكامل] إِنِّي بُلِيْتُ بِأَرْبَعِ تَرْمِيْتَنِي بالنَّبْلِ قَدْ نَصَبُوا عَلَيَّ شِرَاكَا إِبْلِيسُ وَالدُّنْيَا ونَفْسِي والهَوَى مِنْ أَيْنَ أَرْجُو بَيْنَهُنَّ فِكَاكَا؟! يَا رَبِّ سَاعِدْنِي بِعَفْوِكَ إِنَّنِي أَصْبَحْتُ لَا أَرْجُو لَهُنَّ سِوَاكَا ١٤١ - مِنَ الرَّحِيْمِ ثُمَّ نَفْسِي وَالهَوَى فَمَنْ يَمِلْ لِهَؤُلاءِ قَدْ غَوَى : قوله: (مِنَ الرَّحِيْمِ) أي من الوقوع في مكايدِ الشيطان. والرجيم بمعنى المرجوم؛ أي: المطرود عن رحمة الله تعالى؛ أو بمعنى الرَّاحِم للناس بوسوسته،
His saying: '(then in salvation... etc.)' i.e., and I hope in God for salvation from these matters, for 'then' here and afterwards has the meaning of 'and', as indicated by the poet's expression with 'and' in his saying: '(and desire).' How excellent is the saying of some in this meaning: [in the meter of kamil] 'I have been afflicted with four who have shot me with arrows; they have set a trap for me: Iblis, this world, my self, and desire. From where can I hope for deliverance from them? O Lord, help me with Your forgiveness, for I no longer hope for anyone besides You.' 141 - 'From the accursed, then my self and desire; whoever inclines to these has strayed.' His saying: '(from the Accursed)' i.e., from falling into the plots of Satan. And 'al-rajim' means the stoned one, i.e., the one expelled from the mercy of God the Most High; or it means the one who shows mercy to people through his whisperings.
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage is an interpretive commentary on a line of the poem. The commentator first explains the phrase 'then in salvation' as meaning hoping in God for deliverance from these four enemies. He notes that 'then' (thumma) here and in the poem functions like 'and' (waw), as shown by the poet pairing 'and desire' with 'and'. A supporting poetic quote is given, listing the four enemies: Iblis (Satan), dunya (this world), nafs (self), and hawa (whimsical desire). The poet laments being tested by all four and seeks refuge in God alone. Then the commentator glosses the word 'al-rajim' (the accursed) in the poem line 'min al-rajim'. He gives two interpretations: either it means 'the stoned one' i.e., expelled from God's mercy, or it could mean 'the one who shows mercy to people through his whisperings'—a surprising alternative meaning that suggests Satan's 'mercy' is actually his deceptive whisperings. The overall meaning is seeking refuge from falling into the traps of Satan, one's own ego, and desire, warning that whoever inclines to these has strayed from the path.

Key Terms
الرجيم
الشيطان
النفس
الهوى

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator, what are the two possible meanings of 'al-rajim'?
A) The one who stones people and the one who is stoned
B) The accursed/expelled from mercy and the one who shows mercy through whisperings
C) The one who whispers and the one who is silent
D) The one who is merciful and the one who is harsh

Key Takeaway
'Al-rajim' can be understood both as the accursed and as the one who shows deceptive mercy, reminding us of Satan's cunning.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
How have you, specifically, fallen for Satan's seemingly kind suggestions? Think of a time when you felt a harmful action was 'good' for you. What will you do differently now after learning that al-rajim can mean the one who shows mercy?
?
Are there any sins in your life that you initially justified as 'merciful' or 'helpful'? This lesson says that Satan can appear merciful. Will you re-examine your justifications this week?
?
When you seek refuge from al-rajim, are you aware of both his open attacks and his subtle, compassionate-looking deceptions? What practical step can you take today to guard against the latter?

Ruling of Riya' and Tasmee'
Author defines riya' and tasmee' and states their ruling with scholarly disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that riya' and tasmee' nullify reward without invalidating the act, and how apparent contradictory sayings are reconciled.

Core Idea
Riya' and tasmee' spoil reward but not the deed itself.

Sanusi begins by clarifying the ruling on showing off in worship. He distinguishes between nullifying reward and invalidating the act, and reconciles two hadith-like statements that might seem to tolerate suspicion. This passage establishes the gravity of intention-based corruption.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation to grasp the author's statements.
2
Identify the ruling on riya' and tasmee'
The author states that they nullify reward while the act is valid, contrary to the Maliki view that they invalidate the act.
This is a key doctrinal point.
3
Understand the reconciliation of the sayings
The author explains that giving or following a funeral out of shyness is rewarded if the intention is to comfort for Allah's sake.
Otherwise it is riya'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أو لجَلْبِ خير منهم، وكل من الرياء والتسميع مُحبط للثواب مع صحة العمل، خلافاً لما نصَّ عليه السادة المالكية من أنه مُبطل للعبادة. وقول الحسن : (مَنْ أعطى غيره شيئاً حياءً منه له فيه أجر)، وقول ابن سيرين: (مَنْ تَبِعَ جنازة حياءً من أهلها له أَجْرٌ)، كلٌّ منهما محمولٌ على ما إذا قصد جَبْرَ خاطرِ مَنْ أعطاه، وأهل الجنازةِ اللهِ، وإلا فهو رياء. وفي الحديث القدسي: أنا أغنى الشركاء عن الشركِ ؛ فمَنْ عمل عملاً أشرك فيه ،غيري، تركْتُهُ لشريكي (١) ، وقال تعالى: ﴿فَوَيْلٌ لِلْمُصَلِّينَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ عَن صَلَاتِهِمْ سَاهُونَ الَّذِينَ هُمْ يُرَاءُونَ ﴾ [الماعون : ٤-٦] . والرياء قسمان: جَلي، وخَفِيٌّ . فالأول : أن يفعل الطاعة بحضرة الناس لا غير فإن خلا بنفسه لا يفعلُ شيئاً . والثاني : : أن يفعلها مطلقاً حضر الناس أو لا، لكن يفرح عند حضورهم. قال الفضيل بن عياض: العمل لأجل الناس شِرْكٌ، وترك العمل لأجل الناس هو الرياء، والإخلاصُ أَنْ يعافيك الله منهما ، فمَنْ عزم على عبادة فتركها خوف الناس فهو مُرَاء، إلا إن تركها ليفعلها في الخلوة، فهو مُستَحبُّ).
Or for attracting good from them, and both riya' (showing off) and tasmee' (making heard) nullify reward while the act is sound, contrary to what the Maliki authorities stated that it invalidates worship. And the saying of al-Hasan: 'Whoever gives something to another out of shyness, he has a reward for it,' and the saying of Ibn Sireen: 'Whoever follows a funeral procession out of shyness of its family, he has a reward,' both are interpreted as when he intended to comfort the heart of the one he gave to, and the family of the deceased for Allah's sake, otherwise it is riya'. And in the hadith qudsi: 'I am the most independent of partners from partnership; whoever does an act in which he associates others with Me, I leave him and his partner.' And the Exalted said: {So woe to those who pray, those who are heedless of their prayer, those who show off} [al-Ma'un: 4-6]. And riya' is of two types: clear and hidden. The first: that he performs obedience in the presence of people only, such that if he is alone he does nothing. The second: that he performs it absolutely, whether people are present or not, but he rejoices when they are present. Al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad said: 'Acting for the sake of people is shirk, and abandoning action for the sake of people is riya', and sincerity is that Allah saves you from both. So whoever resolves on worship and then abandons it out of fear of people is a murā'ī (show-off), unless he abandons it to perform it in private, then it is recommended.'
Source pages p. 423

Commentary
This passage defines riya' (ostentation) and its two types, and clarifies its ruling. The author begins by stating that riya' and tasmee' (making one's deeds heard) nullify reward while the act itself remains valid, contravening the Maliki view that they invalidate the act. He then reconciles apparent contradictory sayings of al-Hasan and Ibn Sireen by explaining that if the motive is to comfort others sincerely for Allah, it is not riya'. A hadith qudsi and Quranic verse are cited to emphasize the severity of shirk in intentions. The passage then enumerates the two types of riya': clear (jali) and hidden (khafi). Clear riya' is performing worship only when people are watching; hidden riya' is performing it regardless but feeling joy when people see it. Finally, the statement of al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad distinguishes three states: acting for people is shirk, abandoning action for fear of people is riya', and sincerity is to be safe from both. He adds that leaving a deed out of fear of people is blameworthy unless one intends to do it secretly, which is commendable.

Key Terms
الرياء
التسميع
الإخلاص

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that shyness (haya') in giving or following a funeral always invalidates reward.
Correction: The author clarifies that it depends on intention: if done to comfort for Allah's sake, it is rewarded; otherwise, it is riya'.

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on riya' and tasmee' according to the author?
A) They invalidate the act of worship completely.
B) They nullify reward while the act remains valid.
C) They are minor sins with no effect on reward.
D) They have no effect on worship.

Key Takeaway
Riya' and tasmee' destroy the reward of a valid deed without rendering it invalid.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Think of a recent good deed you did. Before you did it, did the thought cross your mind that someone might see or hear about it? How will you guard against that in your next deed?
?
Have you ever refrained from a good deed out of shyness of people, only to later realize you missed an opportunity to please Allah? What will you do differently when the same situation arises again?
?
The lesson says that even a deed done out of shyness can have reward if the intention is to comfort others for Allah's sake. Examine your heart: when you do something for someone else, is your ultimate motive Allah's pleasure or just social harmony? How can you purify your intention starting today?

Types of Riya' and the Meaning of Sincerity
Author enumerates two types of riya' and cites al-Fudayl on sincerity.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between clear and hidden riya', and understand al-Fudayl's definition of sincerity.

Core Idea
Riya' is either clear (only for show) or hidden (enjoying praise); sincerity is being safe from both.

The author now presents the two categories of riya' backed by Quran and hadith, and concludes with a profound statement from al-Fudayl ibn 'Iyad that clarifies the three states of intention. This lesson helps you identify the subtle forms of ostentation.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage with Quran and hadith
Notice the hadith qudsi and Quranic verse that emphasize the danger of riya'.
2
Learn the two types of riya'
Clear riya' is only for show; hidden riya' is done consistently but with joy at praise.
3
Study al-Fudayl's statement
He distinguishes acting for people (shirk), abandoning for people (riya'), and sincerity (safety from both).
4
Apply the distinction
Consider how hidden riya' can infiltrate even consistent worship.
This is a subtle spiritual disease.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If you were to die tonight and your deeds were presented to you, would you be more concerned that people praised you for them, or that Allah accepted them? What practical change can you make today to ensure your intentions are pure?
